The `MINOR_TRIGGER_SUBSECTIONS` set is unchanged ‚Äî `Internal` is parsed but deliberately not included, so the patch-fallthrough path in `_decideBumpLevel` catches it. **Tests** (in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`'s existing `wrap-step version-bump ‚Äî pure helpers` block): one new `_parseUnreleased` case pinning that `Internal` surfaces in `subsections[]` alongside `Added`; one new `\`### Internal\` subsection (#231)` sub-describe with five cases covering Internal-only ‚Üí patch, Internal+Fixed ‚Üí patch (both orderings), Internal+Added ‚Üí minor (both orderings; user-visible wins), Internal+Changed ‚Üí minor, and BREAKING+Internal ‚Üí major (BREAKING precedence unchanged). Full suite 277/277 pass. **Operator-facing doc.** `CLAUDE.md` Global Rules ‚Üí Releases & Versioning section now carries the bump-level decision table verbatim, so future sessions pick the subsection by user-visible impact rather than file footprint. The next wrap that contains only `### Internal` (or `### Internal` + `### Fixed`) entries will demonstrably bump to patch instead of minor ‚Äî the closed loop the issue called for. Closes #231.
- **Feature Index dogfooded on TC-v3 (#207 Chunk 4)** ‚Äî closes out the four-chunk Feature Index build. `featureIndexEnabled` is now `true` on TC-v3's own project config, and `FEATURES.md` ships at the repo root with hand-authored pointer entries across UI / Web, Server / API, Methodologies / Engines, and CLI / Tooling. The Chunk-1 stub-seeding helper was verified end-to-end via a `PATCH /api/projects/TangleClaw-v3 {"featureIndexEnabled": true}` API call: the seed template lands when the toggle flips, and the hand-authored content replaces the placeholder sections. **Verification deferred.** Two parts of the plan's verification matrix can only run in *future* sessions and are intentionally not part of this PR: (1) starting a fresh Claude Code session on TC-v3 to confirm the Chunk-2 SessionStart injection actually pastes `## Feature Index` into the prime context, and (2) producing a PR that touches a brand-new file to confirm Chunk-3's `features-toc` wrap-step appends a TBD stub. Both will happen organically as the project continues; if either misbehaves, the regression is captured in a follow-up issue rather than blocking the dogfood landing. **Cross-references.** `MEMORY.md` gains a `reference_features_index.md` entry pointing at `FEATURES.md` as the canonical "where does feature X live?" lookup, so future sessions know to consult it before spawning Explore agents.

### Internal

- **Stale-plan hygiene rule + `.claude/plans/archive/` convention** ‚Äî adds two paragraphs to `CLAUDE.md` Build Plans & Chunks section codifying that plan files whose chunk has shipped get moved to `<project-root>/.claude/plans/archive/` (preserves the design rationale without polluting the active listing) AND that sessions starting work on a "next chunk" must verify the referenced issue's state via `gh issue view <N> --json state` before treating any plan as canonical. Both halves are needed: archiving is the convention, the issue-state check is the contract that protects across clones (the `.claude/` directory is gitignored, so archives are local-only). **Why now.** The 2026-05-23 session recommended #137 as the next chunk because `build-plan.md` was present at the repo root; the issue had been closed 18 days prior. The trap was structural ‚Äî "plan exists" was treated as "work is ready" ‚Äî and now the rule explicitly requires the issue-state check. **Local cleanup performed this session (not in this PR diff because `.claude/` and `build-plan*.md` are gitignored):** 19 stale plan files moved to `.claude/plans/archive/` ‚Äî 13 from `.claude/plans/` covering closed issues #103, #131, #139, #144, #145, #155, #158, #165, #207, plus three unnumbered plans self-marked closed (`prawduct-aicontent-prompts.md` via PR #200, `version-bump-handler.md` via PR #202, `replicated-coalescing-journal.md` whose `syncAllProjects()` shipped at `lib/projects.js:728`), and 6 stale `build-plan*.md` files at the repo root (including the #137-specific `build-plan.md` that triggered this whole janitor pass). Active plans directory is now empty; future planning sessions start from a clean slate.

## [3.18.0] - 2026-05-23

### Fixed

- **Case-insensitive project identity for orphan-port import banner + every identity-creating gate (#221, closes #188)** ‚Äî the landing page's `checkPortImports` (`public/landing.js:732-762`) compared lease project names against TC project names case-sensitively. A PortHub lease registered as `monad-1` (lowercase, from a programmatic registration) against a TC project named `Monad-1` (mixed-case, from a human-typed create) was falsely advertised as an "unregistered project" ‚Äî clicking Import would have created a duplicate. Dogfooded today; the user spotted the false banner and asked whether the bug was on the PortHub side or the TC side. **Fix.** New `_canonicalProjectName(name)` helper in `public/landing.js` normalizes to lowercase. `checkPortImports`'s `Set` membership check, ignored-list check, and conflict-detection cross-reference now all run through it on both sides. Lease bucketing preserves the original casing (the banner shows the lease's wire-form name, not a normalized form). **Symmetric gate audit (#188 closure scope, Critic-driven expansion).** Added `store.projects.getByNameCaseInsensitive(name)` (SQL `WHERE name = ? COLLATE NOCASE`). Per `feedback_symmetric_capability_gates`, every gate around the same conceptual flag (project-name identity) must check the same predicate, so every identity-CREATING site was migrated together: `createProject`'s duplicate-check, `updateProject`'s rename-collision check, `attachProject`'s already-registered check (`lib/projects.js:1119`), `listAllProjects`'s filesystem-scan unregistered-filter (`lib/projects.js:1619`), the startup project-sync warning (`server.js:642`), and the `POST /api/projects/import` warning (`server.js:969`). Without this audit, attach + import + startup-sync would have remained back doors that could introduce the very case-collisions the new validator rejects. **Error message format.** When `existing.name === requested.name` exactly, the legacy error format is preserved (no spurious "case-insensitive match" suffix). When they differ in case, the error cites the existing project's actual casing so the operator can find it ‚Äî e.g. `Project "foo-1" already exists (case-insensitive match for "Foo-1")`. Same pattern across create, rename, attach, sync, and import paths. **Self-rename allowance.** `updateProject`'s rename-collision check uses an `existing.id !== project.id` guard so case-only self-rename (`foo-1` ‚Üí `Foo-1` on the same project) stays legal at the validator layer. The filesystem-side directory rename is a separate concern that case-insensitive filesystems (macOS APFS-CI, Windows) silently absorb anyway. **Deliberately out of scope.** Auto-lowercasing existing project names at storage. Project names are filesystem-coupled (`<projectsDir>/<name>`) and display-coupled (modal headers, tmux session names, pill text); renaming `Monad-1 ‚Üí monad-1` would touch directories, tmux sessions, port leases, engine configs, `.claude/settings.json` hooks, and `.tangleclaw/project.json` files ‚Äî high blast radius for marginal payoff. Preserve original casing for display; canonicalize only at comparison sites. `store.projects.getByName` stays case-sensitive ‚Äî only identity-check call sites opt into the looser match via the new `getByNameCaseInsensitive`. URL-lookup routes (`GET /api/projects/:name`, status queries) also stay exact-case ‚Äî the URL is the identity, surprising substitution would be worse than the false-match. **Test coverage:** 3 new tests in `test/projects.test.js`'s `createProject` block (case-collision rejection both directions, error-message correctness, exact-case back-compat), 3 new tests in a new `updateProject` rename-collision sub-describe (case-only self-rename allowed at validator layer with case-insensitive-FS skip, cross-rename rejected with case-collision cite, exact-case rename-target legacy error format), 1 new attach-collision test (case-insensitive-FS skip pattern matching the rename test), 4 new `test/store-projects.test.js` tests for `getByNameCaseInsensitive` (cross-case match, exact-case match, null on absent, distinct-from-getByName regression pin). Full suite 2438 / 2438 pass with 1 skipped on this case-insensitive host (net +11 from this fix). Closes #221 + #188.

### Added

- **Stale-server detection + banner (#199)** ‚Äî new `lib/server-info.js` captures the git HEAD SHA at server boot and exposes a snapshot-comparison API. New `GET /api/server-info` route returns `{startupSha, currentDiskSha, isStale, commitsAhead, startedAt, uptimeSeconds}`. The landing page's init sequence fetches this in parallel with the other background loads, **polls every 60s** so the banner surfaces mid-session when the operator merges/pulls with a tab open, and renders a danger-coloured banner above the projects grid when `isStale === true` ‚Äî the text shows the short SHAs of both states, the commit count between them, the running-since duration (e.g. "Running for 3h 12m"), and instructs the operator to restart TC. Wired into the existing `.orphan-banner` class shape via a `.stale-server-banner` colour variant (danger red instead of amber) so the two banners read distinctly when both surface together. **Why this matters.** Node caches required modules at process start. When the operator pulls or merges code while TC is running, the on-disk source advances but the running process keeps using its in-memory copy until restart. The browser fetches fresh static assets each page load ‚Äî so the front-end shows the latest UI while the server still runs old behaviour. Silent-mismatch bugs follow: the canonical incident this issue was filed for was the Feature Index toggle clicked in a post-#208 UI, sent to a pre-#208 backend that doesn't recognize `featureIndexEnabled` and silently drops it on save (toggle appears to revert on the next read). Dogfooded today during the #207 series merge. **No-git fallback.** TC run outside a git checkout (tarball install, packaged distribution, CI) returns null for both SHAs; `isStale` reduces to `false` and the banner never fires. Detection is opt-in via the presence of a `.git` directory. Dirty-tree detection (uncommitted changes) is deliberately out of scope for v1 ‚Äî only merged-since-startup commits surface. Auto-restart and per-module hot-reload are deferred. **XSS-defensive UI.** `renderStaleServerBanner` clamps `commitsAhead` to a non-negative integer (`Math.max(0, Number(x) | 0)`) and `esc()`-passes every string before assignment to `innerHTML` ‚Äî matches the rest-of-file convention; a future server bug that leaks a non-numeric `commitsAhead` cannot inject markup. **Test-only reset export.** The module exposes `__unsafeResetForTest` (double-underscore + `unsafe` token) instead of the more conventional `_resetForTest`, so accidental production usage is grep-loud at review time. **Test coverage:** new `test/server-info.test.js` with 17 tests ‚Äî capture/idempotence/no-git-fallback for `captureStartup`; clean-state, stale-state, degraded-state semantics for `getServerInfo` (matched SHAs, null SHAs, mid-runtime git removal, non-numeric rev-list output, exec timeouts via ETIMEDOUT); detached-HEAD scenario (real SHA returned, stale detection still works); pure-helper coverage for `_countCommitsAhead` (null inputs, identical SHAs that short-circuit without shelling out). Full suite 2427 / 2427 pass (net +17 from this feature). Closes #199.

### Changed

- **Extracted `todayIsoLocal` to shared `lib/wrap-steps/_date.js`** ‚Äî post-#216 / post-#215 refactor that closes the duplication called out in both PRs' CHANGELOG entries. The local-zoned date formatter (`Date#getFullYear` / `getMonth` / `getDate`) previously lived inline in BOTH `lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js` (#216's fix for `## [version] - YYYY-MM-DD` headings) and `lib/wrap-steps/features-toc.js` (#215's `## TODO (auto-stubbed YYYY-MM-DD)` heading); duplicating it meant a future "fix it" patch could silently regress one call site. **Refactor shape:** new `lib/wrap-steps/_date.js` (underscore-prefixed filename signals "internal helper, not a step kind that `STEP_DISPATCH` dispatches to") exports a single `todayIsoLocal()` function. Both handlers now `require('./_date')` and bind their `_internal.todayIso` to the shared export. The pre-existing public names `versionBump._todayIsoLocal` and `featuresToc._todayIsoLocal` are preserved as **re-exports** of the shared function ‚Äî referentially identical to `_internal.todayIso` and to `dateUtil.todayIsoLocal`. This keeps every existing wiring-pin test passing untouched (no test file changes required for #216 or #215's coverage to stay valid) while collapsing the implementation to one source of truth. **Test coverage:** new `test/wrap-steps-date.test.js` with 7 tests ‚Äî shape pin (YYYY-MM-DD, 10 chars, separators), local-vs-UTC behavior pin (uses a `global.Date` subclass to pin a UTC moment whose local projection differs by date; skips gracefully on UTC-host CI where the distinction is unobservable), and 5 wiring/identity pins asserting that `dateUtil.todayIsoLocal`, `versionBump._internal.todayIso`, `versionBump._todayIsoLocal`, `featuresToc._internal.todayIso`, and `featuresToc._todayIsoLocal` ALL resolve to the same function reference. The all-five-references-identical pin is the core refactor invariant ‚Äî if anyone ever copies the helper back inline to "fix it in one place," this test fails on the very next suite run. Full suite 2410 / 2410 pass (net +7 from this refactor).

### Fixed

- **`_parseFields` now accepts natural-English heading variants (#201)** ‚Äî `lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js:_parseFields` previously required exact-string equality (after `.toLowerCase()`) between the `## Heading` text and the declared `captureField` name. This silently rejected the most natural Markdown a human or AI would write: `step.captureFields: ['nextSteps']` would match `## nextsteps` but NOT `## Next Steps` (space-separated), `## next-steps` (kebab), `## NEXT_STEPS` (screaming snake), or `## Next.Steps`. The handler then returned `{ok:false, status:'blocked', blockers:['Required captureField "nextSteps" missing or empty in AI response']}` and halted the wrap pipeline. Surfaced as Critic n1 on PR #200; the workaround there was to harden the `memory-update` prompt with explicit "use these exact spellings" instructions ‚Äî works, but every prompt edit is one slip away from re-introducing the block. **Fix:** new `_normalizeFieldKey(s)` helper lowercases and strips every non-`[a-z0-9]` character, applied symmetrically to both sides of the comparison. After normalization, `Next Steps`, `next-steps`, `next_steps`, `NEXT.STEPS`, and `nextSteps` all collapse to the same match key `nextsteps`. Output map keys remain the DECLARED `captureField` name (not the normalized form) so downstream consumers (`_completeV2Wrap`'s summary deriver, the prawduct lockstep / inverse-drift pins in `test/prawduct-aicontent-prompts.test.js`) do not have to also normalize. Normalization is a strict superset of the prior equality contract ‚Äî every input the old parser matched still matches; only the previously-rejected variants now also match. **Test coverage:** 11 new tests in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`'s `_parseFields` describe block ‚Äî natural-English variants (`## Next Steps`, kebab, screaming snake, dotted), canonical form still works (regression pin against over-correction), multiple mixed-style headings in one response, output-key contract (declared name, not normalized form). Plus a dedicated `_normalizeFieldKey` describe block covering non-alphanumeric stripping, case folding, digit preservation, and defensive inputs (empty, null, undefined, number coercion). The prawduct lockstep / inverse-drift tests are intentionally left untouched ‚Äî they enforce a STRICTER convention than the parser (single-word PascalCase headings) as a style guide for bundled methodology prompts; the parser is the safety net for community-authored methodologies and for AI responses that drift from canonical. Full suite 2360 / 2360 pass (net +11 from this fix). Closes #201.

### Added

- **YOLO mode in the launch picker for Gemini / Aider / Codex (#209)** ‚Äî extends the session-launch mode modal beyond Claude Code so every engine with a documented skip-permissions / unattended-execution flag exposes it as a picker option. **Gemini CLI** gains four modes mirroring Claude's structure: `Interactive` (default), `Auto Edit` (`--approval-mode auto_edit`), `Plan Only` (`--approval-mode plan`), and `YOLO` (`--yolo` ‚Äî auto-approve all actions). **Aider** gains `Interactive` + `YOLO` (`--yes-always`). **Codex** gains `Interactive` + `Full Auto` (`--full-auto` ‚Äî sandboxed automatic execution, not true YOLO; the label and description call out the distinction). The modal's render gate at `public/landing.js:470` (`Object.keys(launchModes).length > 1`) means each engine needs ‚â•2 modes to surface the picker, which all three satisfy. Backend wiring (`lib/sessions.js:_buildLaunchCommand`) is already engine-agnostic ‚Äî no JS changes required, only data. **OpenClaw** was deliberately scoped out: it's TC's in-house wrapper with no upstream YOLO flag to map, so its `launchModes` semantics need to be designed deliberately (follow-up tracked at [#210](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/210)). **Per-engine flag rationale:** all four CLIs (`claude --dangerously-skip-permissions`, `gemini --yolo`, `aider --yes-always`, `codex --full-auto`) verified against the locally installed binary's `--help` output before wiring. **Test coverage:** new `launchModes parity across engines (#209)` describe block in `test/engines.test.js` pinning (a) each engine's YOLO flag args exactly, (b) presence of `warning` text on every YOLO mode, (c) `defaultLaunchMode` key exists in `launchModes`, (d) every engine with `launchModes` has >1 mode so the modal renders, (e) sentinel pin asserting OpenClaw intentionally has no `launchModes` until [#210](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/210) is resolved. Full suite 2349 / 2349 pass (net +6 from this PR).

- **Feature Index ‚Äî `features-toc` wrap-step handler (#207, Chunk 3)** ‚Äî third sub-chunk of the multi-chunk Feature Index build. New `lib/wrap-steps/features-toc.js` handler appends stub entries to `<projectPath>/FEATURES.md` for files touched on the current branch that are not yet referenced anywhere in the index. Inserted into prawduct's `wrap_pipeline.steps[]` between `next-session-prime` and `memory-update` (`data/templates/prawduct/template.json`); registered in the dispatch table at `lib/wrap-pipeline.js`. **Never blocks** (matches the ADR 0002 step-kind contract + `version-bump` precedent): every degraded condition ‚Äî missing `FEATURES.md`, toggle off, base branch not resolvable, empty diff, all-touched-files-already-indexed, all-touched-files-filtered ‚Äî returns `{ok:true, status:'skipped'}` with `reason` / `detail` in `output` for the wrap drawer. **Gate (ADR 0001 symmetric, write-side scope):** only `projConfig.featureIndexEnabled === true` is checked here; the engine-capability + `silentPrime` predicates are injection-site concerns (Chunk 2) ‚Äî gating the wrap-side handler on engine capability would falsely deny index writes on engines that maintain the file without injecting it. **Single-transaction discipline:** the handler stages content under `staged['features-toc:append'] = {primingPath, newContent, changed:true, addedCount, addedFiles, todoDate}` ‚Äî `lib/wrap-steps/commit.js:_flushStagedWrites` already duck-types on `{primingPath, newContent, changed}` so the write happens during the commit step's flush, never inside this handler. **Commit body line:** new duck-type case in `_buildBodyLines` matches `{addedCount, addedFiles, todoDate}` ‚Äî emits `- Feature Index: N stub(s) appended (file1, file2, file3, +M more)` so wrap commits surface the index churn in `git log`. **Drift detection:** `_extractIndexedPaths` scans existing `FEATURES.md` for path-like tokens using a single regex against the same extension allowlist; the matcher is intentionally permissive (matches inside backticks, free text, comments) so an entry written `` `lib/foo.js:42` `` or `lib/foo.js (line 42)` both register the file. Bias is toward over-skipping ‚Äî a missed stub is recoverable, a false-positive duplicate would pollute the index. **Filter:** extension allowlist (`.js .jsx .ts .tsx .json .md .html .css .yaml .yml .sh`), prefix exclusion (`node_modules/`, `dist/`, `coverage/`, `build/`, `.git/`, `.tangleclaw/`), leading-dot-segment exclusion, basename exclusion (`CHANGELOG.md`, `README.md`, `FEATURES.md`). Set is intentionally moderate; Chunk 4 dogfood will surface whether tightening is needed. **Base branch resolution:** tries `main`, falls back to `master`, skips when neither resolves locally ‚Äî uses `git diff --name-only <base>...HEAD` three-dot syntax so only branch-introduced changes (not mainline drift since branch point) are scanned. **Idempotence on re-wrap:** after a successful flush, the appended paths are present in `FEATURES.md`; the next wrap's drift scan finds them and skips with `reason: 'no drift'`. No explicit "this run" marker is needed ‚Äî drift detection is naturally idempotent against the cumulative index state. **Migration note for existing prawduct installs.** `wrap_pipeline.steps[]` is reconciled by `_reconcileMergeBy:id` (ADR 0001), which is **additive-only AND end-appending** ‚Äî bundled entries with a new `idKey` are pushed to the end of the live array, not inserted at the bundled position. On existing installs with a cached `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/template.json` predating this PR, `features-toc` will land AFTER `commit` rather than between `next-session-prime` and `memory-update`. Because `commit` is the flusher, this means the stub append silently no-ops on cached installs until the cache is refreshed. Workaround mirrors the v3.17.0 ai-content prompts recipe: (a) stop the TC server, delete `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/template.json` (or the full `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/` directory), then restart ‚Äî `_copyBundledTemplates` re-copies from `data/templates/prawduct/template.json` only when the cached dir is missing; or (b) wait for a future chunk that introduces position-aware reconciliation. The dogfood pass in Chunk 4 will exercise this refresh path. **UTC-date parity (#205, applied in-chunk).** The `## TODO (auto-stubbed YYYY-MM-DD)` heading date uses a `_todayIsoLocal` formatter (`Date#getFullYear`/`getMonth`/`getDate`) instead of `Date#toISOString().slice(0,10)` so the date reflects the operator's local clock, not UTC ‚Äî same bug pattern as `version-bump` was fixed for in #216. Both call sites should ultimately share a util module; deliberately duplicated here to keep this chunk's surface contained, with the shared-util refactor tracked as a follow-up after #216 + #215 merge. **Test coverage:** new `test/wrap-step-features-toc.test.js` with 31 tests across pure helpers (`_isIndexableCandidate`, `_extractIndexedPaths`, `_appendTodoSection`, `_todayIsoLocal`), handler skip semantics (every degraded path), happy-path stage shape (6-field assertion), single-transaction discipline (no filesystem write inside the handler), idempotence (re-run after simulated flush yields no new appends), commit-body line emission (truncation, defensive zero-count, duck-type precedence), and UTC-date parity (shape, local-vs-UTC behavior with host-aware skip, wiring pin). Cached-install regression test in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` pins `_reconcileMergeBy:id` end-append behavior so future drift here is caught at unit-test level. Step-count + step-order pins updated in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` (3 assertions: STEP_DISPATCH expected list, step-id order, kind order; runWrapPipeline step count 8‚Üí9), `test/sessions.test.js` (V2 lifecycle step-count 8‚Üí9; legacy NL prompt `Wrap steps:` string), and `test/skills.test.js` (`getWrapSkill('prawduct').steps[]`). **What's deferred to Chunk 4 (the final chunk):** TC-v3 itself gets a populated `FEATURES.md` hand-authored from the Explore findings; a small test commit touching a new file ‚Üí wrap ‚Üí confirms `features-toc` stubs it; CHANGELOG + MEMORY.md gain pointers to `FEATURES.md` as a discoverable surface. Full suite 2381 / 2381 pass (net +23 from this chunk ‚Äî Chunk 3 base 28 tests + cached-install regression pin + 3 UTC-parity tests). GitHub issue [#207](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/207); plan at `.claude/plans/feature-index.md`.

- **Feature Index ‚Äî SessionStart injection (#207, Chunk 2)** ‚Äî second sub-chunk of the multi-chunk Feature Index build. When `featureIndexEnabled === true` AND `silentPrime === true` AND the engine profile has `capabilities.supportsSilentPrime === true`, `generatePrimePrompt()` in `lib/sessions.js` reads the project's `FEATURES.md` from the project root and pushes its trimmed contents into the prime prompt under a `## Feature Index` heading. Injection slots between the Last Session Summary and Eval Audit Mode blocks so it's adjacent to other session-dynamic state (Active Learnings, Last Session). **Symmetric gate (ADR 0001):** all three predicates must be true ‚Äî asymmetric gates leak orphan state (the lesson pinned by `feedback_symmetric_capability_gates` after PR #125's Critic-caught regression). **Defensive shape-checks:** `engineProfile` and `engineProfile.capabilities` are explicitly null-checked before `supportsSilentPrime` is read, so a synthesized / minimal profile (the integration-test path and any future engine that omits the capabilities object) skips cleanly. **Graceful skip on read failure:** missing / unreadable `FEATURES.md` is caught silently ‚Äî absence must never block session start (the file is opt-in scaffolding seeded by Chunk 1 only when the user toggles on). **Whitespace short-circuit:** a file containing only whitespace produces no section in the prime, so a freshly-seeded but un-edited template doesn't surface an empty heading. **Truncation preserved:** the existing `template.prime.maxTokens` truncation at `lib/sessions.js:408-413` still runs after the section is appended, so an oversize `FEATURES.md` cannot blow the prompt budget ‚Äî surfaced as a `[Prime prompt truncated]` marker matching every other prime-state addition. **Test coverage:** 8 new tests in `test/sessions.test.js`'s `generatePrimePrompt` describe block ‚Äî happy path (all three gates true ‚Üí section present with body); each gate's negative case (toggle off / silentPrime off / engine capability false / missing capabilities object entirely); missing FEATURES.md graceful skip; whitespace-only file produces no section; truncation budget honored against an oversized FEATURES.md. **What's deferred to remaining chunks:** the `features-toc` wrap-step handler that auto-appends stubs for PR-touched files not in `FEATURES.md` (Chunk 3); dogfooding TC-v3 itself with a populated index (Chunk 4). Full suite 2357 / 2357 pass (net +8 from this chunk). GitHub issue [#207](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/207); plan at `.claude/plans/feature-index.md`.

- **Feature Index ‚Äî per-project toggle + template seeding (#207, Chunk 1)** ‚Äî first sub-chunk of the multi-chunk Feature Index build. Introduces an opt-in `featureIndexEnabled` field in `DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG` (default `false`) plus a settings-modal toggle that, when flipped on, seeds a `FEATURES.md` template at the project root if the file does not already exist. The seed helper `_seedFeatureIndexFile` is idempotent ‚Äî never overwrites pre-existing content, never deletes on toggle-off (the file is a user-owned, git-tracked artifact). **What this chunk does:** persists the flag, surfaces it through `enrichProject`, renders the toggle in `public/ui.js`'s settings modal (engine-agnostic, always shown ‚Äî the file + future wrap-step parity are engine-independent), and seeds the template stub. **What's deferred to later chunks:** SessionStart prime-prompt injection of `FEATURES.md` contents (Chunk 2, engine-capability-gated at the injection site per ADR 0001 symmetric-gate principle); the `features-toc` wrap-step handler that auto-appends stubs for PR-touched files not in `FEATURES.md` (Chunk 3); dogfooding TC-v3 itself with a populated index (Chunk 4). **Validation placement** mirrors the `silentPrime` precedent (`lib/projects.js:1169`): boolean type-check runs pre-mutation so a rejection drops cleanly without partial-state corruption. **API surface:** `PATCH /api/projects/:name` accepts `featureIndexEnabled: boolean`; `GET /api/projects/:name` and `GET /api/projects` return `featureIndexEnabled` on each project. **Test coverage:** new `test/feature-index.test.js` with 15 tests across DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG default, helper idempotence (create / preserve existing / non-throwing on error), updateProject validation (5 non-boolean shapes rejected), seeding behavior on toggle-on / toggle-off / idempotent true‚Üítrue save, enrichProject surface, and PATCH-body independence (combo updates persist both fields; rejection isolation). Full suite 2343 / 2343 pass (net +15 from this chunk). GitHub issue [#207](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/207); plan at `.claude/plans/feature-index.md`.

### Fixed

- **`version-bump` handler now stamps the release heading with the operator's LOCAL date instead of UTC (#205)** ‚Äî `lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js:_internal.todayIso` previously called `new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10)`, which always returns UTC. When the wrap ran after the operator's local-zone day had ended but before midnight UTC (e.g. 5pm PT on 2026-05-22 = 00:25 UTC on 2026-05-23), the new `## [version] - YYYY-MM-DD` heading came out one day ahead of every other entry in the file. Surfaced the evening this PR landed when cutting v3.17.0 itself: handler stamped `## [3.17.0] - 2026-05-23` against a local 2026-05-22, requiring a manual patch before the release shipped ‚Äî Critic n4 of that release flagged the inconsistency. **Fix:** extracted a named `_todayIsoLocal` formatter using `Date#getFullYear` / `getMonth` / `getDate`, no timezone-database dependency, exported it so tests can pin the wiring. `_internal.todayIso` now points to `_todayIsoLocal`. **Test coverage:** three new regression tests in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`'s `wrap-step version-bump ‚Äî pure helpers` describe block ‚Äî (1) YYYY-MM-DD shape pin (10 chars, separators at indices 4 and 7, regex match); (2) local-vs-UTC behavior pin using a `global.Date` subclass that pins the wall clock to a known local moment and asserts the formatter returns the local date regardless of host TZ; (3) wiring pin asserting `_internal.todayIso === _todayIsoLocal` so a future refactor cannot silently regress to a UTC-emitting default. All existing handler tests already stub `_internal.todayIso` to a deterministic literal, so the fix is purely internal to the default factory ‚Äî no test plumbing churn elsewhere. **Note on `features-toc` (#207 Chunk 3, PR #215):** the new handler ships the same `todayIso: () => new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10)` pattern; it inherits the same bug until either #215 is rebased against this fix post-merge or a follow-up applies the same change to `lib/wrap-steps/features-toc.js`. Both call sites should ultimately share a single utility; deferred so this fix stays surgical and #215 can land on its own merits. Full suite 2347 / 2347 pass (net +3 from this fix).

## [3.17.0] - 2026-05-22

### Changed

- **Prawduct `ai-content` step prompts populated (open-queue #2 post-#139)** ‚Äî `data/templates/prawduct/template.json`'s three `ai-content` steps (`changelog-update`, `learnings-capture`, `memory-update`) gain real prompts. Prior to this change the steps shipped with `prompt: ""` and surfaced as `skipped` rows in every V2 wrap drawer post-Chunk-11c ‚Äî functional, but produced no user-visible session output. New prompts instruct the AI to: (`changelog-update`) read `git log <lastWrapSha>..HEAD` + working tree, then edit CHANGELOG.md `[Unreleased]` per Keep-a-Changelog style with a `## Result` tail; (`learnings-capture`) reflect on non-obvious takeaways and append to `.tangleclaw/memories/learnings.md`, or write `no novel learnings` rather than fabricating signal; (`memory-update`) demote prior `Last Session` block to `wrap-log.md`, write a new block to `MEMORY.md`, then emit `## Summary` + `## NextSteps` + `## Learnings` heading blocks that `_parseFields` in `lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js` parses against the step's `captureFields` and `_completeV2Wrap`'s summary deriver consumes for the wrap commit subject. **Migration note for existing prawduct projects:** the methodology template is cached at `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/template.json` (via `_copyBundledTemplates` at `lib/store.js` on TC server boot). `_reconcileMergeBy:id` (ADR 0001) is additive-only on existing step ids, so cached templates with `prompt: ""` keep their empty prompts on every subsequent boot. To pick up the populated prompts on an existing install: (a) stop the TC server, delete `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/template.json` (or the full `~/.tangleclaw/templates/prawduct/` directory), then restart ‚Äî `_copyBundledTemplates` re-copies from `data/templates/prawduct/template.json` only when the cached dir is missing; or (b) wait for a future chunk that introduces per-field reconciliation of `step.prompt`. The per-project `.tangleclaw/project.json` is the per-project *config*, NOT the methodology template cache ‚Äî deleting it does not refresh the bundled prompts. New test file `test/prawduct-aicontent-prompts.test.js` pins the prompt invariants (>=200 chars each, `## Summary` / `## NextSteps` / `## Learnings` instructions in memory-update, `captureFields` lockstep) and the minimal-methodology empty-prompt anchor (Chunk 11c contract still exercised by bundled methodology). ADR 0002 Status line carries the extension marker.

- **`DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.wrapV2: false ‚Üí true` (#139, Chunk 11c)** ‚Äî **closes the #139 series.** The Session Wrap button now drives the server-side `wrap_pipeline` runner by default; the legacy NL-prompt-via-tmux flow is reachable only via explicit per-project opt-out (`wrapV2: false` in `<project>/.tangleclaw/project.json`). Combined with Chunk 11a (V2 lifecycle transition) and Chunk 11b (`invoke-critic` action producer) that landed earlier in the day, V2 is now a quality default: sessions wrap-to-completion correctly, the `critic-check` step has a real producer for `.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json`, and prawduct's bundled pipeline runs the full step set (`open-pr-check` + `critic-check` are wired in here for the first time).
  - **`lib/store.js`** ‚Äî `DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.wrapV2: false ‚Üí true`. The block comment that previously documented the opt-in is replaced with the opt-out semantics + migration recipe. `projectConfigApi.load`'s deep-merge is unchanged, so existing projects with an explicit `wrapV2: false` in their on-disk config preserve the legacy path with no further intervention; only projects without a `project.json` (brand-new) or whose `project.json` predates the field (legacy installs that never touched the field) pick up the new V2 default.
  - **`data/templates/prawduct/template.json`** ‚Äî `wrap_pipeline.steps[]` gains two leading steps: `{id: "open-pr-check", kind: "pr-check", blocker: false}` and `{id: "critic-check", kind: "critic-check", blocker: false}`. Chunks 7 + 8 deliberately did not wire these into prawduct's pipeline so the legacy NL prompt's byte-equal pin could keep passing through Chunks 4‚Äì10; the wiring lands now alongside the flag flip so V2 prawduct projects get the full surface (PR-state surfacing + Critic warning) immediately. Order: PR-check first (surfaces session-scoped PRs before any heavy steps so the user can act on the drawer's per-PR resolution dropdowns); critic-check second (its warning state needs to be staged before the `commit` step's body-builder runs). Both are `blocker: false`.
  - **Legacy NL prompt's `Wrap steps:` list changes** as a side effect of the prawduct-template change (`lib/skills.js:wrapShapeFromTemplate` flattens every `step.id` into the legacy `steps` array). The post-Chunk-11c legacy prompt for prawduct reads `Wrap steps: open-pr-check, critic-check, version-bump, changelog-update, learnings-capture, next-session-prime, memory-update, commit`. This is intentional ‚Äî both the V2 pipeline and the legacy NL prompt (for opt-out projects) reflect the same authoritative step list from the methodology template. The byte-equal regression pin in `test/sessions.test.js` and `test/skills.test.js` is updated to reflect the new list.
  - **Two `wrapV2`-related test semantics inverted.** (1) `wrapV2 absent from projConfig (older on-disk state)` was previously pinned to "absent ‚Üí legacy fallback" because pre-flip the default was `false`; post-flip absent ‚Üí V2-routing, so the test is reframed and rewritten to assert the new contract. (2) `wrapV2:false (default)` is renamed to `wrapV2:false (explicit opt-out) uses the legacy NL-prompt path with the post-Chunk-11c step list` and pinned against the new step list (the legacy path's prompt structure ‚Äî prefix, separator, capture-fields suffix ‚Äî is byte-equal to pre-Chunk-11c; only the comma-joined steps inside `Wrap steps:` differ, and that's a function of the methodology template, not the legacy path's behavior).
  - **Test scaffolding fallout.** The `triggerWrap (methodology-driven)` describe block in `test/sessions.test.js` gains a `wrapV2: false` baseline in its `beforeEach` so the (numerous) legacy-asserting tests inside it stay focused on legacy behavior without each one having to repeat the projConfig write. The V2-routing tests inside the same block already write `wrapV2: true` per-test, so the baseline doesn't collide. **Two new tests** pin the Chunk 11c default-flip contract: `DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.wrapV2 is true` (direct invariant pin against `lib/store.js`); `a fresh project (no on-disk config) routes to the V2 path` (deletes the on-disk `project.json` to assert the fresh-project default; stubs `runWrapPipeline` to avoid exercising real-handler state on the tmp project). Step-count assertions in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` and `test/sessions.test.js` for prawduct change from 6 ‚Üí 8 to match the new wired-in surface.
  - **Migration docs.** README's `Configuration` section now carries a `Session Wrap (V2 default, opt-out path)` block with the per-project opt-out recipe. ADR 0002's Status line carries a `Default flipped to V2 on 2026-05-19 via #139 Chunk 11c` marker; the Chunk 11c entry in the migration-path enumeration is expanded with the post-flip contract.
  - **What stays.** Legacy `triggerWrap` NL-prompt branch (one-release-cycle deprecation window). Back-compat shim in `lib/skills.js:wrapShapeFromTemplate` (same window). Inert `wrap.steps` / `wrap.captureFields` reconciler entries in `ARRAY_RECONCILERS` (same window).
  - **What's gone.** The original Chunk 12 "cross-engine prompt-template parity" was marked optional in the build plan; it's now tracked as a separate follow-up to be filed when the codex / gemini-side roadmap firms up. The #139 series itself can close after this PR merges ‚Äî the seven gaps it set out to fix (janitor pass, Critic compliance, test gating, durable memory updates, priming-pointer roll, structured-output derivation, multi-step-commit leak) are all server-side-deterministic now.
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (2 MAJOR + 6 MINORs + 3 NITs addressed; YELLOW ‚Üí GREEN ‚Äî per user directive that every finding land before merge).** (M1) README oversold V2 by listing `lint`, `tests`, and `version-bump` as deterministic V2 steps ‚Äî but `version-bump` is still the Chunk-3 no-op stub and `lint` / `test` aren't wired into prawduct's pipeline. Reworded the README's `Session Wrap (V2 default, opt-out path)` block to describe **only** what prawduct's pipeline actually runs today: `pr-check` + `critic-check` + `version-bump` (placeholder) + three `ai-content` placeholders (`changelog-update`, `learnings-capture`, `memory-update` with empty prompts that surface as `skipped`) + `priming-roll` + `commit`. Methodology authors can opt in `lint` / `test` via their own templates. (M2) Three prawduct `ai-content` steps ship with `"prompt": ""` and the pre-#139-Chunk-11c handler at `lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js:154` returned `{ok: false, status: 'blocked'}` on empty prompts. Pre-flip this was harmless (V2 was opt-in); post-flip every prawduct V2 wrap would surface three `blocked` rows in the drawer. Changed the handler's contract: **empty or whitespace-only `step.prompt` ‚Üí `{ok: true, status: 'skipped', output: null, blockers: []}`**. Methodology-author intent of an empty prompt is "placeholder, no work to do today" ‚Äî `skipped` matches the intent. Three new tests in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` pin the new behavior (empty string; whitespace-only; missing-entirely). The pre-flip `'blocks when step.prompt is empty'` test is rewritten as `'skips cleanly when step.prompt is empty (#139 Chunk 11c ‚Äî placeholder semantics)'`. (N1) Stale comments in `lib/sessions.js:716-721` (`_triggerWrapV2` doc) and `:910-916` (entry-point `triggerWrap` gate) referenced the pre-flip default in future tense ‚Äî both rewritten to describe the post-flip state. The gate-comment now explicitly notes the strict-equality `=== true` defensive contract. (N2) CHANGELOG cited `lib/store.js:420` for the `wrapV2` field; actual line is `426` post-comment-expansion. Dropped the line number ‚Äî field name is unique. (N3) README referenced `v3.17` but `version.json` is `3.16.2`. Replaced with version-agnostic "After #139 Chunk 11c lands" / "this release". (N4) Local plan at `.claude/plans/issue-139-methodology-aware-wrap.md` Status line still read "Discovery complete. Ready to start Chunk 2" ‚Äî replaced with a series-closing summary marker dated 2026-05-19. (N5) Added three round-trip persistence tests to `test/store.test.js`'s `projectConfig` describe block: explicit `wrapV2: false` survives deep-merge against the default-true config; explicit `wrapV2: true` round-trips; absent `wrapV2` defaults to `true` post-flip. These pin the migration guarantee at the unit level (the existing integration tests cover the through-`triggerWrap` path). (N6) Added a minimal-methodology variant of the opt-out test that asserts the legacy NL prompt for minimal contains `Wrap steps: learnings-capture, memory-update, commit`. (T1) Removed the redundant `projectConfig.save` from the fresh-project test's `finally` block ‚Äî the outer `beforeEach` re-establishes the baseline before each test, so the inline restore was double-bookkeeping. Comment rewritten. (T3) Hoisted the duplicated `runWrapPipeline` stub literal into a frozen module-scope `EMPTY_V2_RESULT` constant shared by the absent-flag and fresh-project tests. (T4) Post-merge: delete the self-deleting auto-memory `project_issue_139_methodology_wrap.md` and prune the index line in `MEMORY.md` (per CLAUDE.md Memory Hygiene rule ‚Äî the series-closed condition triggers cleanup). Tracked separately from this PR since auto-memory lives outside the repo.
  - Full suite: 2274 / 2274 pass (was 2266 at end of 11b; net +8 from Chunk 11c: +2 flip-pin tests, +2 new ai-content placeholder-semantics tests (the original `blocks-when-empty` test was rewritten as `skips-when-empty` ‚Äî net replacement, not addition), +3 round-trip persistence tests in `test/store.test.js`, +1 minimal-methodology opt-out variant).

### Fixed

- **`tmux.createSession` env vars now reach the launch command's process (#190)** ‚Äî `lib/tmux.js:createSession` was calling `tmux set-environment` AFTER `tmux new-session -d -s <name> <command>`, so the spawned command (e.g. an engine launcher reading from `~/.tangleclaw/engines/<id>.json` `launch.env`) inherited the original parent process env without the supplemented values. `set-environment` only affects subsequently-spawned child processes ‚Äî the launch command itself was already running. Net effect: every engine override using `launch.env` to inject runtime variables (API keys, base URLs, env-keyed model selectors) silently did nothing. Surfaced via the Aider engine override ‚Üí LiteLLM gateway integration: `OPENAI_API_KEY` never reached the spawned `aider` process, producing `litellm.AuthenticationError: OpenAIException - The api_key client option must be set either by passing api_key to the client or by setting the OPENAI_API_KEY environment variable`. **Fix**: use `tmux new-session -e KEY=VALUE` flags (tmux ‚â• 2.8) so env is applied at session-creation time BEFORE the initial command spawns. Post-create `set-environment` loop removed (redundant once `-e` is in place, and removing it eliminates a second-source-of-truth for the same values). Each `-e VALUE` is wrapped via `_escapeArg` so values with shell metacharacters (spaces, quotes, `$`, `;`) reach the child byte-intact. **Test coverage**: `test/tmux.test.js` had zero coverage for `options.env`; added two regression pins ‚Äî (1) launch command actually inherits the env vars (dump to file, read back, assert) and (2) tricky values with shell metacharacters survive the escape unchanged. **Blast radius**: any engine override using `launch.env` was silently broken; today only the Aider override exercised the path, but future env-keyed engine integrations (LiteLLM-routed codex, env-keyed gemini variants, etc.) would have hit the same trap. Full suite: 2226 / 2226 pass (was 2224 at end of Chunk 10; net +2). Independent corroboration: Monad-1 session identified the same tmux server / session env-cache hypothesis from their side without seeing the TC patch ‚Äî diagnoses converged on `-e per-session` as the proper fix.

### Added

- **Real `version-bump` wrap-step handler (open-queue #3 post-#139)** ‚Äî `lib/wrap-steps/version-bump.js` replaces the #139 Chunk-3 no-op stub with a full handler that reads `CHANGELOG.md` `[Unreleased]` + `version.json`, decides a bump level, promotes `[Unreleased]` to a dated release, and bumps the semver. Closes the last remaining no-op stub in `lib/wrap-steps/`. **Bump-level precedence:** `options.bumpLevel` override (`patch`|`minor`|`major`) wins outright; otherwise `BREAKING` marker anywhere in the [Unreleased] body forces `major`; otherwise `### Added` / `### Changed` / `### Removed` / `### Deprecated` present ‚Üí `minor`; otherwise (only `### Fixed` / `### Security`) ‚Üí `patch`. **Single-transaction discipline + composite-staged-keys.** Handler never writes the filesystem; it stages TWO entries under composite keys (`'version-bump:version-json'` and `'version-bump:changelog'`) so the Chunk-9 `commit` step's `_flushStagedWrites` (already duck-typed on `{primingPath, newContent, changed}`) flushes both with no dispatch-table edit. Establishes the multi-file write-staging convention for any future step that needs to stage more than one file. **Commit body line.** `lib/wrap-steps/commit.js:_buildBodyLines` gains a new duck-type matching `{oldVersion, newVersion, bumpLevel}` ‚Äî emits `- Bumped <old> ‚Üí <new> (<level>)` once per pipeline run (deduped via a local flag since both staged entries carry the metadata). **Never blocks** (matches the ADR 0002 step-kind contract): every degraded condition ‚Äî missing `version.json`, malformed `version.json`, non-semver `version` field, missing `CHANGELOG.md`, missing `[Unreleased]` section, `[Unreleased]` with no entries ‚Äî returns `{ok:true, status:'skipped'}` with a `reason` / `detail` in `output` for the wrap drawer to render inline. **Idempotent on re-wrap:** after a successful bump the `[Unreleased]` body is empty (just the heading); the next wrap observes no entries and skips. **Banner emoji NOT auto-injected** ‚Äî `> üõü` (bug-fix) / `> üöÄ` (feature) leading banners stay a curated operator decision per the project's CHANGELOG convention; the handler promotes `[Unreleased]` body byte-for-byte under the new dated heading and the operator adds the banner manually. **Output for the drawer:** `output.from`, `output.to`, `output.bumpLevel`, `output.detail` (the pre-formatted "from ‚Üí to (level)" string) ‚Äî matches the existing `wrap-drawer.js:deriveDetail`'s `version-bump` case (`if (output.from && output.to)`), no drawer change required. **Test coverage:** 39 net new tests across `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` (pure-helper decision tables for `_parseSemver` / `_bumpSemver` / `_parseUnreleased` / `_decideBumpLevel` / `_promoteUnreleased`; handler tests for every skip path + happy path + idempotency + override + BREAKING-marker + never-blocks contract sweep; commit-body-line duck-type + dedupe pin). The Chunk-3 `wrap-pipeline step stubs` describe block now marks its `kinds` array empty with a sentinel pin so a future stub-introducing chunk has to update the list. **ADR 0002** Status line extended with the open-queue-#3 marker.

- **V2 wrap session-lifecycle transition (#139, Chunk 11a)** ‚Äî first sub-chunk of the original Chunk 11 (split into 11a / 11b / 11c during this session's scope review). Resolves [#186](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/186): a successful V2 wrap that produced a commit now transitions the session record (`status: 'wrapped'`), kills tmux, releases doc locks, and clears idle + wrap-pane caches ‚Äî symmetric with the legacy `completeWrap` teardown minus `_autoCommitIfDirty` (V2's `commit` step already flushed). Pre-#186, V2 wraps left the session `active` indefinitely; the drawer's "Done" only closed the drawer. Halted / thrown / clean-session (`ok` + `null` SHA) runs still leave the session active per spec so the user can retry or continue. **Scope:** this is pre-flip plumbing ‚Äî the flag flip itself moves to Chunk 11c so V2 is a quality experience before becoming the default; `invoke-critic` action producer (Chunk 11b) and prawduct template wiring (Chunk 11c) remain follow-ups.
  - **`lib/sessions.js`** ‚Äî new helpers `_completeV2Wrap(active, pipelineResult)` and `_deriveV2WrapSummary(pipelineResult)`. The completion helper calls `store.sessions.wrap(active.id, summary)`, then independently runs each teardown step inside its own `try/catch` so a failure in one (e.g. tmux already gone, lock-release threw) cannot block the others. The summary deriver resolves in order: (1) first step output with `parsedFields.summary` (a non-empty trimmed string) ‚Äî the prawduct `memory-update` shape; (2) first step output with `capturedText` ‚Äî other `ai-content` steps; (3) `pipelineResult.summary` ‚Äî reserved for a future `summary-derive` step per `lib/wrap-pipeline.js`; (4) `null` so `store.sessions.wrap` keeps the column NULL rather than writing an empty string.
  - **Gate predicate.** `_triggerWrapV2` calls `_completeV2Wrap` only when `pipelineResult.ok && pipelineResult.commitSha`. Clean-session wraps (`ok && !commitSha`, e.g. user clicked Wrap on a truly clean tree ‚Üí `commit` step returned `status: 'skipped'`) preserve the session by design ‚Äî there was nothing to wrap. Halted runs (`!ok`) and runner-thrown errors leave the session active so the user's Retry click re-enters from the same state.
  - **Plan + ADR split.** `.claude/plans/issue-139-methodology-aware-wrap.md` and `docs/adr/0002-wrap-pipeline-contract.md` now describe the Chunk 11 ‚Üí 11a / 11b / 11c split with per-sub-chunk Scope / Acceptance / Critic sections. Rationale recorded inline so future-self / Critic understands why a bare flag flip wasn't the right shape.
  - **Tests** (+11 in `test/sessions.test.js`, new `V2 lifecycle transition (#139 Chunk 11a)` block under `triggerWrap (methodology-driven)`): (1) `ok + commitSha ‚Üí wraps the session and runs full teardown` ‚Äî pins `getActive ‚Üí null`, the wrapped row's `status` + `wrapSummary`, plus `tmux.killSession` / `documentLocks.releaseBySession` were called with the right args; (2) `ok + null commitSha (clean session) ‚Üí session stays active`; (3) `halted (!ok) ‚Üí session stays active` even when `pipelineResult.commitSha` is populated (the halt gates the wrap, not the SHA); (4) `runner thrown ‚Üí session stays active`; (5) `summary: parsedFields.summary wins over capturedText`; (6) `summary: capturedText is fallback when no parsedFields.summary`; (7) `summary: null when no step output carries summary signal`; (8) `tmux.killSession failure is non-fatal ‚Äî session still wraps`; (9) `releaseBySession failure is non-fatal ‚Äî session still wraps`; (10) `store.sessions.wrap failure is non-fatal ‚Äî teardown still runs` (each teardown step's try/catch isolates the others, addressing Critic minor coverage gap); (11) `second triggerWrap after a successful V2 wrap returns "No active session"` (pins the idempotency contract at the call-site level ‚Äî after the first wrap, the entry-point pre-check rejects before reaching the runner). Stubs `wrapPipeline.runWrapPipeline` to return fixed structured results so the lifecycle behavior is pinned without exercising real step handlers. Full suite: 2235 / 2235 pass (was 2224 at end of Chunk 10; net +11).
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (3 MINOR addressed; YELLOW ‚Üí GREEN):** (M1) Coverage gap on `tmuxSession === null/empty` defense-in-depth branch ‚Äî added a comment block on `lib/sessions.js:855‚Äì860` explaining `triggerWrap`'s entry-point pre-check makes the guard unreachable via the normal V2 flow, but kept the guard so the helper remains safe to call from future callers. (M2) No idempotency test ‚Äî added test 11 above. (M3) No test for `store.sessions.wrap` throwing ‚Äî added test 10 above. NIT findings on gate-predicate type narrowing and `clearIdleCache` indentation asymmetry declined as not load-bearing (runner contract guarantees `commitSha` type; cache-clear placement is intentional ‚Äî no cache to clear when there's no tmux session).

- **`invoke-critic` action producer (#139, Chunk 11b)** ‚Äî second sub-chunk of the original Chunk 11 (split into 11a / 11b / 11c during 11a's session-start scope review). Wires the prawduct `invoke-critic` action button (previously a no-op declaration in `data/templates/prawduct/template.json:84`) so clicking "Run Critic" writes an entry to `<project>/.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json` per Chunk 7's read contract: an array of `{branchName: string, timestamp: ISO 8601, ...}` entries. Without this writer, the `critic-check` wrap step always emitted `warning: true` on medium+ work because no producer existed for the file it reads. With Chunks 11a + 11b shipped, the only remaining work to flip `wrapV2: true` by default is Chunk 11c (flag flip + prawduct template wiring + migration docs + test updates).
  - **`lib/actions/invoke-critic.js`** ‚Äî the handler. Resolves the current branch via `git rev-parse --abbrev-ref HEAD` (sync, so a single Node process can't interleave concurrent read-modify-write windows); returns `null` for detached HEAD / non-repo / missing git, which the handler surfaces as `ok: false` with a specific error. Reads existing `critic-runs.json` via a tolerant loader symmetric with the Chunk 7 reader (missing file / malformed JSON / non-array contents all degrade to `[]` so a corrupted file is silently rebuilt on next write). Appends `{branchName, timestamp: new Date().toISOString()}` to the array. **Atomic write:** tempfile + `fs.renameSync` within the same filesystem so a concurrent reader sees either the pre-write content or the full post-write content, never a half-written file. Caller-injection seams: `options.branchName` (skips git resolution), `options.now` (deterministic timestamps for tests).
  - **`lib/actions.js`** ‚Äî the dispatcher. Maps action `command` ‚Üí handler module via `ACTION_DISPATCH`. Validates that the project's methodology declares the command in its `actions[]` block before dispatching: the methodology template is the authorization surface, so a frontend that POSTs a command not declared by the project's methodology gets a 404 rather than executing. Handlers that throw are caught and surfaced as `{ok: false, error: 'action handler threw: ...'}`. Separate from the wrap-pipeline dispatch table (`lib/wrap-pipeline.js:STEP_DISPATCH`) so user-clicked actions and pipeline-runner steps don't accidentally couple ‚Äî adding a new action is a one-line entry plus a sibling module under `lib/actions/`.
  - **`POST /api/projects/:name/actions/:command`** (`server.js`). Body is the handler's `options` (object-only; arrays / strings / numbers / null all coerce to `undefined` so the handler's default-param governs ‚Äî symmetric with the wrap endpoint's body-parsing contract). Status codes: `200` ok or handler-soft-fail (detached HEAD, missing project path, etc ‚Äî frontend surfaces the error inline); `404` for unknown project or undeclared action command; `500` for handler-thrown.
  - **`lib/projects.js:enrichProject`** ‚Äî methodology object now carries `actions[]` (filtered to entries with string `label` + `command`; `confirm` coerced to boolean). The frontend reads this from the `GET /api/projects/:name` response to decide which action buttons to render, so no second round-trip to `/api/methodologies/:id` is needed.
  - **Frontend wire-up** (`public/session.html`, `public/session.js`, `public/session.css`). New `<span id="methodologyActions">` slot in the banner-actions row; `renderMethodologyActions(actions)` populates it after `loadProject`. Click handler: optional `window.confirm` when the action declares `confirm: true`, then `apiMutate POST /api/projects/.../actions/<command>` with the request body `{}`. Inline disable + label-change ("Run Critic‚Ä¶") for the duration of the request so a user can't double-fire. Brief banner-anchored toast (`#methodologyActionToast`) confirms success/error; hides after 3.5s.
  - **Tests** (+31): `test/actions-invoke-critic.test.js` (15 ‚Äî new-file create, append to existing, malformed JSON recovery, top-level-object recovery, caller-supplied branchName, detached HEAD failure, non-git directory failure, empty/missing project.path validation, `now()` injection seam, no `.tmp.*` remnants after success, idempotency across multiple invocations, `.tangleclaw` exists as regular file (post-Critic), `_redactProjectPath` strips absolute path (post-Critic), `_redactProjectPath` no-op when projectPath empty/null (post-Critic), round-trip pin against the Chunk 7 reader's shape filter). `test/actions-dispatcher.test.js` (7 ‚Äî runs invoke-critic for prawduct, rejects undeclared action on minimal, rejects unknown command, returns "not found" for unknown project, validates inputs, forwards options to handler, catches handler throws). `test/api-actions.test.js` (9 ‚Äî 200 ok, 404 unknown project, 404 undeclared action, 404 unknown command, body forwarded as options, non-object body coerced, soft-fail returns 200 ok:false, prawduct project response includes actions[], minimal project response has empty actions[]). Full suite: 2255 / 2255 pass (was 2224 at end of Chunk 10; net +31).
  - **Out of scope (deliberately):** no frontend unit tests for `renderMethodologyActions` / `invokeMethodologyAction` / `showMethodologyActionToast` ‚Äî they're DOM-coupled glue (~80 lines) that don't justify extracting a separate helper module the way `wrap-drawer.js` did for the multi-step drawer's view-model logic. **Per CLAUDE.md frontend-testing rule: the dev server was NOT run to validate the button in a browser ‚Äî manual smoke test required at user review.** Server-side request/response is well-pinned via the API tests; frontend integration is straightforward glue (`apiMutate ‚Üí result.ok ‚Üí toast`).
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (1 MAJOR + 3 MINORs + 1 NIT addressed; YELLOW ‚Üí GREEN).** (M1, MAJOR) `public/session.js:254` accessed `api.lastError.message` to render the error toast ‚Äî but `api.lastError` is a **string** per `public/api-helper.js` (lines 2030 and 2170 in the same file consume it as a bare string, confirming the pattern). Result: every server-returned 4xx error showed the literal "Run Critic: failed" toast instead of the real reason. Fixed by dropping `.message`. No coverage caught this because the disclaimed frontend test gap left the toast string the user sees unpinned. (M2) `execSync('git rev-parse --abbrev-ref HEAD')` had no timeout ‚Äî a pathological FS hang or git-lfs prompt could stall the single-process server's event loop. Added `timeout: 5000`. (M3) Error messages from `fs.mkdirSync` / `fs.writeFileSync` / `fs.renameSync` leak the project absolute path into the HTTP response (low impact for a single-user dev tool but reachable via the public API). Added `_redactProjectPath` helper that replaces the project's absolute path with the literal `<project>` placeholder; applied to both fs error paths. (M4) Test gap on `.tangleclaw` existing as a regular file ‚Äî `mkdirSync({recursive: true})` throws EEXIST in that case; pinned with a new test that verifies the surfaced shape + redaction. (N1) `document.querySelector('.methodology-action-btn[data-command="..."]')` used unescaped template interpolation; defended with `CSS.escape` fallback to a manual escape so methodology-template-supplied command strings containing selector-syntax characters can't break the button-disable behavior. Declined: (MINOR) substring-based error ‚Üí HTTP-status routing in `server.js` is fragile but not regressing today ‚Äî a follow-up to add a `code` field to `runAction`'s return contract is filed conceptually but not pinned to a chunk; (MINOR) `confirm: true` action-path coverage ‚Äî acknowledged scope gap, scope-disclaimed alongside other frontend tests; (NIT) `ACTION_DISPATCH` single-entry table ‚Äî deliberately overbuilt for one entry per the module doc's scope-discipline rationale; (NIT) temp filename `${filePath}.tmp.${pid}.${Date.now()}` ‚Äî single-process sync I/O makes collision impossible, no need for `crypto.randomBytes`.
  - **Bonus follow-up.** Chunk 7's open question ‚Äî "where does `critic-runs.json` get written?" ‚Äî is now answered. The Chunk 11c flag flip can ship without `critic-check` defaulting to `warning: true` on every prawduct project's medium+ work, because the Run Critic button has a real producer.

- **Frontend multi-step wrap progress drawer (#139, Chunk 10)** ‚Äî tenth chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the single-button confirm modal with a drawer that renders each pipeline step's status (`pending` / `running` / `done` / `blocked` / `skipped`) plus inline interactive recovery widgets for blocked or warning steps. The legacy `wrapV2:false` modal flow is unchanged byte-for-byte; the drawer only opens when the server response carries a `pipelineResult` (V2 path). With Chunk 10 landed, the wrap UX is functional end-to-end against the Chunks 4‚Äì9 step handlers; Chunk 11 (default flip) is now validatable against a real interactive flow.
  - **New `public/wrap-drawer.js` helper module** (mirrors `public/api-helper.js` pattern). Exposes `window.tcWrapDrawerHelpers` with seven pure functions ‚Äî `buildStepRow`, `deriveDetail`, `summarizePipelineStatus`, `decisionWidgetForBlockedStep`, `warningWidgetForStep`, `prCheckResolutionWidget`, `collectOptionsFromAccessors`. All DOM-free so they're testable in a Node vm sandbox; `session.js` consumes the view-models and owns the DOM. Module pattern matches the existing api-helper factory: attaches to `window` in the browser, exports via `module.exports` for tests.
  - **`public/session.html`** ‚Äî new drawer markup after the existing wrap modal: `#wrapDrawerBackdrop`, `#wrapDrawer` (with `.wrap-drawer-header`, `#wrapDrawerStatus`, `#wrapStepList`, `#wrapDrawerDecision`, action buttons `#wrapDrawerCancelBtn` / `#wrapDrawerRetryBtn` / `#wrapDrawerDoneBtn` / `#wrapDrawerCloseBtn`). Drawer hidden until `openWrapDrawer(pipelineResult)` is invoked. `wrap-drawer.js` script tag added before `session.js` so the helpers are available at page-script init.
  - **`public/session.css`** ‚Äî full drawer style block. Reuses the existing `.drawer-backdrop` / `.drawer-handle` styles (peek drawer pattern); adds `.wrap-drawer`, per-step row grid (`.wrap-step-row` + `.wrap-step-main` + `.wrap-step-status`), status-pill color tones (`pending` / `running` / `done` / `blocked` / `skipped`), warning + blocker row backgrounds, decision-widget styles for checkbox / textarea / pr-list shapes.
  - **`public/session.js`** ‚Äî `confirmWrap` now branches on response shape: V2 (`data.pipelineResult` present) ‚Üí `openWrapDrawer(data.pipelineResult)`; V1 (legacy `{ok, status:'wrapping'}`) ‚Üí existing `showWrappingState` + polling loop, byte-equal to pre-Chunk-10. New functions: `openWrapDrawer` / `closeWrapDrawer` / `renderWrapDrawer` (orchestrates status banner + step list + decision widget + action-button visibility) / `renderStepRow` (`<li>` per result) / `renderDecisionWidget` (checkbox or textarea) / `renderPrResolutionWidget` (per-PR dropdown row) / `retryWrap` (collects decision-widget values via accessor functions and re-POSTs to `/wrap` with `{options}`). Action-button visibility logic: `Retry` shows when `blockedAt` is set OR a warning/pr-list widget rendered; `Done` shows on clean `ok:true`; `Cancel/Close` always present; close-affordances wired (X button, Cancel button, backdrop click). The `currentPipelineResult` module-level variable retains the most recent result so a retry's response replaces it.
  - **Decision widgets ‚Äî three shapes, one collection path.**
    - **`test` blocked** (`blocker:true` + `allowOverride:true`) ‚Üí checkbox "Override: skip tests and record the override in the commit body" ‚Üí on retry sends `options.skipTests:true`.
    - **`critic-check` warning** (`blocker:false` step with `output.warning === true`) ‚Üí textarea "Skip rationale (recorded in commit body ‚Äî required to clear the warning):" ‚Üí on retry sends `options.criticSkipRationale:<trimmed text>` (whitespace-only text is dropped so a user can't bypass the gate by typing spaces).
    - **`pr-check` unresolved session-scoped PRs** (`output.sessionScoped.length > 0` and not in `output.resolutions`) ‚Üí per-PR `<select>` with `merge` / `defer` / `ignore` ‚Üí on retry sends `options.prHandling: {[prNumber]: 'merge'|'defer'|'ignore'}` (empty selections filtered out; full-map dropped if no PR has a resolution).
    - **`lint` blocked + `commit` blocked** intentionally have NO recovery widget ‚Äî the user fixes outside the drawer (lint errors ‚Üí edit code; pre-commit hook rejection ‚Üí fix the hook-rejected issue) and clicks Retry to re-run the pipeline. `decisionWidgetForBlockedStep` returns `null` for these kinds; drawer still shows the row with blockers surfaced inline.
  - **Server-side options threading** ‚Äî `lib/sessions.js`: `triggerWrap(projectName, options)` now accepts a second arg (V2-only ‚Äî ignored on the legacy NL-prompt path so existing call sites stay back-compat). `_triggerWrapV2(project, active, options)` passes through to `wrapPipeline.runWrapPipeline(name, options)`. The runner already accepted `options = {}` since Chunk 3; Chunk 10 closes the loop from the frontend to the runner. **`server.js`**: `POST /api/sessions/:project/wrap` reads `body.options` (object-only; arrays / strings / numbers / null all coerce to `undefined` so the runner's default-param governs), passes to `sessions.triggerWrap`, and surfaces `pipelineResult` on the response. **HTTP semantics for V2 blocked pipelines: `200 OK` with `status:'blocked'` (not `500`).** A blocked pipeline is an expected outcome the drawer renders ‚Äî the runner produced a structured result, the endpoint returns it. `500` is reserved for the runner throwing (no `pipelineResult` present); `404` still for missing project / session.
  - **No live progress updates yet.** TangleClaw has no WebSocket / SSE infrastructure today (only ttyd's terminal proxy). The pipeline runs synchronously in the request; the drawer renders the final state, not in-progress. Adding live updates means a new SSE channel + per-pipeline run IDs ‚Äî a separate chunk, tracked as a Chunk-11-or-later follow-up. The drawer's "Running‚Ä¶" status banner is a brief flash during the in-flight POST; the result paint happens once on response.
  - **Out of scope (deliberately):** `invoke-critic` action button still has no implementation (Chunk 7's known follow-up); pipeline pause-mid-run (current model is fail ‚Üí collect options ‚Üí retry, which matches the runner's request/response contract); custom-methodology decision widgets beyond the three above (kinds without a widget show the row with raw blockers and rely on user-side fix + retry).
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (4 MAJOR + 3 MINOR + 1 NIT addressed; YELLOW ‚Üí GREEN):** (M1) Retry POST omitted the password ‚Äî broke `deleteProtected` installs. Fixed by caching the password from the initial confirm modal on `openWrapDrawer` and replaying it on retry. The replaced dead-state variable `currentPipelineResult` (N2, never read after assignment) repurposed as `currentWrapPassword`. (M2) ADR 0002 extended with the Chunk-10 entry ‚Äî Status line + Migration-path Chunk 10 + Chunk 11 sections cover the runner-API surface change (`triggerWrap(name, options)` second arg), HTTP 200-on-blocked semantics, the three decision widgets' shape contract, the warning-state re-run trade-off, password replay on retry, the no-live-updates deferral, and scope-discipline note on bundled templates. (M3) `retryWrap` silently swallowed `apiMutate ‚Üí null` (403/404/500/network). Added `renderWrapDrawerError(message)` that surfaces the inline error via the `wrapDrawerStatus` element with `--error` tone, reading the message from the side-channel `api.lastError`. (M4) Critic-warning state hid the Done button so a user with a passing-but-warned wrap had only Retry (re-runs the pipeline ‚Üí second commit) or Close (no rationale recorded). Fixed by showing Done alongside Retry on warning-only state ("accept warning as-is") and surfacing the trade-off inline as a `.wrap-decision-note` in the pr-check resolution widget. (M5) PR-resolution roundtrip had no test ‚Äî frontend ‚Üí server ‚Üí runner for `prHandling` was unverified. Added `test/api-sessions.test.js` "threads prHandling map verbatim from request body to runner" pinning both the shape (`{string-pr-num: enum}`) and the key-type contract (string, matching `_normalizeHandling`'s `String(key)` lookup). (N5) `deriveDetail` had no case for `ai-content` or `version-bump`. Added both ‚Äî ai-content surfaces "captured N fields" or "captured" fallback; version-bump surfaces `from ‚Üí to` or skipped reason. +5 tests for the new cases. (N6) Renderer loop iterated `H.buildStepRow` twice per step (once for the step list, once for the decision widget). Hoisted into a single `rows` array with `{row, raw}` tuples consumed by both loops. (T3) PR-row title was a `<span>` with the URL only in the tooltip. Made it an `<a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">` when the URL is present, falling back to span when absent. (N1) Filed [#185](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/185) ‚Äî "Live wrap pipeline progress via SSE" ‚Äî for the deferred WebSocket/SSE phase. (N7) Filed [#186](https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/issues/186) ‚Äî "V2 wrap success doesn't transition session lifecycle" ‚Äî Chunk 11 will fold the fix into the default-flip work; logged in ADR 0002's Chunk 11 entry. Declined: (N4) `aria-modal` toggle pattern is a pre-existing peek-drawer convention; (T1) `status:'wrapping'` field name is misleading for V2 success but the drawer ignores `status` so impact is zero; (T2) `Object.freeze(options)` comment lie is Chunk-4 debt.
  - **Tests** (+40 after Critic fixes; was +34 pre-Critic): 11 cases for `buildStepRow` (done step with commit detail; blocked step gets `isBlocker:true` + `blocked` tone; warning row from `output.warning`; unknown kind falls back to raw kind; missing output handled gracefully; pr-check detail singular/plural; priming-roll target chunk surfaced; ai-content N-fields plural; ai-content singular; ai-content text-only fallback; version-bump from‚Üíto; version-bump skipped reason ‚Äî last five added in Critic fixes), 6 for `summarizePipelineStatus` (success with sha; success without sha; blocked + reason; warning when ok:true with warning step; error when top-level error without blockedAt; null/undefined input ‚Üí error tone), 4 for `decisionWidgetForBlockedStep` (test gets checkbox; non-blocker null; lint blocker ‚Üí null since no recovery; null/undefined input), 3 for `warningWidgetForStep` (critic-check textarea; warning:false ‚Üí null; unknown kind ‚Üí null), 5 for `prCheckResolutionWidget` (returns prs when session-scoped + unresolved; filters out resolved; null when no session-scoped; null when all resolved; null for non-pr-check kinds), 8 for `collectOptionsFromAccessors` (skipTests true collected; false omitted; rationale trimmed + included; whitespace-only rationale omitted; prHandling filters empties; full-empty prHandling omitted; all-three combined; missing accessor keys tolerated). API-layer (+5 in `test/api-sessions.test.js`, +1 from Critic M5): options threading from request body ‚Üí `runWrapPipeline`; blocked pipeline returns `200` with `pipelineResult`; thrown pipeline returns `500`; non-object options bodies coerced to `undefined`; `prHandling` map round-trips verbatim with `string`-typed keys. Lib-layer (+1 in `test/sessions.test.js`): `triggerWrap` options-threading contract pinned for both present and absent cases. Full suite: 2224 / 2224 pass (was 2179 at end of Chunk 9; net +45 from Chunk 10).

- **Wrap pipeline `commit` step real handler + single-transaction orchestration (#139, Chunk 9)** ‚Äî ninth and load-bearing chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/commit.js` with the real flush + commit + `lastWrapSha`-stamp orchestrator. This is the chunk every prior step has been staging *for*: priming-roll's `newContent`, ai-content's `capturedText`, critic-check's `owedRationale`, pr-check's `resolutions` ‚Äî all of it lands in one git commit (or no commit on a truly clean session) at the end of the pipeline. With Chunk 9 landed, 7 of 8 step kinds (`lint`, `test`, `ai-content`, `priming-roll`, `critic-check`, `pr-check`, `commit`) have real handlers; only `version-bump` remains as a Chunk-3 stub. Behavior remains fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so no existing project sees any wrap-flow change. Chunks 10 (frontend) + 11 (default flip) are now validatable against an end-to-end functional wrap.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/commit.js`**: orchestrates four phases ‚Äî (1) flush staged filesystem writes (currently only `priming-roll` produces these; duck-typed on shape `{primingPath, newContent, changed}` so any future write-producing step that mimics the shape Just Works without a dispatch-table edit), (2) detect "anything to commit?" via `git status --porcelain` ‚Äî empty output ‚Üí `{ok:true, status:'skipped', output:{reason:'no changes to commit', commitSha:null}}` so a session that ran the pipeline but produced no real edits stays a no-op at the git level, (3) `git add -A` + `git commit -m <session-derived message>` (the user clicking Session Wrap is opting into "everything in my working tree belongs to this session" ‚Äî Chunk 10's UI will surface the file list so the user can cancel before this step runs), (4) capture commit SHA via `git rev-parse HEAD` and stamp `lastWrapSha` on `projConfig` so Chunks 4 (lint scope) + 7 (critic-check range detection) can drop their `HEAD~10..HEAD` fallback in a future chunk.
  - **Single-transaction discipline.** A pipeline failure before this step leaves whatever the AI / priming-roll already put into the working tree, but produces NO commit. The user fixes the blocker and retries; on the next attempt this step picks up everything still in the working tree plus the fresh-run staged writes. Re-running the wrap is idempotent at the commit level ‚Äî the runner produces zero or one commit per invocation.
  - **Blocker contract: `blocker:true` (real, not always-ok).** Unlike Chunks 5‚Äì8 which all returned `ok:true` regardless of internal probe failures, this step is the load-bearing transactional gate. `git status` failure, `git add` failure, or `git commit` failure (typically a pre-commit hook rejection) ‚Üí `{ok:false, status:'blocked'}` with the git/hook output surfaced in `blockers[]`. The runner halts the pipeline; the user fixes the hook-rejected issue and retries the wrap. We do **NOT** pass `--no-verify` (per CLAUDE.md's Git Safety Protocol) ‚Äî the pre-commit hook is the user's intentional gate.
  - **Commit message strategy: `session-content`.** Subject derived from a chunk-tag regex on the current branch (`chunk-9-‚Ä¶` ‚Üí `Session wrap (chunk 9)`; dotted/lettered ids like `chunk-10c.2` are honored to match the priming-roll / critic-check chunk-id grammar) with a branch-name fallback (`Session wrap on feat/some-feature`) and a generic fallback for detached HEAD (`Session wrap`). Body assembled from shape-typed staged entries: priming-roll's `pointer.current` ‚Üí `- Priming rolled to Chunk N ‚Äî Title` (with `(blocked on: ‚Ä¶)` on the next line when present), ai-content's `capturedText` ‚Üí `- AI content (<step-id>): captured` or `- AI content (<step-id>): captured fields [a, b, c]` if `parsedFields` is non-empty, critic-check's `owedRationale` ‚Üí `- Critic skip rationale: <text>` (or `- Critic warning: medium+ work without Critic dispatch (no rationale provided)` when warning fired without a rationale), pr-check's `sessionScoped` + `resolutions` ‚Üí `- Open session-scoped PRs: N` + `  - PR #<num>: merge|defer|ignore` per resolution. Subject capped at `MAX_SUBJECT_LEN = 72` chars with `‚Ä¶` truncation marker so `git log --oneline` stays readable. Anything not matching a known shape is silently skipped ‚Äî extra staging keys aren't an error.
  - **`lastWrapSha` stamping is non-fatal on failure.** The commit already landed by the time we reach this stamp; the stamp is a hint for later steps' range detection. We `log.warn` and continue, surfacing the outcome on `output.stamped: boolean` so the Chunk 10 UI can render "stamp failed ‚Äî Chunks 4/7 will keep using the HEAD~10 fallback next wrap" inline rather than producing a runner-level blocker. A clean session that skipped the commit does NOT stamp (no SHA to record).
  - **Bundled templates updated**: `data/templates/prawduct/template.json` and `data/templates/minimal/template.json` each declare `"blocker": true` on their `commit` step. (`data/templates/tilt/template.json` carries the same change locally but is gitignored ‚Äî `.gitignore:24` lists it as an "Unreleased methodology template" ‚Äî so it doesn't ride along in this PR; the matching tilt-blocker test is gracefully skipped when the file isn't on disk.) The back-compat shim (`lib/skills.js:wrapShapeFromTemplate`) reads only `step.id` and `step.captureFields[]`, so adding `blocker` to an existing step does NOT change the legacy `wrapV2:false` NL-prompt path's byte-equal output ‚Äî the regression pin in `test/sessions.test.js` continues to pass. This is the first chunk that DOES touch a bundled template's `wrap_pipeline` schema; doing so explicitly (vs. an implicit "commit kind is implicitly blocker:true" rule in the runner) keeps the runner shape-dumb and the methodology template the single source of truth for the contract.
  - **Runner threading**: `lib/wrap-pipeline.js:runWrapPipeline` now reads `commitSha` from any step result whose `output.commitSha` is a non-empty string, populating the top-level `result.commitSha` field.
