The threading is step-id-agnostic (any step with an `output.commitSha` populates it; first-wins) so a future methodology with a renamed commit step still surfaces the SHA without a runner edit. Halted pipelines and clean-session skips leave `result.commitSha = null`.
  - **`lib/store.js:DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG`** gains `lastWrapSha: null` ‚Äî round-trips through `projectConfig.load` / `.save` and merges with on-disk configs that pre-date this field (the deep-merge loop in `projectConfigApi.load` propagates the default for missing keys). Chunks 4 and 7's range detection will switch to `<lastWrapSha>..HEAD` in a future chunk when they read this field; for now they keep the `HEAD~10..HEAD` fallback that's authoritative on never-wrapped projects.
  - **Six pure helpers exported** for testability: `_flushStagedWrites(staged)` (idempotent ‚Äî `changed:false` is a no-op; missing `changed` defaults to "needs write"; returns array of `{stepId, path}` for the run output), `_buildSubject(branch)` (chunk-tag ‚Üí branch-name ‚Üí generic fallback; truncates over `MAX_SUBJECT_LEN`), `_buildBodyLines(staged)` (shape-typed across the four producers; returns `[]` for null/empty/unknown shapes), `_buildMessage(staged, branch)` (subject + blank + body assembly; subject-only when body is empty), `_stampLastWrapSha(projectPath, sha)` (returns `boolean`; `log.warn`s on failure and continues ‚Äî the commit already landed), plus the `MAX_SUBJECT_LEN` constant.
  - **Three `_internal` shims** for testability: `exec` (thin `execFile`-based Promise wrapper that never throws on non-zero exit ‚Äî matches the pr-check / critic-check pattern), `writeFileSync`, `mkdirSync`. `execFile` rather than `exec` ‚Äî argv-style arg passing means multi-line messages with quotes pass through to `git commit -m` byte-intact without any shell-quoting math.
  - **Test scaffolding pollution fix (Chunk 3 ‚Üí 9).** Several Chunk-3-era tests in `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` and `test/sessions.test.js` ran the full pipeline against tmp-dir projects that aren't git repos ‚Äî they passed in Chunks 3‚Äì8 because every step was either a stub or always-ok. Now that `commit` is a real blocker handler, those tests would hit `git status` failure on a non-repo and return `ok:false`. Fix: the affected tests now monkey-patch `STEP_DISPATCH['commit']` to the canonical no-op for the duration of their assertion (with `finally`-block restore), keeping each test focused on what it actually asserts (runner skeleton, blocker semantics, options threading, V2 routing) rather than accidentally exercising the real commit handler. The Chunk-9 commit-handler tests stand up real git repos via `execSync('git init ...')` in `beforeEach`.
  - **ADR 0002** updated (Status line + Migration-path Chunk 9 entry) with the full contract ‚Äî flush order, single-transaction discipline, blocker:true semantics, message-builder strategy, `lastWrapSha` stamping, bundled-template `blocker:true` addition, and the byte-equal-pin compatibility note.
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes:** 1 MAJOR + 4 MINORs addressed before this PR opened. (MAJOR-1) `data/templates/tilt/template.json` is gitignored as "Unreleased methodology templates" ‚Äî the test asserting `blocker:true` would have broken on a clean clone. Fixed by making the tilt assertion gracefully skip when `store.templates.get('tilt')` returns null, and noting the locally-vs-tracked split in CHANGELOG + ADR 0002. (MINOR-1) Comment in `commit.js:_internal.exec` claimed `-F -` (stdin) but the code uses `-m` (argv) ‚Äî comment rewritten to accurately describe the argv-style execFile-handling. (MINOR-2) Silent-swallow on `priming-roll` staged entries with `pointer:{current:null, allDone:false}` ‚Äî the file was being flushed but the commit body produced no line; added an explicit "Priming refreshed: plan has no parseable chunks" branch in `_buildBodyLines`. (MINOR-3, 4, 5) Three missing failure-path tests added: `_stampLastWrapSha` throwing ‚Üí `output.stamped:false` with `ok:true` (commit landed; stamp is a hint); `git rev-parse HEAD` failing AFTER commit landed ‚Üí `output.commitSha:null` with `ok:true`; `git add -A` failing ‚Üí blocked with the third path in the three-path git matrix (status / add / commit) now covered. **Consistency NIT addressed:** `_buildSubject`'s chunk-tag regex now uses `\bchunk` to mirror priming-roll + critic-check's CHUNK_TAG regex shape per ADR 0002 (prevents `junkchunk-9` matching). **Concurrent-wrap NIT addressed:** `_stampLastWrapSha` JSDoc now documents the lock-free load ‚Üí mutate ‚Üí save sequence relies on the runner's no-concurrent-wraps assumption.
  - **Tests** (+44, after Critic fixes): 5 cases for `_buildSubject` (chunk-tag extracted from `feat/chunk-N-‚Ä¶`; dotted/lettered chunk ids like `10c.2`; branch-name fallback; generic fallback on null branch; truncation at MAX_SUBJECT_LEN with ellipsis), 9 for `_buildBodyLines` (priming-roll pointer; priming-roll `blockedOn` surfaces under the pointer; priming-roll allDone; priming-roll `{current:null, allDone:false}` no-parseable-chunks line ‚Äî Critic MINOR-2 pin; ai-content with `parsedFields` lists the fields; ai-content without `parsedFields` minimal form; critic-check skip rationale; critic-check warning without rationale; pr-check sessionScoped count + per-PR resolutions; unknown-shape entries skipped silently; null/undefined/empty staged ‚Üí `[]`), 2 for `_buildMessage` (subject-only when body empty; subject + blank + body assembly), 5 for `_flushStagedWrites` (skips entries without primingPath/newContent; skips `changed:false`; writes when `changed:true`; writes when `changed` is missing as defensive default; null/undefined staged ‚Üí `[]`), 13 handler-level cases against a real git repo (blocks on missing project.path; skips with no commit when working tree is clean + no staged writes; skips when staged priming has `changed:false` and tree is clean; flushes a priming-roll write + produces one commit + captures hex SHA; picks up an AI-style MEMORY.md edit the AI made before commit step ran; stamps lastWrapSha on projConfig after a successful commit; blocks on pre-commit hook rejection with hook output surfaced ‚Äî `--no-verify` is NOT passed; blocks with explanatory message when `git status` fails ‚Äî non-repo simulation; surfaces flush errors as blockers, never as runner exceptions; session-content message includes priming pointer + AI captureFields + critic rationale on a real commit; generic subject on detached HEAD; `_stampLastWrapSha` throwing leaves `ok:true` with `stamped:false` ‚Äî Critic MINOR-3 pin; `git rev-parse HEAD` non-zero after commit lands leaves `ok:true` with `commitSha:null` ‚Äî Critic MINOR-4 pin; `git add -A` non-zero exit blocks with stderr surfaced ‚Äî Critic MINOR-5 pin), 3 for runner `commitSha` threading (surfaces from `output.commitSha` at the top level; null on a `skipped` commit step; null when the pipeline halts before commit), 3 for bundled-template `blocker:true` on commit step (prawduct, minimal, tilt-when-present), 2 for projConfig `lastWrapSha` (DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG default `null`; round-trips through load/save). Test-scaffolding updates: stub-conformance test (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`) ‚Äî `commit` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; only `version-bump` remains pinned. Full suite: 2179 / 2179 pass (was 2135 at end of Chunk 8).

- **Wrap pipeline `pr-check` step real handler (#139, Chunk 8)** ‚Äî eighth chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/pr-check.js` with a real `gh pr list` integration that surfaces open authored PRs to the wrap UI, partitioned into "this session's PR" and "other open PRs you might want to think about." Behavior fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`. With Chunk 8 landed, 6 of 8 step kinds (`lint`, `test`, `ai-content`, `priming-roll`, `critic-check`, `pr-check`) have real handlers; only `version-bump` and `commit` remain as Chunk-3 stubs.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/pr-check.js`**: shells out to `gh pr list --state open --author @me --json number,title,headRefName,baseRefName,url,createdAt,isDraft,author`. JSON fields kept narrow on purpose ‚Äî the commit-step + UI need just enough to identify and link the PR; adding fields without a downstream consumer is dead surface area. Parses JSON, filters drafts (unless `step.includeDrafts === true`), partitions into `sessionScoped` (PRs whose `headRefName` matches the current branch) and `otherOpen` via `_partitionPrs`. **Session-scope filter is intentionally minimal:** `headRefName === currentBranch` is the single source of truth ‚Äî more elaborate matching (PR title chunk-tag, issue number cross-reference, base-branch heuristic) is Chunk-10 UI territory; overly-clever filtering at the handler level produces false positives the user can't easily undo. **`gh` availability gate:** `gh --version` (no auth required, no network round-trip) up front; missing ‚Üí `{ok:true, status:'skipped', output:{reason:'gh CLI not available'}}`. **`gh pr list` failure modes** (no auth via `gh auth login`, repo isn't on GitHub, API hiccup, malformed JSON, non-array JSON) all degrade to skipped ‚Äî the first 200 chars of `stderr`/`stdout` are surfaced in `output.detail` so the UI can render the recovery hint inline rather than just "gh failed." **Draft filtering:** drafts hidden by default; unfiltered count exposed in `output.counts.rawTotal` so the UI can render "N drafts hidden" without re-calling gh.
  - **Caller-supplied resolution (Chunk 10 hand-off)**: `options.prHandling` accepts two shapes ‚Äî a string shortcut (`'merge'|'defer'|'ignore'`) applied to every session-scoped PR, or a per-PR object map (`{prNumber: 'merge'|'defer'|'ignore'}`). Both string and number keys are normalized to string before lookup, so a UI that emits `{42: 'merge'}` and one that emits `{"42": 'merge'}` resolve identically. Invalid shortcuts (`'squash-bomb'`), invalid map values (`'rebase-and-pray'`), unknown PR numbers (resolution references a non-session-scoped PR), and bad shape (`prHandling` is an array) are all surfaced via `output.invalidHandling[]` with a human-readable descriptor ‚Äî the UI prompts the user to fix and re-submit rather than silently dropping the choice. The handler validates but does NOT act on resolutions; the Chunk 9 `commit` step reads `context.staged[step.id]` to embed the choices in the wrap commit body / MEMORY block.
  - **Blocker contract: always `ok:true`** (matches the Chunk 7 always-ok pattern). The handler wraps ALL `_internal` probes (`isGhAvailable`, `getCurrentBranch`, `listOpenPrs`) in a single outer `try/catch` ‚Äî thrown probes (child_process spawn failure, OOM from maxBuffer, etc.) degrade to `{ok:true, status:'skipped', output:{reason:'pr-check probe failed', error}}` rather than runner-level "step threw" blockers. Even on a misconfigured project (missing `context.project.path`) the handler returns `{ok:true, status:'skipped'}` to honor the same contract ‚Äî a session with an open PR isn't a structural failure.
  - **Single-transaction discipline (matches Chunks 5‚Äì7)**: handler reads only ‚Äî never mutates git, never writes the filesystem. `context.staged[step.id] = {branch, sessionScoped, resolutions, invalidHandling}` only when `sessionScoped.length > 0 || resolutions has entries` (no PRs + no resolutions = nothing for the commit step to do). Invalid-only handling (caller passed a resolution for a PR that doesn't exist) does NOT stage ‚Äî pinned by test so a future refactor that always-stages doesn't accidentally make the commit step think there's work to do.
  - **Three pure helpers exported**: `_filterPrs(prs, step)` (draft filter; missing `isDraft` treated as not-a-draft); `_partitionPrs(prs, currentBranch)` (split into sessionScoped + otherOpen; null currentBranch ‚Üí everything in otherOpen ‚Äî fail-soft); `_normalizeHandling(prHandling, sessionScoped)` (returns `{resolutions, invalid}`; handles undefined / null / string shortcut / object map / array / unknown enum / unknown PR number, all pinned). Constants exported: `VALID_HANDLINGS` (Set), `GH_PR_JSON_FIELDS` (the gh JSON field list ‚Äî pinned so a downstream consumer can rely on the shape).
  - **Four `_internal` shims** for testability: `exec` (thin Promise wrapper for `node:child_process.exec`), `isGhAvailable`, `getCurrentBranch`, `listOpenPrs`. Each stubbable per-test (matches Chunk 7's pattern). The defaults never throw on non-zero exit ‚Äî gh exits non-zero on the no-auth path, no-repo path, and many other recoverable cases, so blanket-rethrow would defeat the never-blocks contract.
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `pr-check` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining two stubs (`version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned. The "runs all stubs end-to-end" runner-skeleton test now monkey-patches `lint`/`test`/`ai-content`/`priming-roll`/`critic-check`/`pr-check` to no-ops inside the test body (with `finally`-block restore). **Test-pollution fix:** the new `wrap-step pr-check ‚Äî handler` describe gets an `after()` hook restoring `_internal` to its true originals so the sibling `defaultListOpenPrs JSON handling` describe captures clean state rather than the previous suite's last-test stubs (caught during test authoring; pinned so other handler suites can follow the pattern when they grow sibling test groups).
  - **Scope discipline**: bundled prawduct template intentionally NOT extended with `{kind: "pr-check"}` in this chunk (matches Chunks 4 / 5 / 6 / 7's strict pattern ‚Äî would change the legacy `wrapV2:false` NL-prompt path's byte-equal pin). A future chunk paired with the Chunk-11 default flip will wire prawduct's pipeline.
  - **ADR 0002** updated (Status line + Migration-path Chunk 8 entry) with the full contract ‚Äî gh availability gate + failure-mode handling + session-scope filter + resolution staging + scope-discipline note.
  - **Critic pre-merge fixes (MINOR):** `_normalizeHandling` string-shortcut branch now writes string keys symmetrically with the object-map branch (both produce `{string: enum}` maps so the Chunk 9 commit step + Chunk 10 UI iterate with predictable key types); `defaultListOpenPrs` non-zero-exit `reason` field appends `‚Ä¶` when the raw gh stderr/stdout was longer than the 200-char truncation cap, so the UI knows there's more to see; added `_partitionPrs` regression pin for `headRefName: null` / empty (gh can return this for orphaned PRs whose source branch was deleted ‚Äî defensive against a future `pr.headRefName.startsWith(...)` refactor); added `GH_PR_JSON_FIELDS` snapshot pin so a rename / reorder of the gh JSON shape forces a CHANGELOG conversation rather than silently breaking downstream consumers.

- **Wrap pipeline `critic-check` step real handler (#139, Chunk 7)** ‚Äî seventh chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/critic-check.js` with a real session-history heuristic + Critic-dispatch detector that warns (never blocks) when medium+ work landed without an Independent Critic review. Behavior remains fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so no existing project sees any wrap-flow change. With Chunk 7 landed, 5 of 8 step kinds (`lint`, `test`, `ai-content`, `priming-roll`, `critic-check`) have real handlers; only `pr-check`, `version-bump`, and `commit` remain as Chunk-3 stubs.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/critic-check.js`**: heuristic for "medium+ work that should have had an Independent Critic review." **Three trip conditions (any-of):** commit count ‚â• `step.commitThreshold` (default 10), total line changes (insertions + deletions) ‚â• `step.lineChangeThreshold` (default 500), or a chunk-tag regex (`\bchunk[\s\-_]?N(?:\.N[a-z]?)*\b`, case-insensitive) matches the current branch name or any commit subject in the session range. **Branch wins over commit subjects** when both match ‚Äî more specific to the session ‚Äî and the matched id (e.g. `7` from `chunk-7`) is exposed in `output.heuristic.chunkTag` so the Chunk 10 UI can show "this looks like Chunk N work" in the warning. Separator-tolerant: matches `Chunk 7`, `chunk-7`, `chunk_7`, `chunk7`, and dotted sub-ids like `chunk-10c.2`. The id regex shape mirrors `priming-roll`'s (Chunk 6) so a chunk a priming-roll knows about is also a chunk-tag this heuristic detects. **Session range** resolved via `git symbolic-ref refs/remotes/origin/HEAD` ‚Üí main branch; range spec `<main>..HEAD`. Degraded fallback: `HEAD~10..HEAD` when the symref is missing, current branch is the main branch (work-directly-on-main case), or HEAD is detached ‚Äî `output.rangeDegraded` + `output.rangeDegradedReason` surface the degradation so the Chunk 10 UI can render "the heuristic is operating in degraded mode" instead of silently producing weird numbers. Chunk 9 will replace this with a `lastWrapSha`-stamped range once the `commit` step starts recording it on project records. **Critic-dispatch detection** reads `<project>/.tangleclaw/critic-runs.json` ‚Äî an array of `{branchName: string, timestamp: ISO 8601, ...}` entries ‚Äî and filters to entries whose `branchName` matches the current branch. Any match ‚Üí `criticRan: true`; otherwise `false`. Missing file / malformed JSON / non-array contents / no current-branch entries ‚Üí `false`. Entries are defensively filtered to those with a string `branchName` to guard against partial writes or schema drift. **The producer is intentionally NOT shipped in Chunk 7** ‚Äî the `invoke-critic` action button in methodology templates (`actions[]`) currently has no implementation, and the frontend wiring lives in Chunk 10. Chunk 7 ships only the read contract so the pipeline can produce meaningful output today via test fixtures, and the write side can land in any later chunk without re-touching this handler.
  - **Blocker contract: always `ok:true`** (Critic MAJOR-1 pre-merge fix). The spec from #139's Discovery says missing-Critic is a methodology rule the user can knowingly skip with rationale, not a structural failure that halts the pipeline. The handler wraps ALL `_internal` git probes (`getCurrentBranch`, `getMainBranch`, `getCommitCount`, `getDiffStats`, `getCommitSubjects`) in a single outer `try/catch` so any throw (git missing, exec timeout that isn't a clean non-zero exit, fs permission, OOM from maxBuffer) becomes a structured `{ok:true, status:'skipped', output:{reason:'git probe failed', error}}` rather than a runner-level "step threw" blocker. Matches the priming-roll / ai-content explicit-catch pattern from Chunks 5 + 6 ‚Äî drift would re-create the Chunk-7 Critic incident class. Even on a misconfigured project (missing `context.project.path`) the handler returns `{ok:true, status:'skipped'}` to honor the same contract.
  - **Rationale staging (matches Chunk 5 / 6 single-transaction discipline)**: when `warning === true` AND `options.criticSkipRationale` is a non-empty trimmed string, the rationale is staged at `context.staged[step.id] = {warning, owedRationale, branchName, isMediumPlus, criticRan, heuristic}` for the Chunk 9 `commit` step + Chunk 5 `memory-update` prompt to consume. Whitespace-only rationale is treated as no rationale (`owedRationale ‚Üí null`); the warning still surfaces and the Chunk 10 UI is expected to prompt the user before letting the pipeline commit. No warning ‚Üí nothing staged. The handler reads only ‚Äî no git mutations, no filesystem writes; staging is the sole side effect.
  - **Configurable thresholds** via `step.commitThreshold` / `step.lineChangeThreshold` (positive integers, default 10 / 500). Surfaced back through `output.heuristic.commitThreshold` / `lineChangeThreshold` so the UI can render the threshold inline ("12 commits exceed the 10-commit threshold"). **Footgun protection (Critic MAJOR-2 pre-merge fix):** `0` and negative values fall back to the defaults ‚Äî without the clamp, `commitThreshold: 0` would trip medium+ on every wrap (`0 ‚â• 0` is true), training users to dismiss the warning. Floats / NaN / strings / `null` / objects also fall back via `Number.isInteger` (not `Number.isFinite`). The chunk-tag regex is intentionally NOT exposed as a `step.chunkTagRegex` ‚Äî exposing regex strings via methodology JSON is a footgun (escaping pitfalls, no validation surface).
  - **Seven `_internal` shims** for testability: `exec` (the thin Promise wrapper for `node:child_process.exec`), `getCurrentBranch`, `getMainBranch`, `getCommitCount`, `getDiffStats`, `getCommitSubjects`, `loadCriticRuns`. Each can be independently stubbed per test (matches Chunk 4's `execShell` + `detectChangedFiles` + Chunk 5's `sendKeys` + `detectIdle` + `capturePane` + `sleep` patterns). The defaults are thin wrappers around real git / fs calls that never throw on non-zero exit ‚Äî they return `null` / `0` / `[]` so callers branch on intent rather than catching at every site.
  - **Four pure helpers exported**: `_detectChunkTag(branchName, subjects)` (branch wins; subjects searched in declaration order; `null` when neither matches; returns `{tag, source, match}` so the UI gets both the id alone for templating and the full match text for highlighting), `_isMediumPlus({commits, lineChanges, chunkTag, commitThreshold, lineChangeThreshold})` (any-of disjunction across the three signals; pinned at each boundary), `_pickRange(branch, mainBranch)` (returns `{rangeSpec, degraded, reason}`; degraded paths are pinned individually so a future refactor that drops a fallback case fails the test), and `_selectRecentRuns(entries, n)` (sorts critic-runs by `timestamp` descending ‚Äî newest first ‚Äî and slices `n`; entries with missing or non-string timestamps sort to the bottom; ISO 8601 string compare matches chronology for any well-formed timestamp). Sorting by timestamp instead of file-insertion order means a future producer that trims or re-sorts the file in-place can't accidentally change the "recent runs" the UI surfaces.
  - **Scope discipline**: bundled prawduct template is intentionally NOT extended with `{kind: "critic-check"}` in this chunk. Doing so would change the legacy `wrapV2:false` NL-prompt path's byte-equal behavior (the back-compat shim flattens `wrap_pipeline.steps[].id` into the legacy `wrap.steps[]` list that the NL prompt enumerates). Matches the strict scope policy from Chunks 4 / 5 / 6, where the bundled template was untouched and the new handler was wired in only via tests. A future chunk (likely paired with the Chunk-11 default flip) will wire prawduct's pipeline to include `critic-check` as part of the methodology-and-UI rollout ‚Äî at that point the legacy NL-prompt byte-equal pin gets a Chunk-7-explicit baseline update.
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `critic-check` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining three stubs (`pr-check`, `version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned. The "runs all stubs end-to-end" runner-skeleton test now monkey-patches `lint`/`test`/`ai-content`/`priming-roll`/`critic-check` to no-ops inside the test body (with `finally`-block restore) so the test continues to validate the runner's iteration + aggregation contract without standing up a real git history.
  - **ADR 0002** updated (Status line + Migration-path Chunk 7 entry) with the full contract ‚Äî heuristic + thresholds + range resolution + Critic-runs.json schema + blocker:false contract + rationale staging + scope-discipline note.
  - **Tests** (+43): 8 cases for `_detectChunkTag` (neither matches ‚Üí null; branch matches; commit subject matches when branch doesn't; branch wins over commits when both match; dotted sub-id `10c.2`; separator variants ‚Äî space/dash/underscore/none; case-insensitive; null/empty inputs), 6 for `_isMediumPlus` (commits boundary 10/10 trips, 9/10 does not; line-changes boundary 500/500 trips, 499/500 does not; chunkTag truthy alone trips; custom thresholds honored), 4 for `_pickRange` (happy `<main>..HEAD`; degraded on branch=main; degraded on detached HEAD; degraded on missing origin symref), 3 for `_selectRecentRuns` (empty/non-array ‚Üí `[]`; descending-by-timestamp ordering pinned regardless of input order; missing/non-string timestamps sort to bottom), 18 handler-level cases (always ok:true / never blocks ‚Äî even on missing project.path; baseline warning=false; commit-count trip with staging; line-change trip; chunk-tag-in-branch trip; chunk-tag-in-commit trip; critic-run on current branch suppresses warning; critic-run only on OTHER branches still warns ‚Äî filter pinned; rationale stages when warning + non-empty string; whitespace-only rationale ‚Üí null; custom thresholds honored; rangeDegraded on main branch; rangeDegraded on missing symref; `criticRunsRecent` sorts by timestamp descending regardless of file-write order ‚Äî Critic MINOR pin; thrown git probe ‚Üí structured skipped ‚Äî Critic MAJOR-1 pin; commitThreshold:0 falls back to default ‚Äî Critic MAJOR-2 pin; negative thresholds fall back; non-integer thresholds (3.7 / NaN / "5" / null / undefined / {}) fall back; non-string criticSkipRationale (number / array / object / true / null) staged as null ‚Äî typeof-guard pin), 4 for `defaultLoadCriticRuns` (missing file ‚Üí `[]`; malformed JSON ‚Üí `[]` no throw; non-array ‚Üí `[]`; filters out entries missing `branchName`). Full suite: 2106 / 2106 pass (was 2063 at end of Chunk 6).

- **Wrap pipeline `priming-roll` step real handler (#139, Chunk 6)** ‚Äî sixth chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/priming-roll.js` with a real plan-parser + managed-block roller. Pure server-side filesystem reads + a staged (deferred) write ‚Äî no AI handoff and no tmux interaction. Behavior remains fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so no existing project sees any wrap-flow change. With Chunk 6 landed, only `pr-check`, `critic-check`, `version-bump`, and `commit` remain as Chunk-3 no-op stubs; the dispatch table for V2 pipelines is now real for 4 of 8 kinds.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/priming-roll.js`**: parses `<project>/.claude/plans/<plan>.md` for the active chunk pointer and rolls forward a managed block in `<project>/.claude/priming/build-session.md`. **Plan format** matches the convention TangleClaw's own #139 build plan already uses: `### Chunk N: Title` headings, with `‚úÖ` anywhere on the heading line marking that chunk done. Chunk ids tolerate dotted / lettered sub-chunk numbering ‚Äî `1`, `2a`, `10c.2`, `12.3a.4` all parse (regex: `[0-9]+[a-z]?(?:\.[0-9]+[a-z]?)*`). **CRLF tolerance:** the parser splits on `/\r?\n/` and strips any trailing `\r` so Windows-authored / cross-edited plans parse byte-identical to LF-only ones (Critic MAJOR pre-merge fix ‚Äî repro: a CRLF plan was returning `[]` and bricking the wrap). The "current" chunk is the first un-done heading in document order; the "next" chunk is whatever follows it (or `null` when current is the tail). A `‚úÖ` body line does NOT promote a sibling chunk to done ‚Äî done-state is decided on the heading line only, so embedding ‚úÖ inside a chunk's prose stays safe. **Malformed `### Chunk Foo:` headings** (id slot non-numeric) are skipped from the chunk list but emit a `log.warn` with the line number and a 120-char tail ‚Äî the user has a recovery path instead of silent confusion (Critic MAJOR pre-merge fix; the parser stays strict, the user just sees what was dropped). **Blocker annotations:** the first `**Blocked on:** <text>` line in a chunk body (case-insensitive) is captured into the rolled pointer so the next session sees the blocker inline rather than discovering it by re-reading the plan; additional `**Blocked on:**` lines in the same chunk are ignored (the first wins). **Plan path resolution:** `step.planPath` (project-relative or absolute) wins when set; otherwise the handler scans `<project>/.claude/plans/*.md` and requires exactly one match ‚Äî zero or two+ ‚Üí `{ok:false, status:'blocked'}` with a "set step.planPath to disambiguate" message that names the colliding files. Project-relative `step.planPath` values get a containment check (`path.resolve` + `startsWith(projectRoot + sep)`) so `../escaped.md`-style traversal is refused ‚Äî defense-in-depth for the Chunk 11 default-flip and any future user-editable methodology authoring (Critic MINOR pre-merge fix). Absolute paths are accepted as-is on the assumption an author writing an absolute path knows what they're pointing at (e.g. a shared corporate plan archive). **Priming-file managed block:** the handler edits a region of `.claude/priming/build-session.md` (overridable via `step.primingPath`) delimited by `<!-- TANGLECLAW:PRIMING-ROLL:BEGIN -->` / `<!-- TANGLECLAW:PRIMING-ROLL:END -->`. The rest of the priming file is sacrosanct ‚Äî user-authored content surrounding the managed block is preserved byte-for-byte. When the markers don't exist yet, the handler appends a fresh managed block separated by a blank line; when the file itself doesn't exist yet, the handler stages a brand-new file at the priming path. **Out-of-order markers** (END before BEGIN, indicating a corrupted file) are defensively treated as "no managed block" ‚Üí fresh-append, doubling the markers rather than silently corrupting the file via wrong slice math (regression-pinned with a "user content between misordered markers survives" assertion). **Duplicated managed blocks** (user copy-pasted) edit only the first BEGIN/END pair; the orphan second pair is left as inert content ‚Äî pinned by test so a future "find all markers" refactor is intentional, not accidental.
  - **Single-transaction discipline (matches Chunk 5 `ai-content`)**: the handler does NOT touch the filesystem itself. It stages `context.staged[step.id] = {primingPath, newContent, changed, pointer, planPath}` for the Chunk 9 `commit` step to flush. A re-run against an unchanged plan + already-rolled priming file produces an unchanged `newContent` and reports `output.changed === false` ‚Äî the commit step is expected to skip writes when `changed === false`, so idempotent wraps stay no-op (pinned by the "reports changed=false when the rolled content matches existing file exactly" test). The single-transaction inertness pin from Chunk 3 (`runner is transactionally inert ‚Äî every stub receives an empty staged scratch`) still passes because that test monkey-patches every dispatch entry.
  - **Six pure helpers exported** for testability and Chunk 9 commit-step contract: `_parseChunks(planContent)` (returns `[{id, title, done, blockedOn, lineNo}]` in document order; tolerates the ‚úÖ-in-title case by stripping it from the rendered title while still using its presence to mark done; tolerates `### Chunk N (suffix): Title` heading variants like the plan's own "Chunk 12 (optional): ‚Ä¶"), `_selectPointer(chunks)` (returns `{current, next, allDone}`; first un-done wins; `next` is `null` when current is the tail; both `null` when allDone), `_renderPointerBody(pointer, planRelPath)` (markdown rendering of the rolled pointer ‚Äî no nested code fences so it nests safely inside a surrounding markdown body), `_replaceManagedBlock(prior, body)` (replaces in place when markers found; appends fresh block separated by a blank line when not; defensively appends on out-of-order markers), `_resolvePlanPath(projectPath, step)` (the disambiguation logic described above), `_resolvePrimingPath(projectPath, step)` (absolute-path resolver). Marker constants and default paths also exported: `BEGIN_MARKER`, `END_MARKER`, `DEFAULT_PRIMING_PATH`, `DEFAULT_PLANS_DIR`.
  - **`_internal`** holds `readFileSync`, `existsSync`, `readdirSync` so tests can stub disk failures (matches the `_internal.execShell` / `_internal.sendKeys` pattern from Chunks 4 and 5). The handler intentionally does NOT expose `writeFileSync` ‚Äî there's no write path to mock because there's no write path at all (the commit step in Chunk 9 owns that).
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `priming-roll` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining four stubs (`pr-check`, `critic-check`, `version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned. The "runs all stubs end-to-end" runner-skeleton test now monkey-patches `lint`/`test`/`ai-content`/`priming-roll` to no-ops inside the test body (with `finally`-block restore) so the test continues to validate the runner's iteration + aggregation contract without standing up a real plans dir.
  - **ADR 0002** updated (Status line + Migration-path section) with the Chunk 6 entry pinning the plan-format, managed-block-delimiter, and staged-write contracts so downstream chunks (Chunk 9 commit step, Chunk 10 progress drawer) can rely on them.
  - **Known follow-up (multi-plan disambiguation):** TangleClaw's own `.claude/plans/` already holds 10 plans; the prawduct bundled template's `next-session-prime` step ships without a `planPath` override. A wrap on TC-v3 itself with `wrapV2: true` would block with the disambiguation message until `step.planPath` is set per-project. This is gated entirely behind the Chunk-3 opt-in flag (default `false`), so no existing wrap is affected ‚Äî but Chunk 11 will need a smarter default-resolution strategy (most-recently-modified plan, an active-plan symlink convention, or a project-level "current plan" pointer) before the default flip lands. Captured here so it doesn't get lost.
  - **Tests** (+42): 11 cases for `_parseChunks` (basic id+title; ‚úÖ-anywhere done detection with ‚úÖ-in-title strip; body ‚úÖ does NOT promote; dotted/lettered sub-chunk ids `1`, `10c.2`, `12.3a.4`; **Blocked on:** capture; first-wins on multiple **Blocked on:** lines; case-insensitive match; empty/null input ‚Üí `[]`; `(suffix):` heading tolerance; CRLF parses byte-equivalent to LF ‚Äî Critic MAJOR-1 regression pin; malformed `### Chunk Foo:` heading skipped while well-formed siblings still parse ‚Äî Critic MAJOR-2 regression pin), 4 for `_selectPointer` (first-undone wins; tail current ‚Üí next=null; all-done; empty input), 5 for `_replaceManagedBlock` (in-place replace preserves surround; append-with-separator when no markers; no separator when prior empty; defensive double-append on out-of-order markers AND user content between misordered markers survives ‚Äî Critic MINOR pin; duplicated managed blocks edit only the first pair ‚Äî pin for refactor intentionality), 4 for `_renderPointerBody` (active + on-deck; blockedOn surfaces on active; allDone explicit; "no headings" fallback), 17 handler-level cases (missing project.path ‚Üí blocked; no plans dir ‚Üí blocked; empty plans dir ‚Üí blocked; multiple plans ‚Üí blocked with disambiguation; `step.planPath` honored; `step.planPath` missing file ‚Üí blocked; project-relative `step.planPath` escaping project root ‚Üí blocked ‚Äî Critic MINOR path-traversal defense pin; absolute `step.planPath` outside project root is accepted ‚Äî pinning the "absolute is trusted" branch; no chunk headings in plan ‚Üí blocked; fresh priming file ‚Üí managed block created in stage with `changed=true` AND no real disk write ‚Äî single-transaction pin; existing managed block replaced while user surround preserved byte-for-byte; idempotent re-roll ‚Üí `changed=false`; allDone reflected in pointer + rendered body; **Blocked on:** carries into rolled pointer; `step.primingPath` honored; plan-read throw ‚Üí blocked; priming-read throw with successful plan-read ‚Üí blocked). Full suite: 2063 / 2063 pass (was 2021 at end of Chunk 5).

- **Wrap pipeline `ai-content` step real handler (#139, Chunk 5)** ‚Äî fourth implementation chunk. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stub at `lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js` with a real send-prompt ‚Üí poll-idle ‚Üí capture-pane ‚Üí validate-fields handler. The same handler powers both prawduct's `memory-update` step (AI writes the session block to `.tangleclaw/memories/MEMORY.md` via its own file tools ‚Äî TangleClaw owns the *prompt*, not the write) and `summary-derive` (AI emits `## Heading` blocks that the handler parses against `step.captureFields`). One substitution token is supported in this chunk: `{previousMemoryBlock}` interpolates the captured text of the prior step whose `stepId === 'memory-update'`, enabling `summary-derive` to deterministically reference the memory block the AI just produced (instead of trusting the AI to re-read its own scrollback). Behavior remains fully gated behind `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so no existing project sees any wrap-flow change.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/ai-content.js`**: defensive blocks on missing `context.session.tmuxSession` or empty `step.prompt`. Sends the interpolated prompt via `_internal.sendKeys(tmuxSession, prompt, {enter:true})`. Sleeps an initial settle window (`INITIAL_SETTLE_MS = 3000`), then polls `_internal.detectIdle(tmuxSession)` every `POLL_INTERVAL_MS = 2000` until idle is reported (`detectIdle` defines idle as ‚â•10s of unchanged pane output ‚Äî pinned in `lib/sessions.js`). Total wait capped by `MAX_WAIT_MS = 5 min`; exceeded ‚Üí `{ok:false, status:'blocked', blockers:['AI did not return within Xs']}`. On idle, captures full pane scrollback via `_internal.capturePane(tmuxSession, {full:true})` and validates. If `step.captureFields[]` is set, each field must appear as a `## Heading` (case-insensitive) with non-empty content; otherwise the handler asserts only that the AI returned ‚â•`MIN_RESPONSE_CHARS = 20` chars (catches no-ops and rare premature-idle captures). Successful captures are staged in `context.staged[step.id] = {capturedText, parsedFields}` for the eventual `commit` step (Chunk 9) to consume. Failures of `sendKeys` / `detectIdle` / `capturePane` are caught and surfaced as blocker entries rather than thrown ‚Äî the runner already converts thrown handlers to blocked results, but explicit handling produces sharper error messages.
  - **`lib/sessions.js` import: lazy via `require('../sessions')` inside `defaultDetectIdle`** to break the module-load cycle `sessions.js ‚Üí wrap-pipeline.js ‚Üí wrap-steps/ai-content.js ‚Üí sessions.js`. At call time the cycle is fully resolved, so `sessions.detectIdle` is always defined. `lib/tmux.js` has no back-edge to sessions and is eager-required as before.
  - **Two pure helpers exported** for testability: `_interpolatePrompt(promptTemplate, previousResults)` (single-token substitution; unrecognized braces pass through; null prompt ‚Üí empty string; non-`status:'done'` prior memory steps are ignored ‚Äî symmetric with the runner's halt-aware aggregation) and `_parseFields(rawOutput, captureFields)` (returns the `{field: content}` map; mirrors `lib/sessions.js:parseWrapSummary`'s parsing but without the flattened-string return shape, so the handler can validate field-by-field for missing-or-empty cases).
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `ai-content` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining five stubs (`pr-check`, `critic-check`, `priming-roll`, `version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned. The "runs all stubs end-to-end" runner-skeleton test now monkey-patches `lint`/`test`/`ai-content` to no-ops inside the test body (with `finally`-block restore) so the test continues to validate the runner's iteration + aggregation contract without re-implementing tmux state in the harness.
  - **Tests** (+20): 5 cases for `_interpolatePrompt` (token substitution; missing prior step ‚Üí empty; unrecognized braces pass through; null prompt; non-`done` prior step ignored), 5 for `_parseFields` (case-insensitive matching; absent captureFields; empty rawOutput; non-matching headings skipped; multi-field parse), 10 for the handler (missing session blocks, missing prompt blocks, happy path no-captureFields, short-response no-captureFields blocks, captureFields-all-present succeeds with staged output, missing-or-empty captureFields surfaces per-field blockers, `{previousMemoryBlock}` interpolation snapshot, idle timeout via `Date.now` monkey-patch, `sendKeys` throws ‚Üí blocker, `detectIdle` throws ‚Üí blocker, `capturePane` throws ‚Üí blocker). Full suite: 2021 / 2021 pass.

- **Wrap pipeline `lint` + `test` step real handlers (#139, Chunk 4)** ‚Äî third implementation chunk. Replaces the Chunk 3 no-op stubs at `lib/wrap-steps/test.js` and `lib/wrap-steps/lint.js` with real server-side handlers that shell out to the project's configured commands and surface exit-code + tailed stderr/stdout. `lib/wrap-pipeline.js` extends to (a) thread caller-supplied `options` into each step's `context` so handlers can read overrides like `skipTests`, and (b) honor `blocker: "errors-only"` as a halt condition (was `"errors-only resolved inside the handler"` in Chunk 3 ‚Äî collapsed the contradiction with the build plan's "blocks on lint errors but not warnings" wording). Default opt-in remains `projConfig.wrapV2: false`, so this chunk produces zero behavior change on any existing project ‚Äî only sessions explicitly opting in see the real handlers fire.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/test.js`**: reads `projConfig.testCommand`; `null` ‚Üí `{status:'skipped', output:{reason:'no testCommand configured'}}`. With `step.allowOverride === true` AND `options.skipTests === true` ‚Üí `{status:'skipped', output:{override:true,reason:‚Ä¶}}` and the command never runs (Chunk 9's `commit` step will record the override in the wrap commit body). Otherwise shells out via the internal `_internal.execShell` (10-min timeout, 10 MiB buffer cap); exit 0 ‚Üí `{ok:true, status:'done', output:{exitCode:0}}`; exit ‚âÝ 0 ‚Üí `{ok:false, status:'blocked', blockers:['Tests failed (exit N)', last-50-lines of stderr-or-stdout]}`. Timeouts surface as exit code 124. The `_internal` object is exported so tests can override `execShell` without spawning real processes (matches the Chunk 3 `STEP_DISPATCH` monkey-patch idiom).
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/lint.js`**: reads `projConfig.lintCommand`; `null` ‚Üí skipped. Computes "in-session" file set via `_internal.detectChangedFiles(cwd)` (parses `git status --porcelain` ‚Äî staged + unstaged + untracked-but-tracked, deletes excluded, rename arrows resolved to destination, porcelain-quoted paths unquoted). Empty file set ‚Üí skipped with `output.reason: 'no in-session changes to lint'`. Otherwise builds `<lintCommand> -- <quoted-files‚Ä¶>` ‚Äî the `--` POSIX end-of-options separator prevents a git-legal filename starting with `-` (e.g. `-rf.js`) from being interpreted as a flag by the lint binary (Critic-MINOR-1); each file is then single-quote-escaped via the standard `'\''` close-reopen idiom (exposed as `_shellQuote`, unit-pinned against filenames with spaces and embedded single quotes) and the whole string is handed to `exec`. Blocker semantics: `blocker:"errors-only"` (or `true`) + exit ‚âÝ 0 ‚Üí `{ok:false, status:'blocked'}`; `blocker:false` + exit ‚âÝ 0 ‚Üí `{ok:true, status:'done', output.warnings: tail}` (informational only ‚Äî pipeline continues). Chunk 9 will widen the in-session scope to "since last wrap commit" once the `commit` step starts stamping `lastWrapSha` on project records.
  - **`lib/wrap-pipeline.js:_buildStepContext`** now accepts and forwards `options` from `runWrapPipeline(name, options)` into the step context's new `context.options` field. Defaults to `{}` (handlers can read `context.options.skipTests` etc without guarding against undefined). Block-condition broadened from `step.blocker === true` to `step.blocker === true || step.blocker === "errors-only"` ‚Äî the runner now halts on either form when the handler returns `!ok`. JSDoc updated to document the broader contract; the previous "enum-style blockers resolved inside the handler" wording was load-bearing in Chunk 3's no-op world but contradicted #139's pipeline-blocking requirement once real handlers landed. **ADR 0002** updated in this PR (Status line, Runner contract section, Migration-path Chunk 4 entry) to reflect the broadened halt condition (Critic-MAJOR-1).
  - **Stub-conformance test** (`test/wrap-pipeline.test.js`): `lint` and `test` removed from the Chunk-3 canonical-no-op assertion loop; remaining six stubs (`pr-check`, `critic-check`, `ai-content`, `priming-roll`, `version-bump`, `commit`) still pinned to the canonical shape so a half-inlined implementation on any of them fails this test.
  - **Tests** (+18): six per-handler `test` cases (no command ‚Üí skipped; passing ‚Üí done with exitCode 0; failing ‚Üí blocked with stderr tail; allowOverride+skipTests ‚Üí skipped with override flag; skipTests without allowOverride ‚Üí still runs; shell command observed exactly), seven `lint` cases (no command ‚Üí skipped; no in-session files ‚Üí skipped; `errors-only` + exit 1 ‚Üí blocked with file count and shell-quoting verified; `errors-only` + exit 0 ‚Üí done with warnings surfaced; `blocker:false` + exit 1 ‚Üí informational ok:true; `_shellQuote` unit test against `simple.js` / `with space.js` / `it's.js`; real-git integration against a throwaway repo that exercises the actual `git status --porcelain` parser end-to-end). Two runner-level `"errors-only"` block-condition tests (halts on `!ok`; ignores unrecognized enum values). Two `options`-threading tests (forwards through `context.options`; defaults to `{}` when caller omits options). Full suite: 2001 tests pass.

- **Wrap pipeline runner skeleton + `projConfig.wrapV2` opt-in (#139, Chunk 3)** ‚Äî second implementation chunk. Ships the server-side pipeline runner (`lib/wrap-pipeline.js:runWrapPipeline`), the eight per-kind step modules under `lib/wrap-steps/`, and the opt-in flag that routes `lib/sessions.js:triggerWrap` to the new path when `projConfig.wrapV2 === true`. Default is `false` through Chunk 10 ‚Äî every existing wrap continues on the legacy NL-prompt path byte-equal to pre-#139 behavior (regression-pinned in `test/sessions.test.js`). Chunk 11 will flip the default.
  - **`lib/wrap-pipeline.js`** (NEW, ~190 lines): the runner. Reads `wrap_pipeline.steps[]` from the methodology template, dispatches each step by `kind` to a handler module via `STEP_DISPATCH`, threads a single-transaction `runState` (`results` + `staged` scratch space ‚Äî only the `commit` step in Chunk 9 will flush `staged` to git), and returns `{ok, blockedAt, results:[{stepId, kind, status, output, blockers}], commitSha:null, summary:null, error:null}`. Block-true semantics: a step declared `blocker: true` whose handler returns `!ok` halts the pipeline immediately, and every subsequent step is reported as `'pending'` so the Chunk 10 UI can render where the pipeline froze. Enum-style blockers (e.g. `"errors-only"`) stay inside handlers ‚Äî the runner only knows boolean. Unknown step kinds skip (forward-compat with future bundled changes); thrown handler errors are caught and surfaced as `blockers[]` entries on a synthesized `'blocked'` result.
  - **`lib/wrap-steps/`** (NEW subdir): eight files ‚Äî `pr-check.js`, `lint.js`, `test.js`, `critic-check.js`, `ai-content.js`, `priming-roll.js`, `version-bump.js`, `commit.js`. Each exports `async function run(context)` returning the canonical no-op `{ok:true, status:'done', output:null, blockers:[]}` and JSDoc'd with the future-chunk contract. Real implementations land in Chunks 4‚Äì9.
  - **`lib/store.js:DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG`**: three new fields ‚Äî `wrapV2: false` (the opt-in flag), `testCommand: null`, `lintCommand: null` (explicit declarations the `test` and `lint` step kinds will shell out to in Chunk 4; auto-detection is rejected as a monorepo-class footgun).
  - **`lib/sessions.js:triggerWrap`**: now `async`. Reads `projConfig.wrapV2` from `store.projectConfig.load(project.path)`; on `true` delegates to the new `_triggerWrapV2` helper (invokes the runner, returns the canonical wrap shape + a `pipelineResult` field carrying the runner's structured output, does NOT send any tmux command since the runner is server-side). On `false` (default) the legacy NL-prompt path runs unchanged. All callers updated to `await`: `server.js:POST /api/sessions/:project/wrap` and existing `test/sessions.test.js` cases.
  - **ADR 0002** updated with a Chunk 3 status line noting the runner skeleton landed behind the flag.
  - **Tests** (+22): `test/wrap-pipeline.test.js` (NEW) ‚Äî dispatch-table covers every contract kind; dispatch covers every kind referenced by bundled prawduct + minimal templates; runner runs all stubs end-to-end and returns ok:true; preserves step ID order; attaches `kind` to each result; preflight errors (unknown project, missing `wrap_pipeline`); block-true halts and marks subsequent steps `pending`; blocker:false `!ok` does NOT halt; thrown handler error surfaces as blocker; unknown-kind skips without dispatch; each of the eight step stubs pinned to the canonical no-op shape. `test/sessions.test.js` ‚Äî V2-opt-in test (no tmux command sent, pipelineResult attached) + V2:false byte-equal regression pin against the Chunk 2 NL prompt.

- **Wrap pipeline schema migration + back-compat shim (#139, Chunk 2)** ‚Äî first implementation chunk of the methodology-aware single-button session wrap. Replaces the legacy `wrap: {command, steps, captureFields}` block in bundled methodology templates with a typed `wrap_pipeline: {schemaVersion, promptTemplates, steps[]}` schema. Each step is an `{id, kind, ...}` object that the runner (Chunk 3+) will dispatch via a typed dispatch table ‚Äî kinds enumerated in ADR 0002. Bundled methodology templates migrated: `prawduct` (6 steps) and `minimal` (3 steps); the gitignored `tilt` template migrates symmetrically when present locally. No runtime behavior change in this chunk: `lib/sessions.js:triggerWrap` continues to fabricate the legacy NL prompt byte-equal to pre-migration via a back-compat shim.
  - **`lib/skills.js`**: new exported helper `wrapShapeFromTemplate(template)` synthesizes the legacy `{command, steps, captureFields}` shape from either schema. When `wrap_pipeline` is present, `steps` is the ordered list of `pipeline.steps[].id`, `captureFields` is the flattened deduplicated union of every step's `captureFields[]`, and `command` is `null` (custom overrides will move to `promptTemplates.<engine>` once the runner honors them in later chunks). Falls back to the legacy `wrap` block verbatim for installs that haven't yet picked up the new bundled schema. `getWrapSkill` is a thin wrapper over `wrapShapeFromTemplate(store.templates.get(id))` ‚Äî the helper is the single read-point so callers can't drift into asymmetric reads of the two schemas (ADR 0001).
  - **`lib/eval-audit.js:scoreWrapQuality`** routes through the new shim instead of reading `methodology.wrap.steps` directly. Both `triggerWrap` and `scoreWrapQuality` now answer "what are the wrap steps?" through the same predicate ‚Äî symmetric capability gates per ADR 0001.
  - **`lib/store.js:ARRAY_RECONCILERS`** gains `wrap_pipeline.steps` with `mergeBy:id` policy (the #155 Chunk 2 reconciler) so new bundled steps with a new `id` value propagate additively to live runtime templates on init. Legacy `wrap.steps` and `wrap.captureFields` entries remain in the table as inert safety nets during the migration window ‚Äî bundled templates no longer ship those paths, so the policy short-circuits on missing bundled arrays, leaving any legacy `wrap` blocks on live templates untouched.
  - **ADR 0002 ‚Äî Wrap Pipeline Contract** (`docs/adr/0002-wrap-pipeline-contract.md`) documents the schema, the step-kind dispatch table, the runner contract (`runWrapPipeline` signature, step return shape, single-transaction semantics), the back-compat shim semantics, the reconciler choice, and the phased Chunks 3 ‚Üí 11 rollout via `projConfig.wrapV2`. ADR 0001 updated to cross-link to ADR 0002 as an instance of the "one read predicate per conceptual state" rule.
  - **Tests**: +6 in `test/skills.test.js` (byte-equal legacy shape for all three migrated templates pinning behavior preservation; `wrap_pipeline` ‚Üí legacy synthesis with captureFields union; legacy fallback; `wrap_pipeline` preferred when both present; null/empty input handling; defensive skip of malformed entries), +5 in `test/store.test.js` (`wrap_pipeline.steps` mergeBy:id append; user-added step preserved; field-overwrite forbidden on matched entries; user-removed re-add limitation pin per ADR 0001; inert-legacy-reconciler safety-net behavior when bundled drops the `wrap` block), +1 in `test/eval-audit.test.js` (`scoreWrapQuality` works against a `wrap_pipeline`-shaped methodology object ‚Äî proves the shim routing). The #136 init-glue integration test in `test/store.test.js` updated for the new world: legacy `wrap` block on live is preserved untouched while `wrap_pipeline` is propagated from bundled.
  - **Scope discipline**: this chunk lands schema + shim + reconciler + ADR only. No runner, no step kinds, no UI, no `wrapV2` opt-in flag ‚Äî those are Chunks 3‚Äì11. The legacy NL-prompt code in `triggerWrap` is unchanged; `triggerWrap` continues to fabricate the exact same prompt it did before this PR via the shim. Out-of-scope items pinned in ADR 0002: auto-Critic-dispatch, tombstone-based step removal, branch-protection push flow, methodology authoring UX, per-step retry. The self-deleting bridging auto-memory `project-issue-139-methodology-wrap.md` continues to point at the build plan; deletion is gated on #139 closing.

- **Template-array reconciliation extends to object-keyed arrays (#155, Chunk 2)** ‚Äî `lib/store.js:ARRAY_RECONCILERS` policy table grows to nine paths total. Chunk 2 adds the `_reconcileMergeBy(live, bundled, idKey)` policy and wires five previously-drifting object-keyed arrays through it: `phases` (idKey=`id`), `evalDimensions.tier1`, `evalDimensions.tier2`, `evalDimensions.tier3` (idKey=`id`), and `actions` (idKey=`label` ‚Äî prawduct's `actions` entries don't have an `id` field, the `label` field is the natural identifier). The policy matches by string equality on `entry[idKey]` and appends bundled entries whose key value is absent from live; matched entries are left untouched (additive only, never overwrites). Appended entries are deep-cloned so in-process reuse of the same bundled object across multiple live targets cannot leak mutations.
  - **ADR 0001 extended**: new section "Generalized template-array reconciliation (#155 extension)" documents the full pattern (table + policies + driver), the three policies' behavior at-a-glance, and the user-removed-entry acknowledged limitation that's symmetric across `orderedSubsetReplace` and `mergeBy`. A new rule in the ADR captures the operational follow-through: when adding a new array to any bundled template, add a one-line `ARRAY_RECONCILERS` entry in the same PR ‚Äî the cost of forgetting it is exactly the incident-then-patch cycle #119, #136, and #158 each paid.
  - **Driver change**: the inner loop in `_mergeBundledTemplate` now passes `entry.idKey` to the reconciler, allowing each path to declare its own identifier field. Log payload simplified from per-entry `added` list (only meaningful for primitive arrays) to `addedCount` (works uniformly across string and object arrays).
  - **Acknowledged limitation (re-add on user-removed entry)**: symmetric with `_reconcileOrderedSubset`. `_reconcileMergeBy` cannot distinguish "user removed entry X" from "user is on an older bundled version that never had entry X" ‚Äî both produce a live whose id-set is a subset of bundled's. The policy choice is to re-add, documented in the reconciler's JSDoc and pinned by a regression test (`treats user-removed object-keyed entry as stale and re-adds it`). Tombstones would solve it but are out of scope for #155.
  - **Tests**: +22 in `test/store.test.js` ‚Äî 13 unit tests on `_reconcileMergeBy` (additive append; live order preserved; null when in sync; user-added preserved; field-overwrite forbidden on matched entries; deep-clones appended entries; empty live ‚Üí bundled copy; empty bundled ‚Üí null; non-array inputs ‚Üí null; missing/empty idKey ‚Üí null; non-`id` key names supported via `'label'`; bundled entries without idKey skipped; bundled internal duplicates protected) + 9 integration tests on `_mergeBundledTemplate` (phases append by id; phases user-added preserved; phases field-overwrite forbidden; evalDimensions.tier1 append by id; actions append by label; deep-clone integration; multi-path single-pass spanning string and object arrays; no-op mtime pin; user-removed re-add limitation pin). The Chunk 1 phases-untouched pin is replaced with a generalized "unregistered path stays alone" pin (`customCategory.items` ‚Äî outside the table, must not be reconciled). All 1927 prior tests continue to pass ‚Äî 1949 total.

- **Template-array reconciliation generalized beyond `wrap.steps` (#155, Chunk 1)** ‚Äî `lib/store.js:_mergeBundledTemplate` now drives plain-array reconciliation through a declarative policy table (`ARRAY_RECONCILERS`) instead of hardcoding `wrap.steps`. Three previously-drifting paths join the table in this chunk: `prime.sections` (orderedSubsetReplace, same policy as wrap.steps), `wrap.captureFields` (setUnion, additive set merge), and `init.directories` (setUnion). Adding a newly-tracked array path is now a one-line registry entry ‚Äî no driver change. The original wrap.steps inline code from #136 migrates into the same table-driven loop; all existing wrap.steps tests pass unchanged, proving the refactor is behavior-preserving.
  - **New pure functions**: `_reconcileOrderedSubset(live, bundled)` (extracted from the original #136 inline logic) and `_reconcileSetUnion(live, bundled)` (new). Both return a new array OR `null` meaning "leave alone" ‚Äî uniform shape lets the driver dispatch identically across every policy. `_getAtPath(obj, dotPath)` resolves nested array references for both bundled and live sides.
  - **Policy choices**: `setUnion` preserves `live`'s element order at the front and appends bundled-only entries at the end in bundled-iteration order. `orderedSubsetReplace` carries forward the #136 acknowledged limitation verbatim ‚Äî a user-removed entry that leaves the array as a strict subset of bundled is indistinguishable from "user is on an older version missing that entry", and is treated as stale-older (re-added). This policy now applies uniformly to `wrap.steps` AND `prime.sections`; if either ever needs different semantics, the table makes the wiring split explicit.
  - **Scope discipline**: `hooks.<engine>.<event>[]` continues to flow through `_mergeBundledHookEntries` (#158) ‚Äî match-by-matcher semantics don't fit the plain-array driver and the existing hook-entry path is unchanged. Object-id-keyed arrays (`phases`, `evalDimensions.tier1/tier2/tier3`, `actions`) are explicitly NOT in the table ‚Äî they're deferred to Chunk 2 along with `_reconcileMergeById` and the ADR 0001 update documenting the full generalized pattern. A pinning test asserts the Chunk 1 driver leaves `phases` alone even when drifted, locking the scope boundary against future drift.
  - **Tests**: 22 new in `test/store.test.js` ‚Äî 6 for `_reconcileOrderedSubset` (subset ‚Üí returns bundled copy; identical ‚Üí null; user-customized ‚Üí null; reordered ‚Üí null; non-array inputs ‚Üí null; result is not the bundled reference), 8 for `_reconcileSetUnion` (appends bundled-only entries in order; preserves live order at front; null when live is superset; preserves user-added entries; empty live returns bundled copy; empty bundled returns null; non-array inputs ‚Üí null; no duplication when bundled has repeats live already covers), 8 integration in the existing `_mergeBundledTemplate (#136)` block (prime.sections subset reconcile; prime.sections user customization preserved; wrap.captureFields additive merge; wrap.captureFields user-added preserved with bundled appended; init.directories additive merge; no-op when every array is in sync ‚Äî pinned via mtime; multi-array reconcile in single pass; pinning test that `phases` stays untouched in Chunk 1). All 1927 prior tests still pass (was 1905 pre-chunk).

- **CHANGELOG.md structural-invariants test (#168)** ‚Äî `test/changelog-structure.test.js` asserts four structural invariants on `CHANGELOG.md`: every release banner (`> üõü` / `> üöÄ`) is inside a `## [X.Y.Z] - YYYY-MM-DD` section (catches the PR #166-class regression where a heading was silently consumed); released-version headings appear in descending semver order (catches cherry-pick / backport misorderings); no released-version heading appears twice (catches bad merge resolutions); the top released-version heading agrees with `version.json` (the load-bearing invariant ‚Äî would have caught PR #166 directly, where the cache self-heal then propagated `3.16.0` to dashboards on every install). Invariant detectors are factored as pure functions so a second describe block exercises them against a synthesized post-#166 / pre-#167 file shape, proving the regression is detected. ~180 lines, 9 tests, runs in < 40ms inside the standard `node --test 'test/*.test.js'` sweep ‚Äî no new tooling. Structural-only; lints body content of release entries is intentionally out of scope (style / completeness remains Critic territory).

## [3.16.2] - 2026-05-13

> üõü **Recommended bug-fix release.** Two patch-class fixes since v3.16.1: **ttyd-watcher actually fires on macOS** (#144) ‚Äî closes a 6+-month silent regression where the watcher's `pgrep -c` proxy exited 2 on every BSD invocation, leaving #94's session-killing PTY-exhaustion bug unprotected since #95 merged; users had been manually `launchctl kickstart`-ing ttyd on every incident. The replacement measures `kern.tty.ptmx_max` vs `/dev/ttys*` directly and trips at 85% pool saturation. **Dashboard project-version label self-heals on enrichment** (#165) ‚Äî closes the stale-label gap where external version bumps (release-PR merges, manual `version.json` edits) didn't reach the dashboard until the next TC-managed session launch or wrap on the same project. Anyone on v3.16.1 will get the update-pill notification with a clickable link to this release page.

### Fixed

- **ttyd-watcher now actually fires on macOS ‚Äî measures PTY pool, not broken `pgrep -c` proxy (#144)** ‚Äî `lib/ttyd-watcher.js` shipped in PR #95 to auto-recover from #94's session-killing PTY-exhaustion bug. It has been a silent no-op on every macOS install since merge. `_countTtydChildren` invoked `pgrep -c -P <pid>` ‚Äî but BSD `pgrep` (`/usr/bin/pgrep` on macOS) has no `-c` flag and exits 2 with `illegal option -- c`. The catch only special-cased `err.status === 1` (no matches), so exit 2 fell through to a `pgrep failed` warn that has been logged every 5 minutes since at least 2026-05-02. The kickstart never fired; users have been manually running `launchctl kickstart -k gui/$UID/com.tangleclaw.ttyd` to recover from every incident. The PR #95 unit tests stubbed the runner via `_setRunner`, so the production code path against real BSD `pgrep` was never exercised by CI ‚Äî three defects compounded into a silent regression that took 6+ months to surface.
  - **`lib/ttyd-watcher.js:_isPtyPoolExhausted(thresholdRatio)`** ‚Äî new function replacing `_countTtydChildren`. Measures the actual exhausted resource: `sysctl -n kern.tty.ptmx_max` (cap) vs `sh -c 'ls /dev/ttys* 2>/dev/null | wc -l'` (used). Returns `{ exhausted, used, cap, ratio }`. The pool measurement counts both live and zombie PTY-holding processes because it asks the kernel rather than introspecting a process tree ‚Äî closing the second compounding defect (BSD `pgrep` filters out zombies). Fail-safe: any non-numeric reading, throwing binary, or `cap <= 0` returns `{ exhausted: false, used: 0, cap: 0, ratio: 0 }` and the watcher never kickstarts on a failed measurement.
  - **`lib/ttyd-watcher.js:_countTtydZombies(pid)`** ‚Äî new diagnostic-only function using `ps -A -o ppid=,stat=` (which unlike BSD `pgrep` DOES include zombies). Counts rows where `ppid == pid` AND `stat` contains `Z`. **Never gates the kickstart decision** ‚Äî captured purely for diagnostic logging so production logs on the next incident carry the data that answers "how many zombie children did ttyd have when we kickstarted?" with a grep rather than a guess. Returns 0 on any error.
  - **`lib/ttyd-watcher.js:_check`** ‚Äî rewired to gate kickstart on `_isPtyPoolExhausted` (pool-only, per the #144 issue body's explicit proposal). Trigger log line moves from `'ttyd child count above threshold, kickstarting'` to `'ttyd PTY pool exhausted, kickstarting'` and carries `{ ttydLabel, pid, used, cap, ratio, zombies, threshold }`. The below-threshold debug log carries the same fields so verbose operators can watch the pool fill over time. Zombie count is included in both log lines as diagnostic-only data.
  - **API change**: `DEFAULT_THRESHOLD = 50` (child count) ‚Üí `DEFAULT_PTY_THRESHOLD = 0.85` (pool ratio). `_check` opt `threshold` ‚Üí `ptyThresholdRatio`. `start()` opt `threshold` ‚Üí `ptyThresholdRatio`. Only caller in the repo (`server.js:3123`) invokes `start()` with no options, so the rename is fully internal.
  - **Design call: pool-only gate (not hybrid pool+zombies AND gate)**. The issue body explicitly proposed pool-only ("trip kickstart when used/cap crosses ~0.85"). Simpler. If unrelated PTY saturation produces false-positive kickstarts in practice (no observed case yet), can add a hybrid gate as a follow-up ‚Äî easier to add a gate later than to remove one. A test pins the policy: pool exhaustion alone triggers kickstart even when zombie count is 0.
  - **Production-runner smoke test (closes the test gap that hid this bug for 6+ months)** ‚Äî `describe('production runner smoke test (darwin only)')` block calling `_isPtyPoolExhausted(0.85)` AND `_countTtydZombies(1)` against the real host shell (no `_setRunner` patch). Gated on `process.platform === 'darwin'`. Asserts both functions return finite values without throwing. Pre-#144 the entire watcher was tested only against a stubbed runner; the same regression class ‚Äî a wrong-flag invocation that silently fails on macOS ‚Äî would slip through CI again without this. Closes the issue's "Test gap to close" requirement.
  - **Tests**: -3 in `test/ttyd-watcher.test.js` (`_countTtydChildren` describe block removed ‚Äî function gone). +9 (`_isPtyPoolExhausted`: trips at threshold; trips at canonical #94 incident shape used=527 cap=511; doesn't trip below threshold; doesn't trip at floor-1 (off-by-one boundary lock, Critic NIT 1); fail-safe on non-numeric sysctl; fail-safe on sysctl throw; fail-safe on ls/wc throw; fail-safe on cap‚â§0; uses DEFAULT_PTY_THRESHOLD when no arg). +6 (`_countTtydZombies`: counts only ppid-match AND Z-stat rows; returns 0 when no rows match parent; returns 0 when all matching rows are live; fail-safe on ps error; empty ps output; skips malformed rows). +2 `_check` tests (still kickstarts when zombies=0 ‚Äî pins the pool-only design call; doesn't kickstart on fail-safe measurement and short-circuits to the new measurement-failed warn ‚Äî Critic MINOR 1). +2 production-runner smoke (darwin-gated). 1896 total passing (was 1880).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 0 MAJORs / 2 MINORs / 4 NITs. MINORs + 3 NITs addressed in-chunk. **M1** (fail-safe `{ cap: 0 }` fell through to the "PTY pool ok" debug log so operators grepping `ratio: 0.000` couldn't distinguish "pool empty" from "measurement broken") ‚Äî `_check` now branches early on `cap === 0`, emits a `warn` with `'ttyd PTY pool measurement failed (fail-safe ‚Äî no kickstart)'` carrying `{ ttydLabel, pid, zombies, threshold }`. New regression test asserts the branch is reachable from a thrown sysctl and that no kickstart fires. **M2** (CHANGELOG test-count off by one ‚Äî enumeration listed 8 `_isPtyPoolExhausted` tests but the count said `+7`) ‚Äî corrected to `+9` after also adding the boundary-lock test from NIT 1; total now sums correctly at 1896. **N1** (boundary lock missing) ‚Äî added a `used = floor(cap*threshold) - 1` test asserting `exhausted === false` to pin the `>=` vs `>` predicate from drifting in either direction; pairs with the existing `used = floor(cap*threshold)` trip test. **N2** (test body had six lines of working-out-loud commentary about macOS ps STAT codes) ‚Äî collapsed to a one-line `// Expected: rows 3 and 4 match. Others either lack Z or wrong ppid.` comment. **N4** (JSDoc on `_check`'s `ptyThresholdRatio` typed as bare `number` and could mislead a future caller into passing `85` instead of `0.85`) ‚Äî added `/* 0..1 fraction, not percent */` inline comment to the type signature; pulled the better wording in `start()`'s JSDoc through. NIT 3 (whether to keep the unconditional `ps -A` per tick ‚Äî Critic recommended keeping it for diagnostic continuity) accepted as-is; the measurement is microseconds and the symmetric log payload across exhausted/ok branches is more valuable than the saved cycle.
  - **Backwards compatibility**: TC restart picks up the new watcher behavior on launch. The watcher remains macOS-only (Linux installs are unaffected ‚Äî `start()` short-circuits in the existing platform guard). No data migrations.

- **Dashboard project-version label self-heals on enrichment (#165)** ‚Äî The project-version label shown in the dashboard project list (e.g. `TangleClaw-v3 v3.X.Y`) is sourced from each project's `.tangleclaw/project-version.txt` cache file via `lib/projects.js:_detectProjectVersion`. Pre-#165 the cache file was only rewritten by `lib/project-version.js:recordVersion`, which is called from two narrow triggers ‚Äî session launch (`lib/sessions.js:145`) and session wrap (`lib/sessions.js:765`). When a project's on-disk version source changed outside of a TC-managed session (release-PR merge via `gh`, external `git pull`, manual edit of `version.json`), the cache stayed stale and the dashboard kept rendering the pre-bump number until the next launch/wrap. Manifested live on 2026-05-13 when cutting v3.16.1: the TC-v3 project's `version.json` and `CHANGELOG.md` both reflected the new version, but the dashboard label still read `v3.14.0` because no TC-managed session had launched on the TC-v3 project itself since 2026-05-05.
  - **`lib/projects.js:_detectProjectVersion`** ‚Äî semantic inversion. Pre-#165 the cache was the highest-priority source and a divergent on-disk source never reached the label. Post-#165 the function reads both the cached value AND the live chain (CHANGELOG.md ‚Üí version.json ‚Üí package.json) on every call; if live is present and differs from cached, it rewrites the cache with the live value + correct source label and returns live. Live's absence (no source files match) preserves the cached value ‚Äî this is load-bearing for git-tag-derived caches that `lib/project-version.js:recordVersion` may have written via its richer detection chain, which `lib/projects.js`'s live readers can't reproduce.
  - **`lib/projects.js:_detectLiveVersion`** ‚Äî new helper exposing the live half of the detection chain as `{ version, source } | null`. Separated from `_detectProjectVersion` so the self-heal write can label the source correctly (`'CHANGELOG.md'`, `'version.json'`, `'package.json'`) rather than re-detecting source post-facto.
  - **`lib/projects.js:_writeVersionCacheFile`** ‚Äî new helper mirroring `lib/project-version.js:_formatCacheFile`'s output byte-for-byte (`version: ‚Ä¶\nrecorded_at: ‚Ä¶\nsource: ‚Ä¶\n` with ISO-without-ms recorded_at). Write is best-effort via try/catch; logs at warn on failure but returns silently so enrichment never crashes on a read-only filesystem or permission-denied `.tangleclaw/`. Creates `.tangleclaw/` if missing.
  - **Why the write helper lives in `lib/projects.js` rather than calling `projectVersion.recordVersion`**: `lib/project-version.js` already requires `lib/projects.js` for its own readers (`_readChangelogVersion` etc.). A back-require would close a cycle. The cache file format is plain text and stable across the codebase; duplicating the four-line write is cheaper than reorganizing the module graph.
  - **Cost**: every enrichment call now does up to ~3 extra small text-file reads (CHANGELOG.md / version.json / package.json) when the cache is present. Previously the chain short-circuited on cache hit. Filesystem-cache-warm reads are sub-millisecond; no measurable dashboard-refresh slowdown.
  - **Tests**: 1 inverted in `test/projects.test.js` (`layer 1: live source overrides stale cache and self-heals` ‚Äî was the pre-#165 `cache file should win over CHANGELOG, version.json, and package.json` test, asserting `1.0.0-from-cache`; now asserts `2.0.0-from-changelog`). 9 new in a dedicated `describe('_detectProjectVersion self-heal (#165)')` block: rewrites on version.json mismatch (asserts cache file contents + source label + recorded_at shape); rewrites on CHANGELOG mismatch (verifies live-chain priority ‚Äî CHANGELOG over version.json); steady-state byte-equal preservation (no rewrite when cache matches live, filesystem-agnostic); cache preservation when no live source (git-tag-derived caches survive); read-only-directory fail-open (chmod 0o500 forces write failure, function still returns live value); creates `.tangleclaw/` if missing; non-existent path returns null without throwing; `_detectLiveVersion` returns null when no live source; `_detectLiveVersion` source labels match the reader that hit (CHANGELOG / version.json / package.json). 1880 total passing (was 1871).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 1 MAJOR / 3 MINORs / 2 NITs. MAJOR + 2 MINORs addressed in-chunk. **M1** (fail-open test passed for the wrong reason) ‚Äî original test seeded an existing cache file then `chmod 0o500`'d the directory, but POSIX `O_WRONLY|O_TRUNC` on an *existing* file succeeds inside a r-o directory (the test silently exercised the success path, not the catch block). Rewrote the test to stub `fs.writeFileSync` so it throws unconditionally; added positive assertions that the stub was invoked exactly once AND that no cache file was created. The stub-based approach is also cross-platform robust (chmod-based fail-open tests no-op when run as root). **N1** (`_readVersionCacheFile` JSDoc was doubly stale) ‚Äî comment still referenced "AI on session start and wrap once the session-lifecycle hook lands in #55 chunks 2+" from before #101 made TC the writer. Refreshed to document both current TC-side writers (`lib/project-version.js:recordVersion` for the rich chain incl. git-tag, `lib/projects.js:_writeVersionCacheFile` for the #165 self-heal). **N2** (preserve-cached-when-live-null trade-off not documented in-code) ‚Äî added a sentence to `_detectProjectVersion`'s JSDoc explaining the accepted trade-off: a project whose only live source was deleted will keep showing the pre-deletion value until the next session launch's `recordVersion` rewrites the cache with `source: fallback`. The alternative (clobber on null) would regress git-tag-only projects on every enrichment, which is worse. N3 (test pollution risk from chmod permission failures) accepted as-is ‚Äî N1 fix removed the chmod entirely, so the concern no longer applies. NITs (CHANGELOG count framing, duplicated JSDoc rationale) accepted as-is.

## [3.16.1] - 2026-05-13


> üõü **Recommended bug-fix release.** Three OpenClaw / methodology-hook fixes since v3.16.0: **chunk-1 orphan-hook protection now reaches pre-#146 runtime templates** (#158) ‚Äî closes the session-killing infinite Stop-hook loop that resurfaced on TC-v3 itself when chunk-1's `requires` filter silently no-op'd on pre-v3.15.0 runtime templates; **OpenClaw connection flow fixes** (#160) ‚Äî surfaces real save errors, fixes Bridge Port silently defaulting to 3201 for non-ClawBridge deployments, and replaces the generic "check SSH connectivity" message with the actual SSH failure (local-bind conflict, auth failure, network error); **OpenClaw Web UI cached-WS-URL routing fix** (#162) ‚Äî clicking a second OpenClaw connection's Web UI button no longer loads the first connection's dashboard via stale localStorage cache. Anyone on v3.16.0 will get the update-pill notification with a clickable link to this release page.

### Fixed

- **OpenClaw Web UI: clicking a second connection's Web UI button loaded the first connection's dashboard via cached localStorage WS URL (#162)** ‚Äî When TC proxies multiple OpenClaw connections through `/openclaw-direct/<connId>/...` on the same TC origin, the iframe-loaded OpenClaw dashboard caches its derived WebSocket URL in localStorage (e.g. `wss://192.168.10.99:3102/openclaw-direct/<connId>`). Because the dashboard reads localStorage on subsequent loads instead of re-deriving from the iframe URL, the second OpenClaw's Web UI button would silently route WebSocket traffic to the *first* OpenClaw's tunnel. Symptom: clicking Claw-Node-01's Web UI button opens RentalClaw's dashboard. The iframe URL is correct; the dashboard's WebSocket connection is wrong.
  - **Scope honesty (Critic MAJOR-4)**: this fix targets the **observed manifestation** ‚Äî cached values whose string content contains the proxy path `/openclaw-direct/<otherId>/`. The TC parent page can detect and remove those entries before the iframe loads. If a future OpenClaw dashboard caches its WS URL under a key whose value contains no proxy-path substring (e.g. origin-only `wss://host:port` or a structured `{host,port}` JSON), the fix as shipped does NOT clear it and the bug recurs. That broader case is acknowledged-out-of-scope here; would file as a #162-followup needing either a TC-side proxy HTML injection or a coordinated change with OpenClaw upstream.
  - **Fix in `public/openclaw-cache.js`** ‚Äî new helper module `tcClearStaleOpenclawCache(connId, storage)`. Walks `localStorage`, uses `matchAll` to extract every `/openclaw-direct/<id>` reference inside each value, and deletes the entry only when EVERY reference is for a different (case-insensitive) connId than the current one. Composite values that reference both the current connection AND a stale one are PRESERVED ‚Äî the dashboard's legitimate current-connection state shouldn't be lost just because the value also mentions an old id. Loaded via a new `<script src="/openclaw-cache.js">` tag in `openclaw-view.html` (positioned between `api-helper.js` and `openclaw-view.js` so the helper is defined before `openclaw-view.js`'s `init()` calls it). Uses the same UMD-ish factory pattern as `api-helper.js` ‚Äî exposes on `window` for the browser and `module.exports` for tests.
  - **Wiring in `public/openclaw-view.js`** ‚Äî new `setFrameSrc(frame, url)` helper is the only writer of `terminalFrame.src` in the file; it runs `tcClearStaleOpenclawCache(connId)` then sets `frame.src`. Both writer sites (`init()` initial load and the post-pairing auto-approve reload) route through this helper, so the cache-bust is symmetric (Critic MINOR-1 + MINOR-2). The iframe is same-origin with the parent (TC proxies under `/openclaw-direct/`), so localStorage is shared ‚Äî clearing entries from the parent makes the dashboard JS running inside the iframe fall through to deriving its URL fresh from the iframe's own `location` (for the in-scope value shape). Call is guarded by `typeof tcClearStaleOpenclawCache === 'function'` so a missing helper script doesn't crash navigation.
  - **Policy decisions**: (a) **Composite-value safety** ‚Äî `matchAll` + "hasStale && !hasCurrent" predicate: only delete when no reference inside the value matches the current connId (Critic MAJOR-2). (b) **Case-insensitive connId comparison** ‚Äî UUIDs are case-insensitive per RFC 4122 ¬ß3; both extraction and comparison are normalized to lowercase so a value emitted with mixed case (uppercase / mixed canonical form) doesn't get misclassified as stale and over-deleted (Critic MAJOR-3). (c) Only entries whose VALUES reference `/openclaw-direct/<otherId>/` are touched ‚Äî TC's own per-project settings under `tc_<project>_<key>` and other unrelated keys are preserved.
