(d) Same-connection cache is preserved (the dashboard's prior session state survives navigation away and back, including across case differences). (e) Idempotent ‚Äî calling twice with the same connId does nothing the second time. (f) Storage walk goes BACKWARDS so live mutation via `removeItem` doesn't skip keys (regression-tested). (g) Tolerant of incognito/disabled storage ‚Äî wrapped in try/catch, returns 0 on any thrown access. (h) Defensive against missing/empty/malformed `currentConnId` ‚Äî UUID-shape validation (`/^[0-9a-fA-F-]{16,64}$/`) means an accidental empty/typo input returns 0 without touching storage (Critic MINOR-4).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 3 MAJORs / 4 MINORs / 3 NITs. All MAJORs + actionable MINORs addressed in-chunk. **M2** (composite-value over/under-deletion) ‚Äî original match-first-occurrence semantics could either over-delete (first match stale ‚Üí whole value gone even if it also referenced current) or under-delete (first match current ‚Üí preserves entry even if it referenced an old id elsewhere). Rewrote to `matchAll` + "hasStale && !hasCurrent" predicate; composite values containing the current connId are preserved. **M3** (case-policy backwards) ‚Äî original strict-equality comparison would over-delete legitimate same-connection state if OpenClaw ever emitted a mixed-case UUID. UUIDs are case-insensitive per RFC 4122 ¬ß3; both extraction and comparison are now `.toLowerCase()`-normalized. Test that previously asserted "case difference treated as mismatched" was rewritten to assert the correct "case differences are NOT stale" contract. **M4** (CHANGELOG scope honesty) ‚Äî added a "Scope honesty" sub-bullet acknowledging the fix targets the observed manifestation only; cached values whose strings don't contain the proxy path would need a follow-up issue. **Min1 + Min2** (symmetric clearing) ‚Äî pre-Critic, only the initial `init()` write to `frame.src` cleared the cache; the post-pairing auto-approve reload was an un-cleared direct `frame.src = frame.src`. Extracted a `setFrameSrc(frame, url)` helper that's the only writer of `terminalFrame.src` in the file; both call sites route through it. Wiring test asserts there are NO direct `frame.src` writes outside the helper body. **Min4** (malformed connId) ‚Äî added a UUID-shape regex `/^[0-9a-fA-F-]{16,64}$/` so a malformed input returns 0 without touching storage; regression test pins the contract. NITs (comment length, count-claim verification, CHANGELOG phrasing) accepted or addressed inline.
  - **Tests**: 17 new in `test/openclaw-cache.test.js`. Behavioral coverage against a mock `Storage` shim (13 cases): removes mismatched connId entries; preserves matching connId entries (incl. mixed-case); preserves unrelated entries (TC settings, third-party widgets); handles multiple stale entries in one pass; walks backwards so removeItem-during-iteration doesn't skip; tolerates non-string values; returns 0 on null/throwing storage; refuses to touch anything when `currentConnId` is empty/missing/malformed (UUID-shape validation); composite-value with mixed stale + current refs is preserved; all-stale composite is removed. Source-level structural assertions (4 cases): `openclaw-view.html` loads `openclaw-cache.js` BEFORE `openclaw-view.js`; `setFrameSrc` is the only `frame.src` writer outside its own body; `setFrameSrc` is called from at least 2 sites (init + post-pairing reload); the cache-bust call is guarded by `typeof === 'function'`. 1849 total passing (was 1832 at #161 merge).
  - **Backwards compatibility**: TC's own localStorage entries (per-project session settings, update-pill dismissal state, etc.) all use the `tc_*` prefix and don't carry `/openclaw-direct/` substrings ‚Äî they're untouched by the helper. Users who have only ever opened one OpenClaw connection see no behavior change. Cross-connection users who currently see the bug get the fix on next openclaw-view.html load.

- **OpenClaw connection flow: misleading save errors + Bridge Port silently defaulting to 3201 + tunnel "check SSH connectivity" hiding the real failure (#160)** ‚Äî Three compounding UI/UX bugs that made non-ClawBridge OpenClaw connections (any deployment without a ClawBridge sidecar ‚Äî e.g. a fresh Docker-based OpenClaw on a Linux host) effectively unusable until the user manually PATCHed the record via the REST API. All three closed in one PR.
  - **Bug 1 ‚Äî Save toast now surfaces the real server error.** Pre-#160, the New / Edit Connection modal hardcoded `"Save failed. Name may already exist."` for any non-2xx response. The actual error (PORT_CONFLICT, BAD_REQUEST, CONFLICT, etc.) lived in the JSON response body's `error` + `code` fields but never reached the UI. `public/ui.js:saveConnection` now uses `api.lastError` + `api.lastErrorCode` (the side-channel exposed by `public/api-helper.js` since PR #84 / issue #80) to render the real message. Falls back to the previous generic message only when no error payload was returned (e.g. network failure mid-save). Backend tests pin the contract that PORT_CONFLICT responses carry both `error` (string) and `code: 'PORT_CONFLICT'` so the frontend can disambiguate.
  - **Bug 2 ‚Äî Blank Bridge Port now persists as null.** Pre-#160, an empty Bridge Port field in the modal silently saved as `3201` (the ClawBridge default) for three reasons: (a) `public/ui.js:saveConnection` serialized `parseInt(value, 10) || 3201`; (b) `lib/store.js:openclawConnections.create` ran `const bridgePort = data.bridgePort || 3201;`; (c) `lib/store.js:_rowToConnection` coerced null read-back to 3201. Every non-ClawBridge connection carried 3201 in its DB row, which then drove server.js to ask `lib/tunnel.js` for a `-L 3201:127.0.0.1:3201` SSH forward ‚Äî and with `-o ExitOnForwardFailure=yes` set, any local-port conflict on 3201 killed the entire tunnel. Fixed at all three layers: form submit sends `null` on empty; create accepts null verbatim; row read-back preserves null. PATCH-to-clear (sending `bridgePort: null` or `bridgePort: ''` in PUT) now actually clears. Persisted non-null values (e.g. 4501) still round-trip unchanged ‚Äî only the falsy ‚Üí 3201 coercion went away.
  - **Bug 3 ‚Äî Tunnel failure messages now name the actual problem instead of "check SSH connectivity".** Pre-#160, `lib/tunnel.js:ensureTunnel` spawned SSH with `stdio: 'ignore'`, discarding stderr. When `tcpProbe` saw the tunnel didn't come up, the only available message was a generic "SSH tunnel spawned but port not connectable" ‚Äî which `server.js` then wrapped as "Tunnel failed: ‚Ä¶", indistinguishable from a real SSH connectivity issue. The local-bind conflict (the canonical #160 incident shape) is invisible in this message. Fixed by switching stdio to `['ignore', 'ignore', 'pipe']`, buffering stderr (4 KB cap), and routing it through a new `_formatTunnelError(stderr, extraForwards)` helper that recognizes the load-bearing failure modes ‚Äî local-bind conflict (with a special hint when the conflicting port matches a secondary forward like Bridge Port), `Permission denied`/`publickey` auth failures, `Connection refused`/`No route to host`/`Could not resolve hostname` network failures ‚Äî and renders them with actionable text. Unrecognized stderr falls back to surfacing the first non-empty line so the user has something to grep.
  - **Schema migration v14 ‚Üí v15 (`lib/store.js`)**: `openclaw_connections.bridge_port` was `INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 3201` pre-#160. SQLite can't `ALTER COLUMN` to drop NOT NULL, so the migration recreates the table preserving every existing row's data verbatim ‚Äî rows that already have 3201 keep 3201 (the migration changes only the column constraint, not existing values). Wrapped with explicit `BEGIN; ... COMMIT;` SQL (the runtime DB engine is `node:sqlite`'s `DatabaseSync`, which doesn't expose a `.transaction()` wrapper). Postcondition check verifies `PRAGMA table_info` reports `notnull=0` before advancing `schema_version` ‚Äî if the recreate step silently failed for any reason, the migration throws rather than marking the DB v15 with a v14 schema still in place (Critic MAJOR-3). Best-effort `ROLLBACK` in the catch block if a BEGIN landed without COMMIT. Fresh `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` also updated for new installs.
  - **Docs**: `docs/openclaw-setup.md` updated ‚Äî the Bridge Port row in the connection-fields table now says "leave blank for non-ClawBridge OpenClaw deployments" rather than presenting `3201` as the default (Critic MAJOR-4). The "How it works" section also clarifies that the Bridge Port forward is conditional on the field being set.
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 4 MAJORs / 4 MINORs / 2 NITs. All MAJORs + actionable MINORs addressed in-chunk. (M1 ‚Äî `Warning: Permanently added` first-connect noise was leaking into the auth/network/fallback messages) `_firstLine` now filters lines matching `/^Warning: Permanently added/i` before picking the first meaningful line; auth + network + fallback branches all render the real error line, not the host-key Warning. (M2 ‚Äî original "migration preserves data" test was actually testing API round-trip on a fresh v15 DB, not the migration code path) Added a real migration regression test that opens a fresh tmpDir, seeds it directly via `node:sqlite` with the pre-#160 schema (`bridge_port INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 3201`) + `schema_version = 14` + two pre-existing rows (one with `3201`, one with `4501`), then calls `store.init()` to fire `_runMigrations` and asserts (a) `schema_version` advanced to 15, (b) `PRAGMA table_info` reports `notnull=0` + `dflt_value=null`, (c) both pre-existing row values survived verbatim, (d) post-migration inserts with `bridgePort: null` now succeed. (M3 ‚Äî silent migration-failure ‚Üí false v15) Postcondition check throws if `bridge_port` isn't nullable after the recreate step; `schema_version` advancement is gated on the throw not firing. (M4 ‚Äî `docs/openclaw-setup.md` still claimed 3201 as the default) See "Docs" bullet above. (Min1 ‚Äî IPv6 bind-conflict regex) Bind-pattern regex broadened to `/bind\s+(?:\[[^\]]+\]|[^:\s]+):(\d+):\s*Address already in use/i` so `bind [::1]:port` matches the same way `bind [127.0.0.1]:port` does; regression test added. (Min3 ‚Äî spawn-error swallow) `ssh` binary missing / ENOENT now seeds `stderrBuf` with the spawn error message before exiting, so `_formatTunnelError` can surface the real reason instead of the generic "port not connectable" fallback. (Min4 ‚Äî `bridgePort: 0` contract) New test pins current behavior (0 round-trips literally; server.js's `conn.bridgePort ?` truthiness check correctly treats 0 as "no bridge" for the tunnel layer) and documents the contract; explicit input validation tracked separately as future work. NITs (migration comment wording, IIFE vs named helper) accepted as-is. UTF-8-multibyte stderr slice (MINOR-2) accepted as-is ‚Äî message correctness > codepoint hygiene on a 4 KB error path; if it ever matters we have a clear extension point.
  - **Tests**: +20 across `test/api-openclaw.test.js` (9 ‚Äî bridgePort=undefined/null/empty-string/explicit/zero all round-trip through POST + GET, PUT clears bridgePort via null or "", explicit 3201 is preserved on the create‚Üíread-back round-trip locking in data-preservation contract for the migration, PORT_CONFLICT response carries `error` + `code: 'PORT_CONFLICT'` so the frontend toast contract holds), `test/tunnel.test.js` (10 ‚Äî empty/missing stderr falls through to generic; bind conflict on primary port; bind conflict on extra forward with the "Clear the secondary forward" hint; auth-failure recognition; network-error recognition for refused/no-route/DNS; unknown stderr falls back to first non-empty line; multiple bind-error stderr-formatting variants all extract the port correctly; canary that `_formatTunnelError` stays exported; `Warning: Permanently added` first-connect noise is correctly skipped across auth/network/fallback branches; IPv6 bind-conflict extraction), and `test/store-openclaw.test.js` (1 ‚Äî real v14‚Üív15 migration regression test described above; plus the existing assertions updated for the new contract: default `bridgePort` is `null` not 3201, schema column reports `notnull: 0` + `dflt_value: null`). Four other tests had the schema version assertion bumped 14 ‚Üí 15 (`test/store.test.js`, `test/store-portleases.test.js`, `test/sessions-webui.test.js`, `test/store-session-mode.test.js`). 1832 total passing (was 1812 at v3.16.0).
  - **Backwards compatibility**: existing OpenClaw connection records pre-#160 carry `bridge_port = 3201` in their row data. The migration preserves those values verbatim ‚Äî they're read back as 3201, server.js still adds the `-L 3201` forward, and the tunnel still depends on the local 3201 being free (same as before). Only NEW connections created after #160 with the field left blank get `null`, and the tunnel skips the extra forward for those. Users with existing affected records can clear via the UI now that PATCH-to-null works end-to-end.

- **Chunk-1 orphan-hook protection now reaches pre-#146 runtime templates (#158)** ‚Äî `v3.15.0`'s chunk-1 `requires`-array filter on methodology hook entries (`engines._filterHookEntriesByRequires`, #145 chunk 1) is load-bearing for suppressing the infinite Stop-hook ‚Üí synthetic-user-message loop documented in ADR 0001. The filter is only effective when each hook entry carries a `requires` array. Bundled templates have it; runtime templates at `~/.tangleclaw/templates/<methodology>/template.json` that were copied from bundled *before #146 merged* do not. `_mergeBundledTemplate` (#136 / PR #156) reconciled `wrap.steps` and missing top-level *object* fields but did not traverse `hooks.<engine>[].entries[]` ‚Äî so pre-#146 runtime templates stayed `requires`-less even after v3.16.0 self-heal ran, and chunk-1's filter passed those entries through unchanged. Result: every prawduct project on a pre-#146 install was still injecting the orphan Stop hook on every session-launch sync and still hitting the infinite loop. Confirmed live on TC-v3 itself on 2026-05-12 against server already running v3.16.0.
  - **`lib/store.js:_mergeBundledHookEntries(bundled, live)`** ‚Äî new top-level helper that walks `bundled.hooks.<engine>.<event>[]` and additively backfills missing keys (notably `requires`) into matched live entries. **Scope: hook ENTRY top-level keys only** ‚Äî the helper does not recurse into `entry.hooks[]` inner command objects, so a missing `statusMessage` on a nested command stays as-is. Inner-array semantics belong with #155's broader per-array policy work. Match policy: primary join by `matcher` string (the natural identity for hook entries); FIFO index fallback when matchers collide on the live side (e.g. duplicate matchers); same-position index match only when both sides lack a string matcher. Additive only ‚Äî never overwrite a live value, never delete user-added keys, never reorder live entries, never insert bundled-only entries that have no live match, never auto-create a live `hooks.<engine>` block that bundled defines but live lacks (that's `addMissing`'s upstream job). Backfilled values are deep-cloned so subsequent mutations on the bundled object don't leak into live. Acknowledged limitation: when live has two entries sharing a matcher with bundled, the appearance-order FIFO match may attach `requires` to a user-added entry rather than the original-shape entry ‚Äî documented in the helper header; the worst-case outcome is the user's custom entry being filtered when its runtime is missing, which is a missing-hook annoyance, not a session-killing loop.
  - **`lib/store.js:_mergeBundledTemplate`** ‚Äî calls `_mergeBundledHookEntries` after the existing `addMissing` + `wrap.steps` passes. The new helper is independent: it only runs when both bundled and live have a `hooks` object, leaves all other reconciliation policies untouched, and contributes to the existing `changed` flag so the file is rewritten only when something was actually added. The atomic-write semantics (`fs.writeFileSync` with `mode: 0o600`) and fail-open malformed-JSON behavior inherit from the existing `_mergeBundledTemplate` shell.
  - **Why this was deferred to #158 rather than caught in #136**: `#136`'s scope was deliberately narrow (per the v3.16.0 CHANGELOG entry's scope-limitation language). The acknowledged-as-future case for object-id-keyed arrays + hook arrays was filed as #155 for a broader policy-table design pass. The live loop manifesting on TC-v3 on 2026-05-12 ‚Äî chunk-1's protection silently no-op'ing on a real install ‚Äî elevated the hook-entry subset to its own ahead-of-#155 fix, since the latency between filing #155 and shipping it would have meant every prawduct install on the same install class kept hitting the loop. The targeted fix here is small (one new helper + one wiring line) and load-bearing (closes a session-killing safety gap); #155 still owns generalizing the reconciler to `phases` / `init.directories` / `prime.sections` / eval-dimension lists / object-id-keyed arrays under a per-array policy table.
  - **ADR 0001 updated**: incident catalog adds the #158 row. New anti-pattern entry: *"Protective sync exists but doesn't traverse the data shape required to deliver the protection"* ‚Äî codifies the lesson that a reconciler covering only a subset of the bundled‚Üílive state class can leave the gate it was meant to protect un-deployed for existing installs. Resolution rule: when adding a sync intended to protect gate G, write a test proving the sync actually delivers the protection on the canonical legacy data shape, not just on freshly-generated state.
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 2 MAJORs / 3 MINORs / 1 NIT. All MAJORs + MINORs addressed in-chunk. (M1 ‚Äî test-isolation) `test/issue-158-syncEngineHooks-integration.test.js` now scaffolds `store._setBasePath` + `store.init()` in `before`/`after` hooks mirroring `test/engines.test.js`, so the engine profile read inside `engines.syncEngineHooks` doesn't reach the host's real `~/.tangleclaw/engines/`. (M2 ‚Äî additive-at-entry-level contract) Added regression test pinning the documented behavior that the helper does NOT auto-add bundled engine blocks missing from live (that's `addMissing`'s job upstream in `_mergeBundledTemplate`); helper header explicitly states the boundary. (Min1 ‚Äî entry-level-only contract) Helper JSDoc + CHANGELOG bullet now explicitly state the backfill is hook-entry top-level keys only and does not recurse into `entry.hooks[]` inner command objects, plus a regression test that asserts a missing `statusMessage` on an inner command stays missing. (Min2 ‚Äî mtime brittleness on coarse-resolution filesystems) Integration no-op test switched from `fs.statSync(...).mtime` comparison to `fs.readFileSync(...).equals(...)` byte-equal check; filesystem-agnostic. (Min3 ‚Äî defensive-branch coverage gap) Added regression test for malformed entries (null / non-object) inside an otherwise-valid hook entries array ‚Äî pins the contract that malformed entries are skipped silently while well-formed siblings still backfill. NIT findings on CHANGELOG verbosity accepted as-is ‚Äî the post-mortem on "why deferred from #136" stays in for the #155 timeline; future maintenance can trim once #155 lands.
  - **Tests**: 22 new across two files. `test/store.test.js ‚Üí describe('_mergeBundledHookEntries (#158)')` adds 16 unit tests: canonical #158 incident shape, no-overwrite of existing `requires`, user-added-key preservation, matcher-mismatch no-cross-match, bundled-only-entry not inserted, both-sides-no-matcher index fallback, reordered-live entries matched by matcher key (not position), duplicate-matcher FIFO index queue, malformed-shape fail-open, multi-engine independent reconciliation, deep-clone defense, no-op when live has no hooks block, no-op when bundled has no hooks block, bundled-only-engine skipped silently (additive-at-entry-level contract), malformed bundled/live entries (null/string in array) skipped without throwing, entry-level-only contract (inner `entry.hooks[]` not recursed). `test/store.test.js ‚Üí describe('_mergeBundledTemplate hook-entry reconciliation integration (#158)')` adds 2 file-roundtrip tests: end-to-end backfill written back to disk; byte-equal preservation when nothing to add (no rewrite on no-op ‚Äî filesystem-agnostic content comparison, not mtime-based). `test/store.test.js ‚Üí init describe ‚Üí reconciles stale runtime methodology template hook entries against bundled on init (#158)` adds 1 init-level integration test seeding a pre-#146 runtime template into the test's templates dir, calling `store.init()`, and asserting the bundled prawduct template's `requires` reaches the reconciled file. `test/issue-158-syncEngineHooks-integration.test.js` adds 3 end-to-end tests covering the full chain (pre-reconcile bug-locked-in negative control + post-reconcile orphan suppression + post-reconcile-with-runtime hook injection), with `store._setBasePath` + `store.init()` isolation so the engine profile read isn't talking to the host's real `~/.tangleclaw/`. 1834 total passing (was 1812 at v3.16.0).

## [3.16.0] - 2026-05-12

> üöÄ **Default-behavior change for new projects + safety/cleanup bundle.** New TangleClaw projects now default to **silent prime delivery** (#129) ‚Äî cleaner-scrollback session starts via Claude Code's `SessionStart` hook instead of typed-prime via the terminal. Existing projects with explicitly persisted `silentPrime: false` continue to honor that setting; non-Claude engines are untouched (capability-gated). Bundled with three substantive bug fixes / housekeeping items: the **methodology-flip cleanup audit** that closed out the #145 series with the codebase's **first ADR** formalizing the symmetric-capability-gates pattern (#145 chunk 3); **retirement of the `methodology: null` semantic** ‚Äî the dead-code removal branch is gone, projConfig defaults align with the DB schema, and the API now rejects null with a pointer to `'minimal'` (#151); **auto-reconcile of bundled methodology templates on server start** ‚Äî runtime templates at `~/.tangleclaw/templates/` self-heal when bundled updates ship (#136), matching the #119 engine-profile pattern. Anyone on v3.15.0 will get the update-pill notification with a clickable link to this release page.

### Fixed

- **Bundled methodology template updates reach existing installs on next server start (#136)** ‚Äî `~/.tangleclaw/templates/<methodology>/template.json` is a one-shot copy of the bundled `data/templates/<id>/template.json` from `lib/store.js:_copyBundledTemplates`. The original copy logic was gated on `if (!fs.existsSync(destFile))` ‚Äî once a runtime template was on disk, subsequent bundled updates never propagated. Result: v3.13.7's addition of `memory-update` to bundled `wrap.steps` shipped correctly but didn't reach any TC install whose runtime templates pre-dated v3.13.7. Every wrap from such an install continued to omit the MEMORY.md step in the AI-facing wrap text. Same drift class as #119 (engine profile bundled-runtime drift), just on the methodology-template axis instead of the engine-profile axis. The earlier #119 fix added `_mergeBundledProfile` to self-heal engine profiles; #136 adds the equivalent `_mergeBundledTemplate` for methodology templates.
  - **`lib/store.js:_mergeBundledTemplate(bundledPath, livePath)`** ‚Äî mirrors `_mergeBundledProfile` for templates. Two reconciliation policies. (1) **Object fields**: recursively add missing keys from bundled into live (never overwrite, never delete) ‚Äî same `addMissing` closure pattern as the engine reconciler. Picks up brand-new top-level template fields (e.g. a future `eval` block) without disturbing user customizations to existing fields. (2) **`wrap.steps` array**: if the live array is a strict ordered subset of the bundled array ‚Äî i.e. the user is on an older version that's missing some bundled steps but hasn't reordered or added their own ‚Äî replace with bundled. If the live array contains steps not in bundled, or appears in different order, the user has customized; leave alone and log at debug level so verbose-mode operators can see the divergence. The #136 incident shape (v3.13.7 added `memory-update` between `next-session-prime` and `commit`) is exactly the subset-replace case.
  - **`lib/store.js:_isOrderedSubset(needle, haystack)`** ‚Äî pure helper used by the wrap.steps reconciliation policy. Returns true when every element of `needle` appears in `haystack` in the same relative order (possibly with intervening elements). Distinguishes "stale older version" from "user customization" without ambiguity.
  - **`lib/store.js:_copyBundledTemplates`** ‚Äî the previously no-op else branch (`destFile` already exists) now calls `_mergeBundledTemplate` for `template.json` files. Other files in the methodology directory (scripts, README) are left alone ‚Äî the user owns those after first copy and they aren't part of the additive-bundled-changes story.
  - **Safety**: fail-open on malformed JSON (same as `_mergeBundledProfile` and the chunk-2 orphan-hooks scan path); no migration step, no schema version bump, no manual intervention required by users. Next server restart picks up the bundled `wrap.steps` additions on every install and adds any new top-level object fields. Atomic write via `fs.writeFileSync` with `mode: 0o600` matches the existing reconciler's filesystem permissions.
  - **Scope limitation**: only the `wrap.steps` array is reconciled. Other arrays in bundled templates (`phases`, `init.directories`, `prime.sections`, `actions`, eval-dimension lists, hook entries) still drift on existing installs ‚Äî the policies for object-id-keyed arrays and set-union semantics need their own design pass. Filed as **#155** for follow-up. The user-removed-step case (live missing a step that bundled has, where the removal was intentional rather than a stale-version artifact) is acknowledged-indistinguishable from the canonical stale-version case in `wrap.steps`; the chosen behavior is to re-add (treating user-side step deletions as something to re-introduce on next reconcile). A targeted regression test locks this in.
  - **Tests**: 17 new in `test/store.test.js`. `_isOrderedSubset` (6 ‚Äî ordered subsequence, missing elements, reordered elements, non-array inputs, duplicate-element handling in both needle and haystack, empty haystack). `_mergeBundledTemplate` (10 ‚Äî canonical #136 incident shape, user-added own step preserved, user-reordered preserved, identical no-op preserves mtime, missing top-level field added, existing field value preserved over bundled, recursive nested-key add, malformed JSON fail-open, missing bundled file no-op, plus the Critic-driven "user-removed step is re-added ‚Äî acknowledged-limitation regression test"). `init` integration (1 ‚Äî `reconciles stale runtime methodology template against bundled on init (#136)` exercises the full `_copyBundledTemplates` ‚Üí `_mergeBundledTemplate` glue against a seeded stale `template.json`). 1812 total passing (was 1795).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 2 MAJORs (one a non-defect verification, one a scope-limitation) / 3 MINORs / 3 NITs. Addressed in-chunk: (M2 ‚Äî scope-limitation overpromise) CHANGELOG language narrowed from "self-heals every install" to explicitly scope the heal to `wrap.steps` + new top-level object fields; a follow-up issue **#155** was filed to track generalizing the array reconciliation to `phases`, `init.directories`, `prime.sections`, eval-dimension lists, and object-id-keyed arrays under a proper per-array policy table. (Min1) added 2 `_isOrderedSubset` edge cases ‚Äî duplicate elements in needle/haystack with three sub-assertions, and empty-haystack handling. (Min3) added the "user-removed step is re-added on reconcile" test as the Critic recommended, locking in the acknowledged-indistinguishable-from-stale-older policy choice so a future contributor who wants the opposite behavior knows where to update it. NIT findings (log payload verbosity for empty live arrays, wording precision around "wrap text" vs "wrap.steps array", a redundant-but-correct length-check inside the wrap.steps reconciliation block) accepted as-is.

### Changed

- **`silentPrime` now defaults to `true` for new projects (#129)** ‚Äî Per #103's chunk-3 wrap, the original silent-prime feature shipped with `DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.silentPrime: false` as a deliberate "opt-in until proven stable" stance. The acceptance criterion was *"~2 weeks of real use with no regressions."* The soak period is satisfied ‚Äî silent prime has been the active delivery mechanism across the full #137 / #140 / #145 / #146 / #148 / #149 / #150 / #151 / #152 / #153 release cycle, the symmetric-capability-gates ADR locks in all four gates around it, and the prime-file cleanup contract (`sessions._removePrimeFile` on silent‚Üítyped transitions) is regression-tested. Flipping the default makes the cleaner-scrollback experience the standard for new projects without changing the per-project override semantics for anyone who explicitly persisted `silentPrime: false`.
  - **`lib/store.js:DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.silentPrime`**: `false` ‚Üí `true`. Inline comment documents the post-#129 reasoning and points at the capability gate (`engineProfile.capabilities.supportsSilentPrime`) which continues to protect non-Claude engines (Codex / Gemini / Aider) regardless of this default ‚Äî they fall through to the typed-prime path because their engine profiles don't advertise the capability.
  - **Backwards compatibility**: projects with explicit `silentPrime: false` in their `.tangleclaw/project.json` continue to honor that setting (the load merge preserves explicit values over defaults). Only projects with NO `silentPrime` field ‚Äî newly-created projects, or pre-#103 projects that were never opened in the Settings modal ‚Äî pick up the new default on next session launch.
  - **Tests**: 1 inverted in `test/projects.test.js` (`enrichProject exposes silentPrime: true by default (#129)` ‚Äî was `false`); 1 inverted in `test/sessions.test.js` (`DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.silentPrime is true (#129 ‚Äî soak satisfied)` ‚Äî was `false`). 6 tests across `test/projects.test.js`, `test/sessions.test.js`, and `test/engines.test.js` updated to be explicit about `silentPrime: false` in their projConfig setup (rather than implicitly relying on the default). The two-step `beforeEach` pattern in `test/engines.test.js` (now writes a baseline `project.json` with explicit `silentPrime: false`) keeps the methodology-hook tests focused on the methodology hooks alone without the post-#129 baseline injecting an extra `SessionStart` entry. Two `silentPrime=true must not have been written` assertions in `updateProject` rejection tests were re-shaped from "load returns false" to "project.json does not exist" ‚Äî intent-preserving across the default flip (`fs.existsSync(projConfigFile)` is the actual no-write check; the original `silentPrime === false` assertion would now assert the new default, masking a real persistence bug). 1795 total passing (unchanged from #151's count).

- **Retired the `methodology: null` semantic ‚Äî every TC project has a methodology (#151)** ‚Äî Closes the SQL-constraint blocker the #145 chunk 3 audit surfaced. The `PATCH methodology: null` path stacked a `ReferenceError` (fixed in chunk 3) on top of `SQLITE_CONSTRAINT_NOTNULL: NOT NULL constraint failed: projects.methodology` (the DB schema is `methodology TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'minimal'` at `lib/store.js:521`). Rather than picking between "ALTER TABLE allow NULL + migration / treat-null-as-'minimal' / reject-null-at-API," #151 retired the null-methodology semantic entirely ‚Äî per `docs/methodology-guide.md` *"Each project gets one methodology"* and `minimal` is explicitly the no-workflow methodology, the canonical way to clear methodology-specific behavior.
  - **`lib/projects.js:updateProject` methodology branch**: `updates.methodology === null` now returns a 400-style error: `"methodology cannot be null ‚Äî to clear methodology-specific workflow, PATCH methodology to 'minimal'"`. The dead removal branch (~40 lines, lines 1157-1206 of the pre-fix file) deleted entirely. The chunk-3 ReferenceError hoist-fix is also retired with the removal ‚Äî the bug it fixed lived on the now-unreachable removal path.
  - **`lib/projects.js:createProject`**: removed the `data.methodology === null` special case at line 144 that propagated null into projConfig (while the DB always defaulted to `'minimal'`, creating a split-brain). Default chain is now `data.methodology || config.defaultMethodology || 'minimal'` ‚Äî both sources of truth agree. The `if (methodologyId)` guard around `methodologies.initialize` removed since methodologyId is now always truthy; the `methodologyTemplate || {}` fallback in the `engines.generateConfig` call simplified to plain `methodologyTemplate`.
  - **`lib/projects.js:attachProject`**: the trailing `config.defaultMethodology || null` fallback updated to `config.defaultMethodology || 'minimal'`. The `if (methodologyId)` guard around the post-attach `syncEngineHooks` call removed (methodologyId is always truthy after this fix; the guard was dead code).
  - **`lib/store.js:DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG`**: `methodology: null` changed to `methodology: 'minimal'`. Aligns projConfig's source-of-truth with the DB schema's `NOT NULL DEFAULT 'minimal'`. Pre-#151, any reader of projConfig.methodology had to handle null even though the DB never produced it; that ambiguity is gone.
  - **API contract change**: technically a breaking change for callers using `PATCH /api/projects/:name` with `{ methodology: null }`. In practice not breaking because the path was completely unreachable (ReferenceError + SQL constraint) ‚Äî no caller in the wild can have been using it successfully. Documented in this entry so search-engine-readers of "did TC remove a feature?" find the context.
  - **ADR 0001 updated**: incident catalog adds the #151 row; the "anti-patterns this ADR forbids" section gains a new entry ‚Äî "split-brain default values" ‚Äî codifying that DB schema defaults and in-memory config object defaults must agree on the canonical value. The methodology gate in the gates table is unchanged in shape, but the documented behavior is now "every project has one; null is rejected."
  - **Tests**: 4 new in `test/projects.test.js ‚Üí methodology flip cleanup audit (#145, chunk 3)` describe block, 1 updated in `test/store.test.js`. (1) `PATCH methodology: null` returns the rejection error pointing at `'minimal'`; project state (methodology, hooks) unchanged after rejection ‚Äî no destructive partial mutation on validation failure (replaces the chunk-3 `it.skip()` placeholder). (2) Combined `PATCH { name, methodology: null }` rejects without renaming the project on disk or in the DB ‚Äî pre-fix the null-rejection lived inside the methodology branch *after* the rename branch had already mutated state; the new validation runs in the pre-mutation phase so combined-payload rejections don't leave half-applied changes (Critic Major). (3) `store.projectConfig.load` coerces on-disk `methodology: null` to `'minimal'` so pre-#151 installs upgrade cleanly without a separate migration pass (Critic Major). (4) `store.DEFAULT_PROJECT_CONFIG.methodology` equals `'minimal'`, not null ‚Äî locks in the projConfig/DB alignment. `test/store.test.js ‚Üí projectConfig defaults` updated to assert the new default. 1795 total passing (was 1791 + 1 skipped).
  - **Independent Critic ran during the chunk** per `feedback_critic_before_wrap.md`. Verdict: 2 BLOCKERs / 2 MAJORs / 1 MINOR / 2 NITs. All 5 substantive findings addressed in-chunk before the wrap. **B1**: `public/ui.js` Project Settings modal exposed a `<option value="none">None</option>` that POSTed `methodology: null` and would now produce a generic error toast for any user trying to save settings ‚Äî the option also appeared in the create-project wizard (line 1051) and the methodology-switch confirmation modal's copy paths. All three call sites updated to drop the None pseudo-methodology; the picker now shows the real templates only, and `'minimal'` is the canonical no-workflow choice. **B2**: `server.js:980` bulk-import path passed `methodology: detectedMethodology ? detectedMethodology.id : (config.defaultMethodology || null)` directly to `store.projects.create` ‚Äî would have hit `SQLITE_CONSTRAINT_NOTNULL` if a project with no detectable methodology was imported without a `defaultMethodology` configured. Fixed to fall through to `'minimal'`. **M1**: null-rejection originally lived inside the methodology branch after name + engine mutation paths ‚Äî combined `PATCH { name: 'new', methodology: null }` would have renamed the project on disk + in the DB before the rejection fired. Moved the validation to the pre-mutation phase alongside the silentPrime validation; added a regression test for the combined-payload case. **M2**: existing on-disk `project.json` files written by pre-#151 TC carry an explicit `methodology: null` that the merge loop in `store.projectConfig.load` would propagate over the new `'minimal'` default ‚Äî upgraded installs would still see null in projConfig. Added a one-line coercion at the end of `load` (`if (merged.methodology === null) merged.methodology = 'minimal';`) plus a regression test that writes a legacy-shaped project.json and asserts the coercion. **NIT-test-brittleness**: original null-rejection test asserted `errors.length === 1`, which would break for any future unrelated warning the path might surface ‚Äî softened to `errors.some(e => /methodology cannot be null/i.test(e) && /'minimal'/.test(e))`. Two NITs from the Critic accepted as-is (CHANGELOG "API contract change" framing kept; ADR "split-brain default values" wording kept).

### Added

- **`docs/adr/0001-symmetric-capability-gates.md` ‚Äî first ADR (#145 chunk 3)** ‚Äî Documents the symmetric-capability-gates pattern as a permanent design principle for TC. Codifies the rule "when two locations encode the same conceptual state, every transition path between configurations must consistently update both" with the incident catalog (#103, #119, #136, #137, #140, #145, #151), the four currently-in-scope gates (methodology / engine / silentPrime / methodology hook `requires`), the matching callsite verification table, anti-patterns the ADR forbids, and the playbook for applying the pattern to future gates. The ADR is the new home for the rule the Critic surfaced on #103 PR #125; existing memory `feedback_symmetric_capability_gates.md` cross-references it.

### Fixed

- **Methodology-flip cleanup audit + latent `ReferenceError` on the removal path (#145, chunk 3)** ‚Äî The third and final chunk of the #145 series closes the audit-and-document loop on the symmetric-capability-gates work that started with #103.
  - **What chunk 3 was scoped to verify**: does `PATCH /api/projects/:name` with a methodology change correctly strip the previous methodology's hook entries from `.claude/settings.json`? Existing behavior was implicit (`syncEngineHooks` rebuilds the `hooks` block from scratch each call, never carries forward) but had no regression test. Without a test, a future refactor of `syncEngineHooks` to "merge with existing instead of rebuild" would silently re-open the orphan-hook class.
  - **What the audit found**: the implicit behavior was correct ‚Äî the canonical flip cases (prawduct ‚Üí minimal, plus non-hook key preservation, plus silentPrime baseline survival across the flip) all work as expected. But the audit also uncovered a latent `ReferenceError` on the methodology-removal branch at `lib/projects.js:1174`: `currentTemplate` was declared with `const` inside an inner `if (project.methodology)` block (line 1160) but referenced outside that block in the extension-rule reset loop. The reference was in a temporal-dead-zone scope and would throw `ReferenceError: currentTemplate is not defined` on any `PATCH methodology: null` call where the project had a previous methodology. Never exercised by tests, never tripped in production because the UI doesn't currently expose a "remove methodology" affordance ‚Äî but a real latent crash.
  - **Fix in `lib/projects.js`**: `currentTemplate` hoisted to outer scope as `let currentTemplate = null` so the extension-rule reset loop on line 1183 can still see it after the inner block closes. Minimal 2-line change; preserves all existing semantics.
  - **Second bug discovered in the same audit, scope-deferred**: with the `ReferenceError` fixed, the same removal path then throws `SQLITE_CONSTRAINT_NOTNULL: NOT NULL constraint failed: projects.methodology` at `lib/store.js:1278` because the schema is `methodology TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'minimal'` (line 521) but the removal branch sets `storeUpdates.methodology = null`. Three reasonable fixes (ALTER TABLE allow NULL + migration / treat-null-as-'minimal' at the API / reject-null-at-API) require a product decision about how "no methodology" is modeled and which existing readers handle the NULL case. **Filed as #151 for its own session.** The chunk-3 hoist-fix stays ‚Äî it's a real defect on a path that's now SQL-blocked rather than ReferenceError-blocked, and when #151 lands, this fix won't have to be re-done.
  - **Tests**: 4 new + 1 skipped placeholder in `test/projects.test.js ‚Üí methodology flip cleanup audit (#145, chunk 3)` describe block. Scaffold helper sets up a prawduct project with the `tools/product-hook` runtime materialized on disk (so chunk-1's `requires` filter accepts the hooks), registers it via `store.projects.create({ ..., methodology: 'prawduct' })`, and triggers `engines.syncEngineHooks` to inject the prawduct entries ‚Äî same low-level pattern as the existing silentPrime engine-flip tests at line 1076 (bypasses `projects.createProject`'s single-configured-`projectsDir` constraint). Coverage: (1) `PATCH methodology: prawduct ‚Üí minimal` rebuilds hooks without any prawduct entries (canonical audit case the build plan asked for); (2) PATCH preserves non-hook keys in `.claude/settings.json` (`companyAnnouncements`, `permissions`) across the flip ‚Äî same preservation contract chunk 2's bulk-repair locked in for the strip path; (3) `PATCH methodology: minimal ‚Üí prawduct` materializes prawduct hooks (reverse-direction coverage required by ADR 0001 anti-pattern ¬ß4 ‚Äî both directions of every paired transition need testing); (4) silentPrime baseline `SessionStart` hook survives methodology flip when opted in ‚Äî locks in the capability-gate independence (methodology gate clears methodology entries, baseline gate is separate). The flip-to-null path is shipped as a `skip`-flagged placeholder test (`TODO #151: PATCH methodology: null strips all methodology hooks`) so the gap shows up in test-runner output and grep, not just in a prose comment. 1792 total (1791 passing + 1 skipped); was 1787 passing pre-chunk.
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 0 MAJORs / 5 MINORs / 2 NITs. All MINORs addressed in-chunk: (M1, M2, M3) ADR cited drifted/handwaved line numbers for the symmetric-gates callsite table (`line 1156`, `line 1090s`) ‚Äî corrected to actual post-fix line numbers (1149, 1346, 1357) with branch-start lines for the methodology pair (1157 / 1201) added for symmetry; (M4) the `PATCH methodology: null` deferral was prose-only and easy to miss ‚Äî added an `it.skip()` placeholder with a concrete TODO body for #151, so picking up that issue is grep-friendly; (M5) the original test block covered only the strip direction (prawduct ‚Üí minimal) but ADR 0001 ¬ß"Anti-patterns" forbids single-direction regression tests ‚Äî added the `minimal ‚Üí prawduct` materialize-direction test as the fourth in the block. NITs accepted as-is (hoist-fix correctness already verified by passing tests; CHANGELOG verbosity acknowledged but not optimized).
  - **ADR shipped alongside**: `docs/adr/0001-symmetric-capability-gates.md` formalizes the pattern this entire #145 series exercised. The audit-confirmation tests above are the concrete enforcement of the ADR's "write a regression test that asserts the cleanup direction for every transition pair" guidance. With this ADR in place, future flag/field additions that affect on-disk state get the same treatment by default.
  - **#145 closeout**: chunks 1 + 2 + 3 are all merged. The build plan at `.claude/plans/issue-145-methodology-hook-preconditions.md` is now fully resolved. The deferred SQL-constraint follow-up (#151) is its own scope, not a #145 chunk.

## [3.15.0] - 2026-05-10

> üöÄ **Recommended upgrade for ALL TangleClaw users.** This release ships the **update-available pill release-notes link** (#149) **plus the full safety bundle for the orphan methodology-hook loop** that could put any prawduct-tagged project into an infinite Stop-hook ‚Üí synthetic-user-message session-killing cycle (#145 chunks 1 + 2, plus the related symmetric-capability-gates fixes #137 and #140). The loop manifested live across multiple projects on 2026-05-10 ‚Äî every install on v3.14.x or earlier should upgrade. After upgrading, the dashboard banner will auto-detect and one-click-repair any already-injected orphan hook blocks across your registered projects.

### Added

- **Update-available pill links to the GitHub release page (#149)** ‚Äî The dashboard's update-notification pill (shipped in v3.13.0 as a text-only label) was missing the most important affordance: a way to actually see what's in the new release. Users saw "v3.X.Y available" but had no in-product path to the release notes ‚Äî they had to manually navigate to GitHub. Closing this gap turns the pill from a passive notice into a one-click upgrade-discovery surface, and makes the update-notification mechanism a documented, prominent feature of TC (README addition + this entry).
  - **Backend in `lib/update-checker.js`**: new pure parser `_parseGitHubRemote(remoteUrl)` accepts the four remote forms real users + CI environments produce ‚Äî `https://github.com/<owner>/<repo>(.git)?(/)?`, `https://<user>(:<token>)?@github.com/...` (gh-CLI tokenized clones), `ssh://git@github.com/...` (Docker / CI protocol form), and `git@github.com:<owner>/<repo>(.git)?` (classic SCP-style SSH) ‚Äî and returns `{ owner, repo }` or null. Host match is case-insensitive (`GitHub.com` is served as a valid alias). Owner and repo are restricted to GitHub's character class `[A-Za-z0-9._-]+` as a defense-in-depth gate against malformed remotes propagating junk into the rendered href (with `esc()` as the actual escape boundary at the render layer). `_getReleasesUrlBase()` shells out to `git remote get-url origin`, hands the output to the parser, and returns `https://github.com/<owner>/<repo>/releases/tag/` on success or null on non-GitHub remotes / missing remote / git failure. `checkForUpdate()` and `getCachedStatus()` now include a `releaseUrl` field (e.g. `https://github.com/Jason-Vaughan/TangleClaw/releases/tag/v3.15.0`) built from the URL base + the raw tag string (preserves any leading `v` so the URL matches what GitHub serves). Fork installs link to their fork's release pages, not the canonical repo, since the URL follows the same `origin` that the tag-poll uses.
  - **Frontend in `public/landing.js`**: `loadUpdateStatus()` now wraps the version label in `<a class="update-pill-link" href="${esc(data.releaseUrl)}" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" title="View release notes">` when the API supplies `releaseUrl`. Falls back to plain text when `releaseUrl` is null/absent ‚Äî so a v3.15.0+ frontend talking to a v3.14.0-era backend still surfaces the pill, just without the clickable link. The dismiss button, per-version localStorage key (`tc_updateDismissed_<version>`), and dismiss handler are unchanged.
  - **CSS in `public/style.css`**: `.update-pill-link` declared with `color: inherit` (link reads against the pill chrome, not the page's default link color), `text-decoration: underline` for affordance, `text-underline-offset: 2px` for legibility at 10px font size, and a `:hover { text-decoration: none }` swap to confirm interactivity on pointer.
  - **Security**: `href` value escaped through the same `esc()` helper used for all other rendered values, blocking attribute injection if a malformed remote URL ever slipped through `_getReleasesUrlBase`'s parser. `target="_blank"` paired with `rel="noopener noreferrer"` prevents tabnabbing ‚Äî both attrs locked in by a structural test so a future edit can't drop them.
  - **README addition**: new "Stay Updated" section (positioned right after Quick Start so users see it immediately post-install) covers cadence (start + daily), per-version dismiss, privacy stance (one daily GET to whichever remote `origin` points at; no telemetry, no install fingerprinting), offline fallback (silent), and the upgrade command sequence (`git pull --ff-only && ./deploy/install.sh`). Forks get a clarifying note that the link follows their `origin` and not the canonical repo.
  - **Tests**: 39 new in `test/update-pill-link.test.js` covering three surfaces. (1) `_parseGitHubRemote` table-driven coverage: 14 accept cases (all four remote forms √ó `.git` / no-`.git` / trailing-slash combinations, case-insensitive host, tokenized clones, whitespace tolerance, real-world owner/repo characters) + 14 reject cases (non-GitHub hosts, extra path segments, empty/null/undefined, malformed protocols, file://, ftp://) + a defense-in-depth assertion that owners/repos with characters outside `[A-Za-z0-9._-]` are rejected. (2) `_getReleasesUrlBase` integration: derives a `/releases/tag/` URL from the test-runner's actual origin (shape assertion, owner-agnostic so fork test-runs still pass). (3) `getCachedStatus` shape: `releaseUrl` field is always present in the cached status, set to `null` not `undefined`, so the frontend's truthy gate never sees a `releaseUrl` of `undefined`. 6 frontend structural tests mirroring `test/orphan-hooks-banner.test.js` (anchor wrap when `releaseUrl` present, `target="_blank"` + `rel="noopener noreferrer"` lock-in, fallback-to-text branch when `releaseUrl` missing, `esc()` on `href`, dismiss-key regression guard, dismiss-button preservation). 2 CSS tests (inherited color + underline + hover toggle). 1787 total passing (was 1748).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 0 MAJORs / 2 MINORs / 3 NITs. Both MINORs addressed in-chunk: (M1) original regex only matched bare `https://github.com/...` and `git@github.com:...` forms, silently downgrading to plain text on tokenized-https / ssh-protocol / case-variant hosts ‚Äî fixed by extracting the regex into a pure `_parseGitHubRemote` helper that accepts all four real-world forms with case-insensitive host matching; (M2) original test only exercised the regex via the runner's real origin so edge URL shapes were uncovered ‚Äî fixed by adding the 27-row table-driven coverage above plus the defense-in-depth assertion. N1 (owner/repo character-class assertion as defense-in-depth) folded into the M1 fix. N3 (README "once a day" wording vs the actual 60s-after-start cadence) corrected to "Shortly after each server start, then once every 24 hours after that." N2 (test-count claim in CHANGELOG is fragile) accepted as documentation of the current state.

### Fixed

- **Bulk-repair admin pathway for orphan hook entries ‚Äî one-click escape hatch from the infinite Stop-hook loop (#145, chunk 2)** ‚Äî Chunk 1 stopped TC from injecting orphan hook blocks going forward, but existing affected projects only self-heal on their next session-launch sync. The live incident on 2026-05-10 (TC-v3 itself + RentalClaw-Project both hit the orphan Stop hook ‚Üí infinite hook-failure ‚Üí synthetic-user-message loop in the same hour, with Notse experiencing a separate governance-gate block) elevated the chunk-2 bulk-repair from convenience to a safety/UX feature. Without it, a user opening any of the 7 latent prawduct projects between #146 merging and the next session launch hits a session-killing loop with no escape outside hand-editing `.claude/settings.json`. The chunk-2 path detects and strips those entries in one pass without waiting for sync.
  - **New `lib/projects.js:scanForOrphanHooks()`** ‚Äî Read-only. Iterates all non-archived registered projects, reads each `.claude/settings.json`, walks every event's hook entries, and flags entries whose inner-command `command` strings reference `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/<path>` targets that don't exist on disk. Returns `{ scanned, projectsWithOrphans: [{ name, path, orphans: [{ event, index, matcher, missing, commands }] }], errors }`. Archived projects are skipped ‚Äî they aren't candidates for live sessions. Parse failures on a project's settings.json are captured as `errors[]` entries rather than aborting the whole scan, so one corrupt project doesn't blind the dashboard to the others.
  - **New `lib/projects.js:repairOrphanHooks(projectName?)`** ‚Äî Mutating sibling. Strips the orphan entries identified by the scan, preserves all kept entries and all non-hook keys (`companyAnnouncements`, `permissions`, etc.), and writes the file back atomically via tmp-file + same-directory rename. Idempotent ‚Äî a second call on a freshly-repaired project finds nothing to remove and is a no-op (the file is NOT rewritten; mtime preserved, asserted by test). Single-target via optional `projectName` argument; passing a non-existent name returns a `Project not found` error rather than silently scanning all. When all entries under an event are orphans, that event key is removed; when all events are emptied, `settings.hooks` is removed entirely.
  - **Scope decisions** ‚Äî (a) Classification looks for `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/<path>` and `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}/<path>` references only. Absolute paths in command strings (e.g. the silentPrime hook's `/Users/.../sessionstart-prime.sh`) are NOT probed because in shell commands they're ambiguous with CLI flags / URLs and the known incident shapes all involve the env-var form; a false-positive auto-strip would lose a legitimate hook. The TC-v3 incident shape is exactly this ‚Äî orphan `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/tools/product-hook` entries coexisted with a working absolute-path silentPrime entry, and the latter must survive repair (asserted by a dedicated test). (b) Path traversal (`..` segments) and absolute-path entries inside captured groups are treated as not-orphan and skipped ‚Äî the requires-filter (chunk 1) rejects them defensively, but here we fail-open because auto-stripping a hook is destructive. (c) Atomic write via tmp + rename so a crash mid-write can't corrupt settings.json.
  - **New endpoints in `server.js`** ‚Äî `GET /api/projects/orphan-hooks-scan` returns the read-only inventory. `POST /api/projects/repair-orphan-hooks` accepts an optional `{ project: <name> }` body for single-target repair (otherwise repairs all). The GET route is registered before `GET /api/projects/:name` so the literal path wins matching (locked in by a regression test that asserts the inventory shape, not project shape). 400 BAD_REQUEST when `project` is non-string; 404 NOT_FOUND when the named project doesn't exist.
  - **Dashboard banner in `public/index.html` + `public/landing.js` + `public/style.css`** ‚Äî When `loadProjects()` runs (initial load + 10s polling), it also fires `loadOrphanHooksInventory()` non-blocking. If the scan reports any orphans, an amber banner appears above the project cards with a count message, a `Repair All` button, and a `Details` button. The Repair button shows a `confirm()` dialog listing affected project names and explicitly noting "Non-orphan hooks and all other settings keys are preserved" before posting ‚Äî preventing a user from mistakenly thinking this nukes all hooks. The Details button shows an `alert()` with the per-project event / matcher / missing-paths breakdown so the user can sanity-check what will be stripped before confirming repair. After a successful repair, `loadProjects()` reloads, the next scan returns empty, and the banner hides.
  - **Why not wait for next session-launch sync to self-heal** ‚Äî Chunk 1's filter prevents future injections and existing affected projects would self-heal on their next TC-launched session. But the loop mechanic (Stop-hook failure ‚Üí synthetic-user-message ‚Üí new turn ‚Üí Stop hook fires again) burns context and tokens with zero forward progress, and the user has no way to launch a session to trigger the heal because the very-next session hits the loop too. The bulk-repair endpoint is the only path that breaks the cycle without manual intervention.
  - **Cross-cutting reference** ‚Äî Same #145 series as chunk 1. Pattern: when two locations encode the same conceptual state (here: the hook reference in `settings.json` and the runtime script on disk), all transition paths between configurations must consistently update both. Chunk 1 fixed the *creation* path (don't inject if runtime missing). Chunk 2 fixes the *cleanup* path (strip pre-existing injections). The full ADR formalizing the symmetric-capability-gates pattern is still deferred to chunk 3 along with the methodology-flip cleanup audit.
  - **Tests**: 47 new across two files. `test/orphan-hooks.test.js` (30 tests, 5 describe blocks): `_extractClaudeProjectDirPaths` (5 ‚Äî basic, brace form, empty/null, multi-ref, trailing punctuation), `_hookEntryOrphanMissing` (4 ‚Äî all-present, missing, traversal fails-open, malformed entry), `scanForOrphanHooks` (7 ‚Äî basic orphan, working-Notse-shape negative, TC-v3 incident shape with silentPrime preservation, bare-project skip, malformed-settings.json error capture, archived skip, dashboard-detail shape), `repairOrphanHooks` (8 ‚Äî strip-while-preserving, non-hook key preservation, all-orphan event removal, idempotency, single-target, not-found error, bare-project skip, mtime-preserved on no-op), `orphan-hooks API` (6 ‚Äî GET 200 + shape, GET literal-vs-:name regression, POST-all repair, POST-single, POST 400 on non-string project, POST 404 on missing project). `test/orphan-hooks-banner.test.js` (17 tests, source-level structural assertions following the silentPrime-modal test pattern): markup shape (banner element, role, button ids, text slot), CSS amber treatment + hidden toggling, landing.js wiring (state init, loadProjects integration, scan endpoint call, render show/hide + singular/plural copy, repair POST + reload, confirm-dialog scope warning, details breakdown, init-time wiring) plus the 4 Critic-driven tests: M1 partial-failure toast-warn, M1 no-response toast, M1 thrown-error console.error + toast, N3 polling gate on `state.orphanHooksRepairInFlight`. 1748 total passing (was 1701 after chunk 1).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged 0 BLOCKERs / 2 MAJORs / 5 MINORs / 5 NITs. Both MAJORs addressed in-chunk: (M1) `repairAllOrphanHooks` silently failed-closed on the UI side when `apiMutate` threw or the server returned only `errors[]` ‚Äî now surfaces a `toast-warn` for both the no-response and partial-failure paths, plus a fall-through error toast when the wire-handler `.catch` fires (replaces the prior swallow `.catch(() => {})`); (M2) the "TC-v3 incident shape" scan test used a misleading `orphanStopEntry().hooks[0] && { ... }` short-circuit that was dead-but-truthy ‚Äî replaced with a plain object literal. MINORs N1 (regex comment), N2 (formatting-canonicalization JSDoc note), N3 (in-flight gate on `state.orphanHooksRepairInFlight` so polling-driven scan can't briefly flash pre-repair state back during the POST) addressed in-chunk; N4 (info-log per malformed entry kept) deferred ‚Äî fail-open is documented in JSDoc and adding a per-entry log would risk dashboard spam on non-incidents. N5 (filter-Boolean comment) declined as overkill for a self-explanatory pattern. NITs T2 (CHANGELOG TBD placeholder), T3 (POSIX-rename caveat in JSDoc), T5 (unsupported-prefix caveat in JSDoc) addressed in-chunk. T1 (no `--auto` on commit) honored. T4 (test-tag punctuation consistency `(#145, chunk 2)` vs `(#145 chunk 2)`) addressed in-chunk.

- **`syncEngineHooks` injects methodology hooks without verifying their runtime targets exist ‚Äî orphan hook errors across multiple projects (#145, chunk 1)** ‚Äî `lib/engines.js:syncEngineHooks` was reading `methodologyTemplate.hooks.claude` and merging it into `.claude/settings.json` unconditionally. The bundled prawduct template declares hooks pointing at `$CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/tools/product-hook`, a script that the prawduct framework's own `prawduct-setup.py` is responsible for installing ‚Äî TC has no business shipping it. Result: every TC-launched session for a `methodology: prawduct` project that hadn't run prawduct's setup tool got an orphan hook block written into its `.claude/settings.json`, firing `Stop hook error: ... [Errno 2] No such file or directory` on every wrap. Verified live across 11 prawduct projects on 2026-05-10: 1 working (Notse), 2 active orphans (prawduct-test, RentalClaw-Project), 1 dormant orphan (Medusa, gemini engine ‚Äî Claude Code never reads the file), and 7 latent (one TC-launched session from manifesting). RentalClaw was the smoking gun ‚Äî confirmed clean in the morning, then a single TC-launched session injected the orphan block as an uncommitted change. Same conceptual class as #119 / #136 (bundled state drifts away from runtime state without TC reconciling), but on the hook-injection axis instead of the bundled-template-content axis.
  - **Fix in `lib/engines.js`**: new `_filterHookEntriesByRequires(hooks, projectPath)` function honors an optional `requires` field on hook entries (array of project-relative paths). `syncEngineHooks` now wraps `methodologyTemplate.hooks.claude` through the filter before merging with baseline hooks. Entries whose `requires` paths all exist (or have no `requires` field) are kept; entries with any missing path are skipped with an `info`-level log so dashboards can later surface "this methodology declares hooks whose runtime isn't installed." The TC-specific `requires` field is stripped from the output before writing ‚Äî Claude Code does not understand it and would surface as an unknown key in `settings.json`. AND-semantics: a hook needing multiple files needs them all (`requires: ["a", "b"]` means both a AND b must exist). Empty array (`requires: []`) means no preconditions ‚Äî the degenerate-but-explicit case.
  - **Bundled template change in `data/templates/prawduct/template.json`**: SessionStart and Stop entries now declare `requires: ["tools/product-hook"]`. Tripwire test reads the bundled file directly and asserts every hook entry whose command references `tools/product-hook` declares it in `requires` ‚Äî fires before a future PR drops the annotation and re-opens the gap.
  - **Why this design**: rejected three alternatives. (a) Heuristic path-extraction from command strings ‚Äî fragile, would miss commands using shell features. (b) TC scaffolding the prawduct framework's runtime ‚Äî couples TC release cadence to an external repo, supply-chain and version-skew burden. (c) Removing methodology hooks from bundled templates entirely ‚Äî loses the contract value, backwards-incompatible. The declarative-`requires` approach is non-breaking (entries without `requires` retain current behavior), explicit, forward-compatible for any future methodology with runtime dependencies, and most importantly: **self-heals on next session launch** ‚Äî no migration utility needed. Existing affected projects (the 9 with hook refs and 7 latent ones from the inventory above) get their orphan blocks stripped automatically as soon as TC re-runs `syncEngineHooks`.
  - **Engine semantics**: only methodology hooks pass through the filter ‚Äî engine baseline hooks (e.g. silent prime SessionStart from #103, gated by capability + projConfig already) are not subject to `requires` because TC ships those runtimes itself (`data/hooks/sessionstart-prime.sh`). Filtering them would be belt-and-braces with no upside and would couple unrelated subsystems. The non-claude branch (`projConfig.engine !== 'claude'`, `:1007-1024`) is also untouched ‚Äî it deletes the entire hooks block wholesale, doesn't iterate entries.
  - **What's intentionally NOT in chunk 1**: a one-shot bulk-repair admin endpoint (`POST /api/projects/repair-orphan-hooks`) to prune orphans without waiting for re-launch is deferred to chunk 2 ‚Äî optional, since chunk 1 self-heals. A methodology-flip cleanup audit (does PATCHing methodology from prawduct ‚Üí minimal correctly strip the prawduct-specific hook entries?) and a symmetric-capability-gates ADR are deferred to chunk 3. PATCH-time UI warning when methodology runtime isn't installed is filed as a separate enhancement.
  - **Tests**: 12 new in `test/engines.test.js` across three describe blocks. `_filterHookEntriesByRequires (#145)` (9 tests): keeps entries with satisfied requires, skips with single missing path, AND-semantics with multiple paths, backwards-compat for entries without `requires`, empty-array degenerate case, mixed kept-and-skipped within same event, plus the three Critic-driven additions ‚Äî string-requires coercion (S1), fail-closed for empty-string/non-string array entries (S3), path traversal and absolute paths rejected (S2). `syncEngineHooks + requires precondition (#145)` (2 tests): self-heal pruning of orphan block while preserving non-hook keys (the RentalClaw / prawduct-test repro), idempotency across re-syncs flipping skip ‚Üí inject when the requirement appears. `bundled prawduct template hook tripwire (#145)` (1 test): every bundled hook entry that references `tools/product-hook` declares it in `requires`. 1701 total passing (was 1689).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged S1 (string-instead-of-array silently injects ‚Üí coerce non-empty string to single-element array, the common single-precondition case is the most likely template-author typo and now Just Works), S2 (path traversal in `requires` accepted unchecked ‚Üí reject any entry containing `..` segments or starting with `/`, fail closed; matches the project-relative intent), S3 (no test for empty-string / non-string array entries ‚Üí added two assertions plus the negative tests for S1/S2), S4 (`syncEngineHooks` JSDoc didn't mention the new precondition behavior ‚Üí added one sentence pointing at the helper and noting baseline hooks bypass the filter). Critic findings n1-n4 deferred or accepted as-is per project style.
  - **Cross-cutting reference**: this is the next layer of the symmetric-capability-gates work that started with #119, #136, #137, #140. Pattern: when two locations encode the same conceptual state (here: the hook reference in `settings.json` and the runtime script on disk), all transition paths between configurations must consistently update both. Asymmetric transitions leak orphan state. ADR formalizing the pattern deferred to chunk 3.

- **`PATCH /api/projects/:name` engine change leaves orphan `SessionStart` hook in `.claude/settings.json` (#140)** ‚Äî Discovered during Independent Critic review of #137 (PR #141), filed and fixed as a follow-up. Flipping a project from `engine: 'claude'` (with `silentPrime: true`) to a non-claude engine wrote `projConfig.engine` and regenerated the engine config file but never re-synced hooks, so the now-stale `SessionStart` entry sat untouched in `.claude/settings.json`. Dormant in the moment (Claude Code isn't reading the file once the engine flips away), but a violation of the symmetric-capability-gates principle: the methodology and silentPrime PATCH branches both call `syncEngineHooks` after their hook-affecting mutations; the engine branch was the only outlier.
  - **Fix in `lib/engines.js:syncEngineHooks`**: the early-return for `projConfig.engine !== 'claude'` was a silent no-op ‚Äî it left whatever was already in `.claude/settings.json` in place. Replaced with an explicit cleanup pass: when the current engine isn't claude, read `.claude/settings.json` if it exists and `delete settings.hooks` (preserves all non-hook keys). This makes the function's contract honest ‚Äî "sync hooks for the current engine" now means "ensure no stale hooks remain" on the non-claude branch, not "leave whatever is there alone."
  - **Fix in `lib/projects.js` engine PATCH branch (`:858-893`)**: after writing the new engine config file, call `engines.syncEngineHooks(project.path, methodologyTemplate)` wrapped in try/catch. Mirrors the methodology branch (`:990`) and the post-#137 silentPrime branch (`:1068`).
  - **Why both halves**: just adding the call site without changing `syncEngineHooks` would not have cleared the orphan ‚Äî the function read the just-saved `projConfig.engine === 'gemini'` and early-returned. The two-part fix is required for the test to pass.
  - **What's intentionally NOT done**: `projConfig.silentPrime` is left at its prior value across the engine flip (the issue body noted it stays `true`). The right behavior on cross-engine flips is debatable ‚Äî clearing it on the way out would surprise users who flip back to claude expecting their setting preserved. Out of scope; the orphan-hook concern is the safety issue. If a future engine reads `.claude/settings.json`, it now sees a clean file.
  - **Symmetric capability gates**: methodology PATCH (`:990`), silentPrime PATCH (`:1068`), and engine PATCH (`:889`) now all call `syncEngineHooks` after their hook-affecting mutations. Project-attach (`:761`) and project-create (`:237`) likewise. The `feedback_symmetric_capability_gates.md` rule the Critic surfaced on #103 PR #125 holds across the full set.
  - **Tests**: 2 new in `test/projects.test.js` `silentPrime (#103)` describe block. `updateProject clears orphan SessionStart hook when engine flips claude ‚Üí non-claude (#140)` seeds `silentPrime=true` on a claude project (so the SessionStart hook is genuinely materialized on disk), injects a non-hook `permissions` key to verify the cleanup pass preserves it, then PATCHes engine to `gemini` and asserts `settings.hooks.SessionStart` is gone while `permissions` survives. `updateProject materializes SessionStart hook when engine flips non-claude ‚Üí claude with silentPrime=true (#140)` covers the reverse path the CHANGELOG claims ‚Äî that flipping onto claude immediately materializes the hook without waiting for the next `launchSession`. 1689 total passing (was 1687).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: Independent Critic flagged that the original test asserted only the orphan-hook deletion, not non-hook-key preservation (m1) and didn't cover the reverse-flip materialization path the CHANGELOG promised (m2); both are now covered. Critic also flagged that `syncEngineHooks`'s non-claude branch is now write-active rather than a no-op (m3) ‚Äî JSDoc updated to document the contract change. Code-comment line references replaced with branch names rather than absolute line numbers (n1) so future edits don't drift the comments.

- **`PATCH /api/projects/:name` with `silentPrime` doesn't sync `.claude/settings.json` until next session launch (#137)** ‚Äî `updateProject` persisted `silentPrime` to `.tangleclaw/project.json` but never called `engines.syncEngineHooks(...)`, so the actual delivery pipeline only materialized on the next `launchSession`. DB + projConfig agreed but `.claude/settings.json.hooks.SessionStart` was missing ‚Äî the toggle looked enabled, wasn't enabled.
  - **The asymmetry**: the methodology branch (`lib/projects.js:990`) and engine branch (`:760`) already called `syncEngineHooks` after their hook-affecting mutations. The silentPrime branch at `:1057-1061` was the only hook-affecting field that skipped the sync.
  - **Fix in `lib/projects.js`**: after `store.projectConfig.save`, call `engines.syncEngineHooks(project.path, store.templates.get(project.methodology))` wrapped in try/catch (matching `createProject`'s pattern at `:236-240`). On the silent‚Üítyped transition (`silentPrime: false`), also call `sessions._removePrimeFile(project.path)` to clear any stale `.tangleclaw/session-prime.md` left by a previous silent-on session ‚Äî mirrors `launchSession`'s OFF-branch self-heal at `lib/sessions.js:171`. The helper is non-throwing on missing files, so unconditional on the false branch is safe.
  - **What's intentionally NOT done**: the prime file is not written on `silentPrime: true` PATCH. Prime text is launch-context-dependent ‚Äî `generatePrimePrompt` reads `learnings.getActive()`, `sessions.getLatest().wrapSummary`, and eval-audit mode at session-launch time. Writing at PATCH time would persist a snapshot from the wrong moment. The launch-time-only contract is the right boundary; documented in the inline comment.
  - **Cycle check**: the new `const sessions = require('./sessions')` at the top of `lib/projects.js` is safe ‚Äî `lib/sessions.js`'s require list (`store`, `tmux`, `tunnel`, `git`, `engines`, `methodologies`, `skills`, `project-version`, `logger`) does not transitively pull in `lib/projects.js`. Cross-module call is preferred over duplicating the unlink helper.
  - **Symmetric capability gates** (per the symmetric-gates feedback rule): the four silentPrime gates remain aligned. `_buildBaselineHooks` (`engines.js:937-940`), `updateProject` validation (`projects.js:810-820`), `launchSession` derivation (`sessions.js:152-154`), and the new PATCH-sync path (which delegates to `syncEngineHooks` ‚Üí `_buildBaselineHooks`, inheriting the gate) all check `silentPrime===true && engineProfile.capabilities.supportsSilentPrime===true`. No drift introduced.
  - **Tests**: 5 new ‚Äî 4 in `test/projects.test.js` `silentPrime (#103)` describe block (`syncs SessionStart hook on silentPrime=true`, `removes SessionStart hook on silentPrime=false`, `removes stale session-prime.md on silentPrime=false`, `silentPrime=false is a no-op for prime cleanup when file is absent`), 1 in `test/api-projects.test.js` (`PATCH silentPrime=true writes SessionStart hook to .claude/settings.json on disk` ‚Äî locks in the wire-level contract that #137's repro hit). 1687 total tests passing (was 1682).
  - **Critic-driven adjustments**: build-plan note updated to record the cycle-absent verification (was originally hedged toward inlining the helper); test 2's assertion loosened from `after.hooks === undefined` to `after.hooks?.SessionStart === undefined` so future baseline-hook siblings of #103 don't break the test; engine-flip orphan hook noted as a separate follow-up (out of scope for this issue's repro).

## [3.14.0] - 2026-05-01

### Added

- **Silent prime delivery via Claude Code SessionStart hook ‚Äî polish + final Critic (#103, chunk 3)** ‚Äî Closes #103 by addressing all chunk-1/chunk-2 carry-forwards plus the chunk-2 Critic Mn5 UX polish. Behavior is unchanged for opted-in projects; this chunk is hardening + housekeeping.
  - **Hook script hardening (`data/hooks/sessionstart-prime.sh`)** ‚Äî Replaced the no-op `set +e` (errexit is off by default in bash, so the line did nothing) with `set -u` for variable strictness, and switched both `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}` references to the `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR:-}` default form so an unset env var no longer crashes the script. Added a defensive `cat "$PRIME_FILE" || true` so the unlikely race where the file vanishes between the readability check and `cat` cannot exit non-zero (also future-proofs against a later addition of `set -e`). The unset-env-var, missing-file, and exit-0 contracts the chunk-1 hook tests already lock in continue to hold; 4 new tests assert the structural hardening (`set -u` present, `set +e` gone, no bare `${CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR}` dereferences, `cat || true` guard, plus a behavioral test for explicitly-empty `CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR=''`).
  - **Prime-file cleanup on silent‚Üítyped transition (`lib/sessions.js:_removePrimeFile`)** ‚Äî When a project flips `silentPrime: true ‚Üí false`, the SessionStart hook is still installed (via `syncEngineHooks` baseline merge) but no longer expected to read anything. Without cleanup, the hook would replay yesterday's stale prime context to the AI on every subsequent launch. New `_removePrimeFile(projectPath)` helper unlinks `.tangleclaw/session-prime.md` if present (non-throwing, returns true on removal / false on missing or error). `launchSession` calls it on the OFF branch of the silentPrime gate so the cleanup self-heals on the next session launch ‚Äî no PATCH-time hook needed in `updateProject`. 4 new tests: helper round-trip with file present, no-op when absent, non-throwing on unwritable target, and a `launchSession` integration test that pre-seeds a stale prime, sets `silentPrime: false`, launches, and asserts the file is gone.
  - **Settings modal toggle re-renders on engine dropdown change (Critic Mn5 from chunk 2)** ‚Äî The chunk-2 implementation gated the silentPrime toggle's render on `project.engine.capabilities.supportsSilentPrime` at modal-open time only, so switching the engine dropdown to a non-supportive engine left a stale checkbox visible (the backend already rejected the resulting PATCH gracefully, but the user shouldn't be able to send a doomed request in the first place). Refactored to a stable container (`#settingsSilentPrimeContainer`) plus a `renderSilentPrimeToggle(engineId, preserveChecked)` helper that looks up the engine in `state.engines` and renders or wipes the toggle accordingly. A `change` listener on `#settingsEngine` re-invokes the helper with the new engine id and the checkbox's current `checked` state, so the user's intent (e.g., "turn silent prime on") is preserved across engine swaps and hidden when the new engine can't honor it. The chunk-2 settings-modal-silentprime test file was reshaped to match: 3 of the original 7 tests rewritten to follow the helper-based structure (capability gate now via `state.engines` lookup; checkbox tied to `preserveChecked`; non-supportive engines wipe the container) plus 2 brand-new tests (`initial render is wired into openSettings via renderSilentPrimeToggle`, `engine dropdown change re-renders the toggle`); 3 chunk-2 tests carry through unchanged.
  - **CHANGELOG bullet split** ‚Äî Chunks 1 and 2 originally landed as single-paragraph bullets (per the Critic carry-forward note). Restructured into 3-4 sub-bullets each (this entry's format) so a future reader skimming the [Unreleased] section gets a clean overview without parsing dense prose.
  - **Final Critic** ‚Äî Independent Critic ran across the full chunks 1+2+3 surface. Findings + resolutions captured below.
  - **Tests**: 9 new tests in chunk 3 (4 hook-script hardening, 4 prime-file cleanup including the `launchSession` transition test, +1 net on settings-modal-silentprime ‚Äî 8 total now vs the 7 from chunk 2: 3 rewrites + 2 new + 3 unchanged). Total passing: 1682 (was 1673).

- **Silent prime delivery via Claude Code SessionStart hook ‚Äî UI surface (#103, chunk 2)** ‚Äî Per-project toggle that exposes the chunk-1 backend opt-in to users.
  - **Project Settings modal**: `public/ui.js:openSettings` renders a "Silent prime (hidden context)" checkbox when the resolved engine profile advertises `capabilities.supportsSilentPrime === true` (Claude Code today). Gating on the capability flag rather than `engine.id === 'claude'` keeps the UI honest if future engines gain the same capability without needing a UI change. The checkbox state mirrors `project.silentPrime`; `doSaveSettings` only attaches `silentPrime` to the PATCH body when the element was rendered, so a non-supportive engine never receives a stale `silentPrime: undefined`.
